201503	2	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	And in a couple of hours, we will also have a chance to say farewell to President Fisher at a luncheon.	5	5

201503	5	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	I would also like to welcome Blake Prichard to the table, representing the Federal Reserve Bank of Philadelphia.	5	5
201503	6	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	He is serving as acting president of the Philadelphia Bank until Patrick Harker takes office on July 1.	5	5
201503	7	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Before we begin today’s agenda, I want to briefly update you about developments that relate to press briefings.	5	5
201503	8	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	At recent meetings, we have discussed the fact that it is important for the Committee not to feel constrained from taking action whenever we deem appropriate, at any meeting, regardless of whether there is a postmeeting press conference scheduled.	97	9
201503	9	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	And a number of you have suggested to me that I schedule press conferences after every meeting.	97	9
201503	10	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Now, a decision to have press conferences at every meeting is likely to be irreversible.	97	9
201503	11	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	It is something I have, therefore, carefully considered.	97	9
201503	12	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	For now, at least, I think my decision is that it would be best not to schedule press conferences after every meeting.	97	9
201503	13	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Let me just say that, by way of explanation, the time that is required for me and all of our senior staff to prepare for these press conferences is truly nontrivial.	97	9
201503	14	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	In part, that is because preparations involve being up-to-date not only on matters pertaining to monetary policy and the economy, but also on all matters pertaining to Federal Reserve-related issues.	97	9
201503	15	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	And all of that preparation occurs at exactly the same time when all of us are preparing for these meetings.	97	9
201503	16	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	As I reflect on it—and, again, this is just a decision for now, so I am not saying this can’t be revisited—it seems to me that when we are in a more normal mode for conducting monetary policy, and I hope that time is not too far off, and the economic environment is more normal, every-meeting press conferences, especially after meetings for which there are no forecast updates, are really not likely to have much focus on monetary policy decisions and the economy.	97	9
201503	17	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	What I believe will happen is they will become opportunities for the media to explore a host of nonmonetary policy issues, which ultimately could be a distraction rather than a help to us.	97	9
201503	18	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	That would all occur on meeting days.	97	9
201503	19	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	But, at the same time, though I am not inclined now to go to press conferences every meeting, I do think it is important for us to feel—and also to convince the public and market participants—that we are not constrained from taking decisions at meetings for which there is not a subsequent press conference, so that market expectations of our future actions can be appropriately responsive to incoming data.	97	9
201503	20	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	As I have mentioned in the past, we have long had the capability to conduct press briefings by telephone on very short notice.	97	9
201503	21	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Chairman Bernanke did so a number of times during the financial crisis.	97	9
201503	22	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	So the plan I would like to propose is that we remind the public, the markets, and the press that we have that capability and would indeed use it when necessary.	97	9
201503	23	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	And, to firm up that expectation, late on the second day of our meeting in April, the Board’s Public Affairs office plans to conduct a test of our system for media conference calls.	97	9
201503	24	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	We will permit news organizations to report afterward that we conducted this test, and we will state that the reason for the test is to refresh news organizations’ familiarity with how the system works, so that we can use it, if necessary, on meeting days when no press conference is scheduled.	97	9
201503	25	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	That is currently the plan, and I welcome any input that any of you would like to offer on it.	97	9
201503	26	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	But that is what we thought, for the moment.	97	9

201503	33	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	I am going to call on Simon Potter to begin the Desk report.	61	6
201503	34	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	61	6
201503	35	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	We will be splitting the Desk briefing in two parts.	61	6
201503	36	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	I will talk about financial market developments, then Lorie will talk about Desk operations.	61	6
201503	37	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	Over the intermeeting period, the backdrop of monetary policy easing overseas, relative stability in oil prices, and some positive global economic data reportedly contributed to a reduction in perceived downside global growth risks.	61	6
201503	38	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	Longer-dated forward interest rates among major developed economies diverged over the period, as shown in the top-left panel of your first exhibit.	61	6
201503	39	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	The trend of declining longer-run nominal interest rates since the start of 2014 partially retraced itself in the United States and United Kingdom, as some incoming economic data, most notably employment reports, reinforced expectations that the Federal Reserve and Bank of England will begin normalizing policy within the next year.	61	6
201503	40	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	The top-right panel shows a summation of daily changes in US yields over the period, bucketed into a few categories based on market commentary.	61	6
201503	41	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	Increases in both short- and longer-dated yields occurred on days with stronger-than-expected US employment reports and higher-than-expected inflation data, among other factors.	61	6
201503	42	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	These influences in combination more than offset the declines in rates that followed the start of ECB purchases and Federal Reserve communications including the January statement, minutes, and the Chair’s testimony before the Congress.	61	6
201503	43	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	These Federal Reserve communications were generally interpreted as slightly more accommodative than expected due to discussion of the balance of risks around the start of normalization and the outlook for persistently low inflation.	61	6
201503	44	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	However, not all market participants interpreted Federal Reserve commentary as more accommodative than expected.	61	6
201503	45	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	Many market participants expect policy normalization to begin in the second or third quarter of 2015.	61	6
201503	46	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	This is shown in the middle-left panel, which indicates that the average probability assigned to liftoff occurring in June or September increased modestly from the January surveys.	61	6
201503	47	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	This panel also shows that the distribution of individual beliefs about liftoff timing is dispersed, consistent with some of the differing interpretations of Federal Reserve communications over the intermeeting period to which I just alluded.	61	6
201503	48	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	Desk and private surveys also indicate that the vast majority of respondents anticipate the Committee will drop the “patient” language from the statement at this meeting, and the Desk surveys suggest this would result in only a small increase in the average probability assigned to a June liftoff.	61	6
201503	49	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	Desk survey respondents expect liftoff to occur against a backdrop of very subdued realized inflation.	61	6
201503	50	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	The median response for the mostly likely level of 12-month headline PCE inflation at liftoff declined to 0.4 percent in the March survey, as shown in the first column of the middle-right panel.	61	6
201503	51	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	For 12-month core PCE inflation at liftoff, the median response was 1.4 percent, with an interquartile range of 1.3 to 1.5 percent.	61	6
201503	52	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	Although the median point forecast for PCE inflation 1 to 2 years after liftoff remains 2 percent, shown in the second column, the odds that both dealers and buy-side respondents assign to inflation over that horizon remaining below 1.75 percent has increased substantially over recent months.	61	6
201503	53	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	This is shown in the final two columns.	61	6
201503	54	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	The Board’s measure of five-year, five-year-forward inflation compensation moved up slightly, on net, as shown in the bottom-left panel.	61	6
201503	55	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	However, this measure remains far below its average level since 2003.	61	6
201503	56	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	Currently, US forward inflation compensation appears to be surprisingly linked to changes in the price of oil, as can be seen by comparing the trajectories in the bottom-left panel.	61	6
201503	57	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	The US dollar continued to broadly appreciate against both major and emerging market currencies over the intermeeting period, with the DXY dollar index higher by 6.5 percent and at its strongest level since 2002.	61	6
201503	58	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	Contributing to this move was a 7.5 percent weakening of the euro versus the US dollar, shown in the bottom-right panel, which came alongside a 27 basis point widening of the US–German 2-year yield spread over the period.	61	6
201503	59	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	Since the announcement of the public sector asset purchase program at the January ECB meeting, European equities have increased by about 12 percent, as shown in the top-left panel of your next exhibit.	61	6
201503	60	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	In contrast, the S&P 500 is little changed, on net, over the same period.	61	6
201503	61	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	Euro-area corporate credit spreads have also tightened since January, and there has been a substantial narrowing of peripheral sovereign spreads to Germany.	61	6
201503	62	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	The announcement of ECB sovereign debt purchases reportedly contributed to stable peripheral sovereign spreads amid Greek financial assistance negotiations.	61	6
201503	63	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	Steve Kamin will discuss the Greek situation in his briefing.	61	6
201503	64	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	The ECB announced at its recent meeting that purchases would be restricted to bonds with yields above the deposit facility rate, which currently stands at negative 20 basis points.	61	6
201503	65	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	This constraint currently renders 2- and 3-year bunds ineligible and will force the Bundesbank to extend the duration of its purchases unless rates on these securities increase above the deposit facility rate.	61	6
201503	66	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	Following the commencement of purchases last Monday, the German yield curve flattened substantially, as shown in the top-right panel.	61	6
201503	67	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	German yields are now negative out to 7 years, the 10-year German-US interest rate differential is at its widest level in at least 25 years, and the German 30-year yield trades at similar levels to that of a US 2-year note.	61	6
201503	68	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	The negative interest rate environment in Europe has become more pervasive and pronounced, as shown in the middle-left panel.	61	6
201503	69	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	Over the intermeeting period, the Danish National Bank cut its deposit rate to negative 75 basis points to defend its euro currency peg, while the Riksbank moved its main policy rate to negative 10 basis points and initiated a small asset purchase program.	61	6
201503	70	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	There has been some pass-through by banks of negative rates to large corporate depositors but less pass- through to retail-level customers.	61	6
201503	71	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	Contacts have not reported major shifts in market structure, investor behavior, or market functioning due to negative rates.	61	6
201503	72	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	It is possible that more sovereign assets in the euro area will trade at negative yields as the ECB asset purchase program continues.	61	6
201503	73	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	The ECB’s constraint that purchases must be of assets with yields above negative 20 basis points might interact with additional constraints related to the capital key, issue, and issuer share to skew purchases further out on the yield curve, placing additional substantial downward pressure on yields.	61	6
201503	74	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	This feedback loop might be amplified if, as many market participants believe, holders of longer-dated debt are somewhat price-insensitive because of investment mandates or regulations.	61	6
201503	75	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	Thus, some have noted concerns about the potential for a notable deterioration in euro-area sovereign market functioning.	61	6
201503	76	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	Large-scale asset purchases are having a pronounced effect on the JGB market.	61	6
201503	77	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	As shown in the middle-right panel, yields and measures of implied volatility rose sharply in mid-January.	61	6
201503	78	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	The catalyst for this is unclear, although the moves disturbed fragile Japanese rates market dynamics that are dominated by BOJ purchase operations, leading to some paring back of dealer marketmaking activity and several poorly received JGB auctions.	61	6
201503	79	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	Despite their adverse effect on JGB market functioning, large-scale asset purchases in Japan still appear to be having substantial effects on risk assets and the exchange rate as portfolio rebalancing continues.	61	6
201503	80	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	Volatility and market functioning have also been in focus in FX markets, particularly amid rapid dollar appreciation.	61	6
201503	81	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	Some are concerned that the next sharp currency move may be in China.	61	6
201503	82	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	The official dollar-RMB central parity rate has slowly moved higher over recent months, and the onshore dollar-RMB rate has traded toward the top of its trading band, shown in the bottom-left panel.	61	6
201503	83	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	As shown in the bottom-right panel, implied volatility in a number of markets has increased, and there have been some pronounced spikes in volatility.	61	6
201503	84	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	As was detailed in the October 15 memo recently sent to the Committee, the nature of Treasury market liquidity has changed over recent years, reflecting an increased role of algorithmic and high-frequency trading activity and decreased shock-absorbing capacity of dealers.	61	6
201503	85	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	Some market participants have noted that recent spikes in volatility, particularly the intensity of intraday moves, will produce changes in risk management that could further limit capital deployed to marketmaking in volatile markets.	61	6
201503	86	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	These changes in structure are common across a range of markets and might lead to more frequent sharp price moves.	61	6
201503	87	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	While market participants often point out these risks, they also acknowledge that US financial firms are stronger and the financial system is better positioned to handle such bursts of volatility than prior to the financial crisis, consistent with the conclusions from recent QS reports.	61	6
201503	88	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	That completes my report.	61	6

201503	127	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	I’ll discuss testing of tools for normalizing policy and some longer-term changes in money markets and conclude with options for a resolution for quarter-end term RRP testing.	61	6

201503	129	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	We estimate that MBS reinvestments in 2015 will total about $330 billion, roughly $70 billion lower than our estimate at the January meeting due to the increase in Treasury yields but still notably higher than anticipated in December.	61	6
201503	130	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	Reinvestment purchase operations continue to go smoothly, and MBS liquidity remains stable.	61	6
201503	131	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	Over the period, the Federal Reserve executed three overlapping 21-day TDF operations at 28 basis points with same-day settlement and a $20 billion counterparty cap at each operation.	61	6
201503	132	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the top-right panel, the total amount of term deposits reached $404 billion, roughly the same size as the largest operation in the prior testing series, conducted at a slightly higher rate of 30 basis points.	61	6
201503	133	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	The two largest participants accounted for $170 billion.	61	6
201503	134	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	One of these firms, which participated under two separate legal entities and placed a total of $110 billion, indicated that it would have committed roughly $40 billion more if participation was not capped.	61	6
201503	135	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	The other firm suggested it did not have additional demand for TDFs.	61	6
201503	136	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	As expected, the operations did not appear to put upward pressure on short-term rates, and counterparties suggested that, in the current environment, reserve draining from term tools would need to be much larger to directly affect market rates.	61	6
201503	137	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	As outlined in communications in advance of the meeting, the staff has been making progress on a revision to the methodology for the payment of interest on reserves that should help tighten the linkage between the level of the IOER rate on any given day and the level of the effective federal funds rate on that day.	61	6
201503	138	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	Programming efforts are proceeding, and the staff expects to publish a Federal Register notice describing the proposed changes soon after this meeting.	61	6
201503	139	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	The staff also continues to conduct RRP test operations.	61	6
201503	140	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	Average total daily take- up in Federal Reserve RRP operations over the intermeeting period, shown in the middle-left panel, was about $125 billion, similar to recent months.	61	6
201503	141	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	With the exception of some small-value test trades, the ON RRP operations during the period did not include the most recent wave of expanded RRP counterparties, which began trading yesterday.	61	6
201503	142	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	In that operation, the new counterparties represented less than $4 billion of the $112 billion allotted.	61	6
201503	143	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the middle-right panel, the Desk conducted four one-week term operations from mid-February through early March.	61	6
201503	144	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	The amount of bids submitted in each operation was relatively stable, ranging between about $70 billion and $90 billion, and each operation stopped out at 6 basis points.	61	6
201503	145	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	The staff estimates that the majority of demand for term RRPs represented either substitution from the ON RRP—the light blue bars in the bottom-left panel—or rollover of funds allocated to previous term RRP operations, the dark blue bars.	61	6
201503	146	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	Only about 15 percent of take-up appears to be new funds.	61	6
201503	147	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	Given that the stop-out rate for the term operations was just 1 basis point higher than the ON RRP rate, it appears that the additional return required to move $50 billion from overnight into term RRPs for one week was relatively small.	61	6
201503	148	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	Consistent with the idea that take-up at term operations primarily represented substitution from ON RRP operations, market participants did not attribute movements in market rates to these term test operations.	61	6
201503	149	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	Overall, however, the ON RRP continued to provide a soft floor on money market rates.	61	6
201503	150	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the light blue line in the bottom-right panel, with the exception of some increased volatility around month-end dates, the effective federal funds rate remained near the levels observed since mid-December, when the Desk concluded the testing series that involved changes in the ON RRP rate.	61	6
201503	151	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	However, secured rates were somewhat soft over parts of the intermeeting period, with some segments of the repo market at times trading below the ON RRP rate.	61	6
201503	152	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	For example, as shown in the dark blue line in the bottom-right panel, after removing GCF repo transactions—which are a subset of triparty repo that primarily serve as an interdealer market—the volume-weighted average rate of remaining triparty trades briefly dipped below the ON RRP rate.	61	6
201503	153	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	Market participants attributed the broader dynamics in secured rates, in part, to shifts in GSE cash management needs and decreases in Treasury bill supply associated with the Treasury’s shift in short-term financing needs around the April tax date, as well as month-end pressures.	61	6
201503	154	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	Turning to your final exhibit, I wanted to highlight some longer-term developments in money markets.	61	6
201503	155	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	These developments, which market participants indicate partly reflect dealers’ more conservative risk management practices since the crisis as well as ongoing regulatory changes, may affect the constellation of money market rates and the tools for monetary policy implementation.	61	6
201503	156	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	For example, some dealers with large, stable repo funding bases have demanded increased compensation to intermediate between money funds or other lenders in the triparty repo market and the smaller or less creditworthy dealers that seek to borrow funds in the GCF market.	61	6
201503	157	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	This can be seen in the widening spread between the volume-weighted average rates in the GCF market and the broader triparty market, excluding GCF, shown in the top-left panel.	61	6
201503	158	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	There is also some indication that dealers are somewhat less willing to employ their balance sheets for other types of relatively low-margin intermediation activities.	61	6
201503	159	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the top-right panel, dealers have decreased the total size of their overnight repo books.	61	6
201503	160	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	Meanwhile, the stock of Treasury bills, a close substitute to repos, shown in the light blue line, has also declined because of a combination of an improved fiscal outlook and an effort to increase the weighted-average maturity of Treasury debt outstanding.	61	6
201503	161	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	Combined, these shifts have decreased opportunities for money market funds to invest cash in high-quality instruments.	61	6
201503	162	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	At the same time, regulatory changes are increasing the demand for high-quality money market instruments.	61	6
201503	163	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	Over the intermeeting period, Fidelity announced that it would convert three of its prime money market funds, including one of the largest prime retail funds in assets under management, into government funds in response to the 2014 SEC reforms.	61	6
201503	164	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	Combined, these three funds have about $130 billion in assets under management.	61	6
201503	165	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	Additionally, J.P.	61	6
201503	166	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	Morgan announced its intention to reduce certain non-operating wholesale deposits by up to $100 billion, either by introducing fees on certain institutional clients’ deposits or by asking clients to move deposits into other products, such as money funds.	61	6
201503	167	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	Market participants anticipate that other firms are likely to take similar actions as J.P.	61	6
201503	168	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	Morgan and Fidelity, further increasing demand for high-quality money market instruments.	61	6
201503	169	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	These changes reflect, at least in part, actions that firms are taking to align their business models with upcoming regulatory changes intended to increase the safety of money market funds and decrease banks’ and broker-dealers’ reliance on short-term funding.	61	6
201503	170	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	These are, of course, important steps to improve the resiliency of the financial system.	61	6
201503	171	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	They may, however, increase segmentation in money markets and, given the high level of reserves in the system, put some downward pressure on some money market rates.	61	6
201503	172	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	This could in turn increase demand for Fed RRPs or similar instruments during policy normalization.	61	6
201503	173	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	For example, many of the non-operating deposits that J.P.	61	6
201503	174	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	Morgan announced it will try to reduce are likely held by foreign official accounts.	61	6
201503	175	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	As the Federal Reserve’s balance sheet increased, we have seen and allowed foreign central banks to place additional funds in the foreign RP pool, as shown in the middle-left panel.	61	6
201503	176	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	As you may recall, this is a service offered to foreign central banks and international organizations in which funds in their accounts at the end of the day are used for a repo transaction, with SOMA securities as collateral.	61	6
201503	177	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	Recently we have experienced increased demand for storing liquidity by investing cash in the foreign RP pool.	61	6
201503	178	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	One large customer indicated a desire to increase their dollar reserves liquidity to prepare for possible instability as the FOMC raises rates.	61	6
201503	179	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	Despite the announcements emphasizing a shifting landscape in money markets and the discussion of the possibility of an elevated ON RRP cap at liftoff in the January minutes, market participants have not materially increased their expectations for the size of the ON RRP facility during or after liftoff.	61	6
201503	180	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the middle- right panel, the median respondent to the most recent Desk surveys expects that usage of ON RRP at liftoff will be $300 billion and will decline to $250 billion three years after liftoff, broadly similar to expectations in recent surveys.	61	6
201503	181	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	The range between the 10th percentile and 90th percentile of respondents’ views, shown in the red bars in the bottom-left panel, is also largely unchanged from the January survey.	61	6
201503	182	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	The distribution of views remains skewed toward higher usage.	61	6
201503	183	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	Turning to expectations for total RRP usage over the March quarter-end, market participants broadly expect that the combined capacity of $500 billion—inclusive of both term and overnight operations—will be sufficient to support a soft floor on money market rates above the ON RRP rate leading into and on March 31.	61	6
201503	184	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	The first of two planned term RRP operations covering the March quarter-end will be held Thursday.	61	6
201503	185	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	Lastly, the Committee may wish to consider authorizing term tests over future quarter-ends.	61	6
201503	186	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	If the Committee envisions using term RRPs as part of a strategy to limit the size of the ON RRP facility at liftoff or potentially at some other point during normalization, continued testing may be useful, particularly for operational readiness.	61	6
201503	187	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	Even if the Committee plans to provide elevated capacity in the ON RRP facility—one that allows sufficient headroom, even at quarter-end—putting the term RRP test operations in place may also be helpful, particularly if liftoff occurs around a quarter-end date.	61	6
201503	188	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	This is because, in the absence of public information about the Committee’s intentions and implementation, there is potential for money market rates to trade soft to the federal funds target range leading up to the quarter-end.	61	6
201503	189	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	For these reasons, the staff has outlined two options for authorizing such testing if the Committee chooses to do so.	61	6
201503	190	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	As discussed in a memo distributed prior to the meeting and outlined in the bottom-right panel, the first option is for the FOMC to approve a resolution that authorizes term RRP test operations for the June, September, and December 2015 quarter-ends.	61	6
201503	191	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	This option is substantially similar to the resolution adopted for the 2014 year-end term RRP tests and authorizes, but does not obligate, the Federal Reserve to conduct those operations.	61	6
201503	192	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	A resolution of this kind would more closely align the authorization for term RRP testing with that governing testing of ON RRP operations and might reduce the probability that market participants mistakenly interpret future decisions about testing term RRPs over quarter-end as containing information about the likelihood of liftoff.	61	6
201503	193	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	Alternatively, the Committee could continue its current practice of authorizing term RRP test operations each quarter, each time using a resolution approved at an FOMC meeting well ahead of quarter-end.	61	6
201503	194	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	Draft resolutions regarding both approaches are provided in a separate handout in the event that the Committee decides to proceed with authorizing further quarter-end term tests.	61	6
201503	195	2015-03-18	meeting	LOGAN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	61	6

201503	276	2015-03-18	meeting	IHRIG	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201503	277	2015-03-18	meeting	IHRIG	Let me start by noting that at your previous meeting, most participants agreed that it would be useful at coming meetings to discuss and communicate additional information about some operational details of your policy implementation plans.	96	9
201503	278	2015-03-18	meeting	IHRIG	With this in mind, the staff memo titled “More Steps toward Finalizing the FOMC’s Operational Preparations for Liftoff” provided some possible language in bullet point form to include in the March minutes; these bullets were revised in light of your earlier comments.	96	9
201503	279	2015-03-18	meeting	IHRIG	At the end of the go-round that will follow our briefing, the Chair will ask whether you agree to augment the Committee’s Policy Normalization Principles and Plans by providing these additional operational details in the minutes for this meeting; for reference, the bullet points are attached at the end of this handout.	96	9
201503	280	2015-03-18	meeting	IHRIG	Two other issues that were covered in the memos related to the capacity of the ON RRP facility.	96	9
201503	281	2015-03-18	meeting	IHRIG	I will spend some time discussing options for setting the initial aggregate capacity of the ON RRP facility, and then Antoine will review options for reducing capacity during the normalization process.	96	9
201503	282	2015-03-18	meeting	IHRIG	Let me say up front that the appropriate amount of capacity needed at liftoff is uncertain for a couple of reasons.	96	9
201503	283	2015-03-18	meeting	IHRIG	First, your calculation of initial capacity needs to account for expected take-up around liftoff and also allow for additional headroom, both of which are hard to gauge.	96	9
201503	284	2015-03-18	meeting	IHRIG	In addition, although we have some sense of these amounts from the test operations that we have been conducting for some time, there is no guarantee that our testing experience provides an accurate reading on potential ON RRP usage once you move the policy rate above the zero lower bound.	96	9
201503	285	2015-03-18	meeting	IHRIG	Having said this, the top-left panel of your exhibit presents the two options from the staff memo for setting the initial aggregate capacity of the ON RRP facility for your consideration.	96	9
201503	286	2015-03-18	meeting	IHRIG	The first option is to set a temporarily elevated initial cap.	96	9
201503	287	2015-03-18	meeting	IHRIG	Your preferred setting of this cap might depend on your willingness to use term RRPs at quarter-ends.	96	9
201503	288	2015-03-18	meeting	IHRIG	The staff suggested, for illustrative purposes, an ON RRP cap of $800 billion.	96	9
201503	289	2015-03-18	meeting	IHRIG	This would be equivalent to double the take-up of both term and ON RRPs that we saw at year-end 2014.	96	9
201503	290	2015-03-18	meeting	IHRIG	It would also be more than 3½ times the largest non-quarter-end take-up that we’ve had to date.	96	9
201503	291	2015-03-18	meeting	IHRIG	By picking this much larger cap than we’ve had in testing and making clear that this initial setting is intended to be temporary, you would send a message that you are committed to a successful liftoff, and, at the same time, by limiting the facility’s size, you would say you’re also sensitive to the financial stability and footprint concerns that you have noted in previous discussions.	96	9
201503	292	2015-03-18	meeting	IHRIG	Of course, there is always a chance that $800 billion, or another nominal amount chosen, could turn out to be insufficient for interest rate control.	96	9
201503	293	2015-03-18	meeting	IHRIG	Indeed, although as Lorie mentioned, the majority of respondents to the Desk’s surveys expect moderate ON RRP take-up immediately after liftoff, a few market participants surveyed did anticipate that demand will be greater than $800 billion.	96	9
201503	294	2015-03-18	meeting	IHRIG	If that were the case and federal funds traded at rates persistently below the target range, or other money market rates did not firm as much as the Committee desired at liftoff because the cap was regularly being hit or market participants perceived insufficient headroom at the facility, you could subsequently increase the cap size.	96	9
201503	295	2015-03-18	meeting	IHRIG	For policymakers that are concerned about liftoff proceeding smoothly, however, right from the start, this scenario might be unsettling, and they might prefer option 2.	96	9
201503	296	2015-03-18	meeting	IHRIG	Under this option, the FOMC would suspend the aggregate cap for a short period but announce that it would establish a cap at the end of that initial brief period; the cap would be one that reflected the observed effects and take-up of ON RRPs after liftoff.	96	9
201503	297	2015-03-18	meeting	IHRIG	Assuming you would retain a per-counterparty bid limit, a temporary suspension of the aggregate cap would not amount to offering ON RRPs at full allotment, but would nonetheless provide substantial ON RRP capacity to start.	96	9
201503	298	2015-03-18	meeting	IHRIG	As noted to the right, you have many choices for how to move forward with communicating about your initial setting of capacity.	96	9
201503	299	2015-03-18	meeting	IHRIG	The bullets for inclusion in the minutes of this meeting start this process by reporting that ON RRP capacity at liftoff will be “temporarily elevated.”	96	9
201503	300	2015-03-18	meeting	IHRIG	Over time, you could decide on and announce the actual amount of initial capacity you intend to provide, either ahead of liftoff or at liftoff.	96	9
201503	301	2015-03-18	meeting	IHRIG	Early communication could provide market participants with further clarity about your liftoff strategy, mitigating any remaining uncertainty about how much RRP capacity will exist around the time of liftoff.	96	9
201503	302	2015-03-18	meeting	IHRIG	However, deferring a decision until liftoff would enable you to continue to evaluate financial market developments as they evolve in the meantime.	96	9
201503	303	2015-03-18	meeting	IHRIG	Antoine will now continue our presentation.	96	9
201503	304	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	Thanks, Jane.	96	9
201503	305	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	In my remarks, I will discuss options available to policymakers to lower the ON RRP cap, as presented in the memo titled “Lowering the ON RRP Facility Cap after Liftoff.”	96	9
201503	306	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	At this January’s FOMC meeting, most participants indicated that a temporarily elevated ON RRP cap would be appropriate to support monetary policy implementation at the time of liftoff.	96	9
201503	307	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	At the same time, a number of participants emphasized that the Committee should develop plans to ensure that the ON RRP facility is temporary and that it can be phased out once it is no longer needed to help control the federal funds rate.	96	9
201503	308	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	Notably, some policymakers may be uncomfortable with a large Federal Reserve footprint in money markets and may also be concerned that an ON RRP facility with high excess capacity could increase financial-stability risks arising from disruptive surges.	96	9
201503	309	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	In the long run, as the size of the balance sheet normalizes and the level of reserve balances falls, the use of the ON RRP facility could be expected to wane.	96	9
201503	310	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	This process would take several years, as shown by the black line in the lower-left panel, which corresponds to the January Tealbook, Book B baseline scenario.	96	9
201503	311	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	Specifically, once the aggregate level of reserve balances is reduced to its scarcity level, perhaps at about $500 billion, banks’ demand for reserves would likely lead them to bid regularly for federal funds.	96	9
201503	312	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	An ON RRP offering rate at the bottom of the federal funds target range would become relatively unattractive and use of the ON RRP facility would be expected to diminish.	96	9
201503	313	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	This process would make elimination of ON RRPs straightforward.	96	9
201503	314	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	Soon after liftoff, perhaps the most likely outcome is that ON RRP usage will remain well below the elevated cap.	96	9
201503	315	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	Indeed, as Lorie noted, the median respondent to the most recent Desk surveys expects that usage of ON RRP at liftoff will be $300 billion and will decline to $250 billion three years after liftoff, broadly similar with recent surveys.	96	9
201503	316	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	If usage remains well below the elevated cap, that cap could be reduced with likely little effect on money market rates, so long as the facility’s headroom remains sufficient.	96	9
201503	317	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	Such a buffer might be on the order of $100 billion to $200 billion and could potentially change over time to accommodate seasonal or other variation in take-up.	96	9
201503	318	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	One potential complication with reducing the cap relatively quickly after liftoff is that underlying demand for ON RRPs might subsequently increase.	96	9
201503	319	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	For example, some regulatory reforms may lead to greater use of ON RRPs over time.	96	9
201503	320	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	The potential for rising demand could be accommodated in several ways to maintain adequate interest rate control.	96	9
201503	321	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	For example, policymakers could wait longer after liftoff to reduce the cap, could lower the cap but be prepared to raise it if increased demand materializes, or could institute a cap that is responsive to demand.	96	9
201503	322	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	In another scenario, rates remain well controlled and demand for ON RRPs could remain persistently high.	96	9
201503	323	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	This is the more interesting scenario.	96	9
201503	324	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	If usage is high, the ON RRP facility would likely be playing an important role in supporting rates, so the efficacy for interest rate control of elevated ON RRP usage would need to be weighed carefully against its costs.	96	9
201503	325	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	In particular, substantial use of other supplementary tools may be needed to provide sufficient rate support while lowering the ON RRP cap.	96	9
201503	326	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	The potential costs of these tools would likely rise if they are heavily relied upon.	96	9
201503	327	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	The Committee has several options at its disposal to encourage shifts in the composition of the Federal Reserve’s liabilities away from ON RRPs.	96	9
201503	328	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	An advantage of these options is that they could be implemented fairly rapidly and influence money market rates quickly.	96	9
201503	329	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	The simplest option to reduce ON RRP usage is to set a wider spread between the IOER and ON RRP rates by raising the IOER rate.	96	9
201503	330	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	However, the strength of the upward pull due to the IOER rate is unclear, so there is uncertainty about how much this rate would have to be raised; the increase might have to be substantial.	96	9
201503	331	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	Another option would be to substitute term RRPs for ON RRPs.	96	9
201503	332	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	While term RRPs could help reduce the Federal Reserve’s footprint in overnight markets, a shift from ON RRPs to term RRPs likely would not reduce the overall footprint in short-term funding markets, and may even expand it if term operations were sufficiently attractive.	96	9
201503	333	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	Finally, the Committee could use both term RRPs and the TDF to broaden the arbitrage opportunities that are created by IOER and ON RRPs and to attempt to drain enough reserves to create scarcity.	96	9
201503	334	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	Although term tools are unlikely to contribute much to reserve scarcity unless they are used in very substantial sizes, these tools could hasten the reduction in reserve balances to allow the ON RRP facility to be wound down.	96	9
201503	335	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	For example, the blue dashed line illustrates the effect of $1.5 trillion in draining tools on the baseline scenario mentioned above.	96	9
201503	336	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	With this strategy, reserve balances drop to $500 billion around mid-2017, nearly three years earlier than in the baseline scenario.	96	9
201503	337	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	However, substantial use of term tools could increase the Federal Reserve’s involvement in a range of term markets and would likely raise the pecuniary costs of monetary policy implementation.	96	9
201503	338	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	Should circumstances after liftoff change the Committee’s views regarding the costs and benefits of asset sales, it could also consider using such sales to reduce the size of the balance sheet directly.	96	9
201503	339	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	Asset sales may also be effective in reducing ON RRP usage.	96	9
201503	340	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	One approach to asset sales could focus on sales of shorter-dated Treasury securities.	96	9
201503	341	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	At mid-2015, the SOMA Treasury portfolio is projected to hold around $800 billion of Treasury securities with less than three years remaining to maturity.	96	9
201503	342	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	The red dotted line illustrates the projected effect on reserve balances of adding sales to the baseline scenario so that the SOMA portfolio is reduced by roughly $50 billion per month once reinvestment is halted in late 2015.	96	9
201503	343	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	Reserve balances would fall to $2.2 trillion within one year of liftoff (that is, $200 billion lower than the baseline path), and to $700 billion in 2018 (about $700 billion less than the baseline path).	96	9
201503	344	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	Announcing the sales of shorter-dated Treasury securities might also send a signal that boosts short-term rates.	96	9
201503	345	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	However, the effects of such a signal are uncertain, and it could affect rates beyond short-term yields.	96	9
201503	346	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	If longer-term rates rise quickly, financial conditions could tighten more than intended.	96	9
201503	347	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	Combining the liability-side and asset-side tools would likely make them more effective at reducing ON RRP usage quickly.	96	9
201503	348	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	The green dot-dashed line illustrates that the combination of term tools and asset sales described above would reduce reserve balances to about $500 billion by late 2016.	96	9
201503	349	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	To sum up, the Committee has tools at its disposal that can be used to reduce take-up at the ON RRP facility and hence lower an initially high cap while maintaining appropriate interest rate control.	96	9
201503	350	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	The use of these additional tools would have costs, as does ON RRP usage, and the Committee will need to weigh tradeoffs between efficacy and costs for all of the tools.	96	9
201503	351	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	The staff will continue to evaluate the Committee’s policy tools, particularly the ON RRP facility.	96	9
201503	352	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	Finally, clear public communication about the intention to keep the ON RRP capacity only as high as necessary would avoid sending the unintended signal that a large ON RRP facility would be maintained for a period longer than the Committee deems appropriate.	96	9
201503	353	2015-03-18	meeting	MARTIN	While reiterating the importance of a successful liftoff, the Committee could reaffirm its intent to use an ON RRP facility only to the extent necessary and to phase it out when it is no longer needed to help control the federal funds rate.	96	9

201503	477	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	Regarding the initial setting of the aggregate cap on reverse repos, I’d rather not put us in a position of having to raise the cap after liftoff.	96	9
