201503	479	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	It could signal we don’t have adequate interest rate control or that we’re reconsidering whether or not the facility will be temporary.	96	9
201503	480	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	That leaves me with the choice of setting a high cap at the start and then lowering it over time as we gain experience, versus setting no cap at liftoff and then imposing one later.	96	9
201503	481	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	I don’t have strong preferences for one over the other.	96	9
201503	482	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	Either one seems consistent with the normalization plans that we’ve laid out, provided it’s accompanied by appropriate communications.	96	9
201503	483	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	We are going to need to explain the purpose of whatever design choice we make, especially as it is going to differ, I think, from our test design.	96	9
201503	484	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	Then we need to reiterate that we will use the facility only to the extent necessary; that we plan to phase it out; and that phaseout might be accomplished by imposing caps on the facility’s size, which we could reduce over time; and that we’ll periodically reconsider various design features of this and our other tools.	96	9
201503	485	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	Then, once we have a clearer sense of how our tools are working together to control short-term rates, we can communicate a plan for phasing out the facility.	96	9
201503	486	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	To reduce its size while maintaining adequate control of short-term interest rates, we may indeed need to rely on several of our tools, including asset sales.	96	9
201503	487	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	At this point I wouldn’t want to rule them out, but I do think we need further study of how these tools would likely interact with one another.	96	9
201503	488	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	One final thought:  I would be cautious in committing, at this point, to any particular timetable for a reduction in the size of the reverse repo facility cap, or imposition of a cap if we start without one.	96	9
201503	489	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	As I read the staff memo, that seems to be the intention in option 2, and perhaps in option 1 as well.	96	9
201503	490	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	This gives me pause.	96	9
201503	491	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	Even if today we think it likely we could reduce the cap size fairly soon after liftoff, we may run into some surprises.	96	9
201503	492	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	Aren’t the uncertainties surrounding interest rate control the crux of today’s discussion?	96	9
201503	493	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	I wouldn’t want to hurt our credibility by having to go back on an earlier communication.	96	9
201503	494	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	That’s similar to my distaste for putting ourselves in the situation of having to raise the cap at a later date.	96	9
201503	495	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	Rather than commit now to a timetable, I’d prefer more general communication, as I just outlined.	96	9
201503	496	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201503	497	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	96	9
201503	498	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	President Lacker.	96	9
201503	499	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201503	500	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	As I said just a few moments ago, I think the question is, what size of an initial cap we are going to adopt?	96	9
201503	501	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	To me, $800 billion seems like a fine number.	96	9
201503	502	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	I could support $1 trillion.	96	9
201503	503	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	I could go up to the size of our Treasuries portfolio, $2 trillion to $2½ trillion, whatever that calculation is that Simon alluded to.	96	9
201503	504	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	Regarding how to scale back usage after liftoff, the case in which usage falls fairly rapidly of its own accord is straightforward.	96	9
201503	505	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	The harder case is one in which usage remains elevated and high.	96	9
201503	506	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	As I reviewed the staff memo, my attention was immediately attracted to the phrase “asset-side tools,” and I began fantasizing about auctioning off our holdings of MBS and long- term Treasuries at a fairly rapid clip.	96	9
201503	507	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	However, I suspect that option may fail to garner a majority of support from the Committee.	96	9
201503	508	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	In that case, I would favor selling short-term assets, although it seems unlikely that we could sell a quantity sufficient to make reserves scarce enough any time soon.	96	9
201503	509	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	As a third choice, I would favor raising IOER above the top of the federal funds target range, starting with 5 basis points and seeing what happens, moving to 10 or 15 basis points if that is not enough.	96	9
201503	510	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	As to the other options, using term RRPs seems inferior.	96	9
201503	511	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	It is going to leave the RRP program, in general, with the same footprint and would take an unrealistically large set of operations to reach the point at which reserve balances are scarce enough to make a difference.	96	9
201503	512	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	I have always raised questions about whether term tools really make reserves scarce, because they are just term monetary assets.	96	9
201503	513	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	They are not nonmonetary assets and are unlikely to be marginally constraining for the participating institutions.	96	9
201503	514	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201503	515	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Can I ask a clarifying question?	96	9
201503	516	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Yes.	96	9
201503	517	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Let’s imagine that the overnight RRP facility wasn’t very big; let’s just say its usage is $200 billion or $300 billion.	96	9
201503	518	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Would you still sell assets?	96	9
201503	519	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	No, I wouldn’t see a need to.	96	9
201503	520	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Okay.	96	9
201503	521	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	President Rosengren.	96	9
201503	522	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201503	523	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	President Lacker’s fantasy is my nightmare.	96	9
201503	524	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	[Laughter]	96	9
201503	525	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	When we announce that we are raising the range for the federal funds rate, it is critically important that we are successful in quickly moving the federal funds rate within the range and then keeping it there.	96	9
201503	526	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	With our credibility at stake, and with a high degree of uncertainty about the market response when short-term rates are initially raised above current levels, I would argue against any cap on the ON RRP facility at the time of liftoff.	96	9
201503	527	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	If the ON RRP take-up remains very large for some period after liftoff—and we should discuss how long a period we would be comfortable with—we should raise the IOER high enough that the federal funds rate rises to be within the federal funds target range without excessive take-up of the ON RRP facility.	96	9
201503	528	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	Again, we should discuss the Committee’s definition of “excessive.”	96	9
201503	529	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	For example, in order to reduce the risk of extensive use of the ON RRP facility, we might raise the IOER rate to 60 basis points to maintain the federal funds rate within the 25 to 50 basis point range.	96	9
201503	530	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	The IOER rate can then be adjusted subsequently to fine-tune the placement of the federal funds rate as we better understand the relationship that the federal funds rate has with the spread between IOER and ON RRP rates.	96	9
201503	531	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	This raises the question of whether we have communicated sufficiently that, while the target range for the federal funds rate will be 25 basis points, the spread between the IOER and the ON RRP rates may need to be greater than 25 basis points.	96	9
201503	532	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	Particularly in our explanation of liftoff, it should be clear that the IOER rate will be adjusted to ensure that the federal funds rate stays within the target range.	96	9
201503	533	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	As a sidenote, the dependence on the IOER rate to generate the desired range for the federal funds rate does create a governance problem.	96	9
201503	534	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	Ideally, the FOMC would be setting the IOER rate.	96	9
201503	535	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	And, if reform legislation were to move through the Congress, I would prefer the IOER rate be a vote of the FOMC, as it is the key variable in setting monetary policy under our current exit guidelines.	96	9
201503	536	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	The main strategy for reducing the ON RRP take-up after liftoff should be setting the IOER rate high enough that the federal funds rate is trading within the desired range without excessive reliance on the ON RRP.	96	9
201503	537	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	Some of the suggested remedies in the memo might be tantamount to changing monetary policy to minimize reliance on the ON RRP.	96	9
201503	538	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	The tool should be set to generate the desired policy.	96	9
201503	539	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	Policy should not be adjusted to minimize the use of the tool.	96	9
201503	540	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	For example, I am strongly opposed to asset sales.	96	9
201503	541	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	First, this would reverse our often- repeated promise not to engage in significant sales, possibly reducing the credibility of our exit strategy.	96	9
201503	542	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	Second, even if the sales were limited to very short-term securities, I am worried that investors might become concerned that longer-maturity securities would be sold next.	96	9
201503	543	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	This concern would be exacerbated by the relatively small stock of short-term securities currently in our portfolio.	96	9
201503	544	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	If monetary control is at stake and we choose to sell very short-term securities, these could be exhausted before control is regained, implying that longer-term securities will soon be on the auction block.	96	9
201503	545	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	This could potentially cause a Treasuries sales “tantrum” as investors in longer-term securities doubt the credibility of our promise on holding securities to maturity.	96	9
201503	546	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	The costs could be large if our initial announcement of short-term sales results in significantly raising medium- and longer-term rates.	96	9
201503	547	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	The potential benefit would be avoiding elevated use of the ON RRP until our balance sheet is reduced, but that benefit does not seem worth the undermining of our announced exit principles.	96	9
201503	548	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	If we are seriously considering asset sales or other means to minimize the use of the ON RRP, I would want to stop reinvesting sooner, although this would also be changing policy to minimize use of a tool.	96	9
201503	549	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	The key in my mind is that while the costs of a larger overnight RRP facility that lasts for longer are somewhat ill defined, the costs of tightening policy are reasonably clear.	96	9
201503	550	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	As a consequence, we need to have a better discussion of why short-term use of the ON RRP is such a problem that it causes us to tighten by stopping reinvesting or signaling in any way that we would engage in asset sales.	96	9
201503	551	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201503	552	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	96	9
201503	553	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	President Lockhart.	96	9
201503	554	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201503	555	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	On the first question regarding my views on the two aggregate cap options, I have come around to the view that the Committee appropriately should take minimal monetary-control risks in the first phase of liftoff.	96	9
201503	556	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	I prefer suspending the aggregate cap—that is, option 2.	96	9
201503	557	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	I think we can operate the overnight reverse repo facility without a cap for a brief period without serious consequence.	96	9
201503	558	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	As a practical matter, if an episode of severe financial instability or risk of instability were to materialize in the early weeks post-liftoff, we could react with limits on take-up appropriate to the circumstances at hand.	96	9
201503	559	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	I see little need to impose a limit at the outset as long as we clearly intend to assess take- up, assess rate control effectiveness and the risks post-liftoff, and then, on that basis, impose a cap.	96	9
201503	560	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	On the second question, strategies to later reduce the overnight reverse repo take-up, the staff memo lays out two discrete methods:  widening the spread to IOER and draining reserves.	96	9
201503	561	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	Early on, I think we must rely on widening the spread.	96	9
201503	562	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	Execution of a draining strategy that includes asset sales would take a while.	96	9
201503	563	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	For planning purposes, I anticipate a shorter time horizon for reducing and phasing out the overnight reverse repo program.	96	9
201503	564	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	I think there may be some scope for a combination of spread widening and draining, but I am hoping the need for the overnight reverse repo program will fall away long before we could get excess reserve balances of $500 billion.	96	9
201503	565	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	So, I see draining operations, including asset sales, as a supplemental tool.	96	9
201503	566	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	The questions posed for this round were very high level, asking for our general views.	96	9
201503	567	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	I think it would be prudent to go a little further and try to agree, at least tentatively, on a baseline post-liftoff plan for implementing reductions in the overnight reverse repo facility, if things go well.	96	9
201503	568	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	To be sure, we will be learning by doing and we will make tactical adjustments as we go, but I think a discussion at this meeting or the April meeting of a plan with more specifics might highlight some issues important to consider.	96	9
201503	569	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	For discussion purposes, should participants care to react, here is how I am thinking about phaseout, if things go well.	96	9
201503	570	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	After a couple of moves of the federal funds rate target range, we assess whether and where federal funds are trading in range and where other short-term rates are trading.	96	9
201503	571	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	If satisfactory, at that point we announce an overnight reverse repo cap.	96	9
201503	572	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	If all goes well with respect to volatility and the rate continues to trade in range, at the next rate move we widen the spread by holding the overnight reverse repo rate where it is.	96	9
201503	573	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	We continue to widen the spread with each rate move until take-up under the program fades away.	96	9
201503	574	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	I am sure we can imagine other scenarios, and certainly the more adverse scenarios have been discussed earlier.	96	9
201503	575	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	For example, if federal funds trade at or very near the floor, and there is large take-up, that would be one scenario.	96	9
201503	576	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	If such a situation persisted, it seems to me that we might have to resort earlier and longer to term tools and the decision to cease reinvestment, and maybe sales, as part of this process.	96	9
201503	577	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	If, as we proceed post-liftoff, we are to optimize the tradeoff between monetary control and avoidance of the costs and undesirable potential consequences of a large and persistent long- term overnight reverse repo program, I favor some concrete advance planning as a frame of reference, at least, for future decisions.	96	9
201503	578	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201503	579	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	96	9
201503	580	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Tarullo.	96	9
201503	581	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201503	582	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	I guess, in part, my remarks are taking up the issue that Eric raised.	96	9
201503	583	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	I think it’s quite hard to say how much of a risk to financial stability an ON RRP facility could pose if it continued long enough and on a sufficient scale as to be plausibly regarded as a safe haven to which money markets could run from privately created assets, such as commercial paper, during a period of stress.	96	9
201503	584	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	But because I seem to have fallen into the role of Cassandra for this topic, let me play to type today, at least for the heuristic purpose of exploring some of the potential costs of the ON RRP, which the staff memo alluded to but didn’t actually discuss.	96	9
201503	585	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	I want to do that by placing this discussion in a little bit of context, and the context is essentially the progressive growth of the ON RRP as the centerpiece, what we expect to be the most important tool for policy-normalization purposes.	96	9
201503	586	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	The use of an ON RRP was explicitly proposed to the Committee less than two years ago.	96	9
201503	587	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	In a July 23, 2013, memo to the Committee, it was characterized as a “useful addition” to the proposed set of normalizing tools that had been previously identified as consisting of IOER, TDF, and non-overnight RRPs.	96	9
201503	588	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	In the intervening period, the staff and many Committee members have come to conclude that the ON RRP will actually be essential to making IOER an effective tool, and that the other tools, while perhaps playing a secondary or tertiary role, have significant limitations.	96	9
201503	589	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	This focus on ON RRP was evident in the memos that were circulated to the Committee prior to our discussion last year.	96	9
201503	590	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	As you may recall, at the time, the staff suggested a facility with a $500 billion to $600 billion cap.	96	9
201503	591	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	And, in response to concerns expressed by a number of us, the testing has proceeded with a cap of $300 billion.	96	9
201503	592	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	This apparently had the intended effect of curbing market expectations regarding the eventual size of the facility.	96	9
201503	593	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Obviously, this is one means of trying to prevent the expectation that the Federal Reserve would be available as a borrower of last resort.	96	9
201503	594	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	In truth, of course, even a cap might not do the trick in a stress period during which we might come under heavy, perhaps even self-generated, pressure to expand an ON RRP program in the interest of stabilizing money market funds in the wake of Dodd-Frank’s elimination of other sources of support for those funds.	96	9
201503	595	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	But at least at the margin, and potentially more fundamentally, a moderate cap would work against the development of money market fund business models based on regular or contingent investment opportunities at the Federal Reserve.	96	9
201503	596	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	I gather that the mention in the January minutes of a likely increase in the cap at the time of liftoff didn’t lead to a basic change in market perceptions, but I think Governor Powell mentioned—and I noticed the same thing—that there has been at least some change among some market participants in the expectation of a significantly larger program.	96	9
201503	597	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Now, in the memo distributed prior to this meeting, the choice presented to the Committee is no longer $500 billion or $600 billion, but $800 billion or no cap at all.	96	9
201503	598	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	This is not a particularly appealing choice for me because I think either one risks communicating a substantial program.	96	9
201503	599	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	And it’s not hard to imagine a decision dynamic in the FOMC that gravitates, at each meeting, toward maximum assurance that our target range will be achieved with some precision, because financial-stability risks will probably always seem hypothetical and much less immediate than monetary policy targeting.	96	9
201503	600	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	This is the way financial-stability risks arise.	96	9
201503	601	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	At any one moment, near-term policy desiderata always trump the potential hypothetical growth of financial stability concerns, whether it’s commercial real estate lending or mortgage-backed securities or anything else.	96	9
201503	602	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	That’s not to say that’s what’s going to happen here, but that really is the dynamic of decisionmaking:  You have something hypothetical, and you’ve got a near-term policy aim of some sort—whether it’s economic growth or monetary policy control—that, among the decisionmakers, always seems to have a higher priority.	96	9
201503	603	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	By the time our balance sheet shrinks enough to make the ON RRP less relevant, it’s not hard to imagine a future FOMC being warned that reducing the cap or eliminating the ON RRP could itself produce significant disruptions in money markets.	96	9
201503	604	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	At that point, the tradeoff between avoiding near-term disruptions and a possible exacerbation of what are, again, hypothetical, longer-term financial-stability risks, could well be decided in favor of avoiding short-term problems.	96	9
201503	605	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	So, at least at this time, I don’t have a favorite across those two alternatives, and picking up on one of President Lockart’s themes, I would like to hear at a future meeting a more elaborated proposal.	96	9
201503	606	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	My preference is not to decide this issue today but to try to build into the obvious imperative of achieving monetary policy control a more specific set of proposals for how to deal with the potential risks.	96	9
201503	607	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	As to the second question on strategies to reduce the ON RRP after liftoff, let me first say that I appreciate the language changes that were made in the bullet points on operational details proposed to be included in the minutes of this meeting.	96	9
201503	608	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	I think the specific invocation of other tools in the context of an anticipated early reduction in the size of the ON RRP is helpful in countering expectations of ongoing, larger scales for the facility.	96	9
201503	609	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	I think, though I’m honestly not entirely sure, that I would favor something like an explicit commitment to reduce the cap beginning within a few meetings following liftoff, because I believe that the imperative is to have a successful liftoff at the early stage of normalization, but that the possibility of a little softness in the funds rate six or eight months later would not be damaging to our credibility.	96	9
201503	610	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Also, a specific commitment of this sort would force us to make use of some of the other tools mentioned in the staff memo.	96	9
201503	611	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	However, based on Committee discussion to date and, indeed, the first group of speakers this morning, I’m not at all sure that I’d get much support for this approach—which, by the way, whether it’s reducing the cap or putting a cap in place following a no cap or $2.5 trillion cap at the outset is basically the same exercise.	96	9
201503	612	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	In the absence of such a commitment, I’d probably go along with just about any configuration of other tools and reducing reliance on the ON RRP that could garner substantial support on the Committee.	96	9
201503	613	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	My own instinct is toward some combination of a higher IOER rate and greater use of term RRPs, and, depending on how large the ON RRP had become, perhaps even some sales of shorter-term Treasuries.	96	9
201503	614	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	I think Eric has already pointed out a certain clunkiness in trying to put these tools together, which, as a governance matter, is probably something that we need to address.	96	9
201503	615	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	But more important to me than any of these particulars are, first, that we convince ourselves that we have alternatives to a large, ongoing ON RRP that we are willing to deploy with full recognition of their possible downsides; and, second, that we state this position publicly with as much detail as fairly reflects our actual eventual consensus.	96	9
201503	616	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	In a similar vein, I would note in passing that I would favor continued testing of term RRPs at the end of quarters precisely because it will signal that we’re taking this tool seriously, though I also will note that I would understand the reluctance of members who might favor a liftoff during the next several meetings to authorize testing for the rest of the year because, as Simon says, once “patient” is off, that may send some signal on liftoff timing.	96	9
201503	617	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Finally, Madam Chair, let me close with the hope that initial takeoff turns out to be about what we’ve been anticipating lately so that we’re spared having to make what I think is an increasingly difficult tradeoff that we’re contemplating in this discussion.	96	9
201503	618	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Thank you.	96	9
201503	619	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	96	9
201503	620	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Acting President Prichard.	96	9
201503	621	2015-03-18	meeting	PRICHARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201503	622	2015-03-18	meeting	PRICHARD	The FOMC must appear confident during the early stages of liftoff by exercising fairly tight control over the funds rate.	96	9
201503	623	2015-03-18	meeting	PRICHARD	Doing so would establish our ability to conduct monetary policy under these unprecedented conditions and provide the necessary confidence to markets and the general public that the Committee can maintain sufficient control over monetary policy until such time as our balance sheet is fully normalized.	96	9
201503	624	2015-03-18	meeting	PRICHARD	In this regard, I believe that we should operate for a brief period without a cap and, then, as quickly as is prudent, impose a cap based on our initial experience.	96	9
201503	625	2015-03-18	meeting	PRICHARD	We would initially refrain from imposing a cap because of the uncertainty of what that initial take-up would be.	96	9
201503	626	2015-03-18	meeting	PRICHARD	By setting a specific cap, we could err on the low side by ending up with a cap that initially binds, resulting in a funds rate that would trade below the targeted range, or we could set a cap that’s too high, which might be misinterpreted as a Committee desiring an unnecessarily large ON RRP facility.	96	9
201503	627	2015-03-18	meeting	PRICHARD	By not specifying a number, we would avoid communicating any particular position as to the size of the facility.	96	9
201503	628	2015-03-18	meeting	PRICHARD	However, it would also be important to communicate that it is the combination of this uncertainty regarding the initial take-up and our desire that the funds rate trade within its target range that leads us to begin without an aggregate quantity restriction.	96	9
201503	629	2015-03-18	meeting	PRICHARD	After obtaining information about the necessary size of the facility, a cap would be established.	96	9
201503	630	2015-03-18	meeting	PRICHARD	Further, we would emphasize that the ON RRP facility is intended to be temporary, and that we will reduce its size as circumstances allow.	96	9
201503	631	2015-03-18	meeting	PRICHARD	We may also wish to authorize the term RRP facility to initially operate only around quarter-end in order to counter the volatility associated with those periods.	96	9
201503	632	2015-03-18	meeting	PRICHARD	However, once we have established our ability to move the funds rate in a regular and fairly precise fashion, I would prefer to ignore the quarter-end effects, as they will have little influence on the effectiveness of overall monetary policy.	96	9
201503	633	2015-03-18	meeting	PRICHARD	It is not unlikely we will find the initial size of the ON RRP facility to be uncomfortably large and, over time, wish to reduce its footprint on financial markets.	96	9
201503	634	2015-03-18	meeting	PRICHARD	Reducing the size of our balance sheet will no doubt help, but that process will be quite long and drawn out, and, therefore, we will require other options.	96	9
201503	635	2015-03-18	meeting	PRICHARD	The outcome I find most appealing is to widen the spread between the IOER rate and the rate paid on the ON RRP facility.	96	9
201503	636	2015-03-18	meeting	PRICHARD	The alternative of introducing a permanent term RRP facility does not seem like an alternative at all because it merely introduces a close substitute, and by not reducing the sum of the two instruments, has little effect on the imprint we will have on financial markets.	96	9
201503	637	2015-03-18	meeting	PRICHARD	The only meaningful way to reduce the size of the facility is to make reserves scarcer or to increase the spread between IOER and the ON RRP rate.	96	9
201503	638	2015-03-18	meeting	PRICHARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201503	639	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	96	9
201503	640	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	First Vice President Holcomb.	96	9
201503	641	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201503	642	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	I am hesitant to comment on the issues related to tools, knowing that this discussion builds on many previous discussions in which I did not participate.	96	9
201503	643	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	However, I have closely read the transcript from the previous meeting and found very insightful comments there, and I would like to thank the authors of the background memo, which was very helpful in helping me to understand these issues.	96	9
201503	644	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	I gained some perspective on the concept of liftoff as a result of a recent discussion with our director, who heads the Johnson Space Center, where liftoffs [laughter] are a regular occurrence.	96	9
201503	645	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	I know that you all are well aware that in Texas, we like to speak using analogies, so if the Committee will indulge me, a couple of comparisons seem relevant.	96	9
201503	646	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	A NASA liftoff shares many characteristics with the liftoff that we are contemplating, including the possibility of last-minute circumstances and issues that change the plan or abort a launch, as well as the need for multiple gauges and alternatives that support in-flight corrections.	96	9
201503	647	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	Our director noted that a successful liftoff is an important step to overall mission success, but what happens after the liftoff in the next 73 seconds, days, weeks, and—in the case of the mission they are launching this month—the next year are more important than the liftoff itself.	96	9
201503	648	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	So, in turning to the question regarding the initial cap, I understand that, like a space launch, our liftoff must go smoothly in order to ensure the successful completion of the mission.	96	9
201503	649	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	Therefore, it will be important that the initial combined cap on RRP take-up be set high enough to ensure that the funds rate stays within the designated target range at liftoff.	96	9
201503	650	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	Therefore, I support operating without a cap initially.	96	9
201503	651	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	To preserve the credibility of our pledge to minimize use of the ON RRP facility, it will be important to either quickly reimpose the cap, if we begin without one, or to reduce our initial cap over time, even if the overnight bank funding rate falls below the lower limit of the Committee’s target range from time to time as a result.	96	9
201503	652	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	You asked that we include our comments on the options for the term RRP quarter-end testing as we go around.	96	9
201503	653	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	On that front, I would say that obviously good quarter-end control of the funds rate will be important, at least through the early phases of the policy normalization process.	96	9
201503	654	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	The Federal Reserve Bank of Dallas research staff has advised that the best way to achieve this control will be with a term RRP facility, as the end-of-quarter term RRPs are relatively illiquid and not continuously on offer, and thus are less likely to facilitate bank runs than our overnight RRPs.	96	9
201503	655	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	So, I would oppose discontinuing quarter-end RRP operations, as noted in our option 3, which I don’t think is really on the table.	96	9
201503	656	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	Recognizing that through this period of transition, the Committee will be watching market developments very closely in order to make in-flight corrections, either of the other proposed options—reauthorizing term RRP operations on a quarter-by-quarter basis or through the end of the year—is a good alternative.	96	9
201503	657	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	We lean toward option 2, knowing that there is still the opportunity to make decisions as to whether or not to actually conduct the operations, as was pointed out.	96	9
201503	658	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	After liftoff, we’ve looked at the remaining tools under consideration and have a few comments.	96	9
201503	659	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	As previously indicated, we favor continuing end-of-quarter term RRP operations through at least early phases of normalization.	96	9
201503	660	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	These operations help achieve good monetary policy control at quarter-ends, and the financial-stability risks associated with term RRPs seem likely to be lower than those associated with overnight RRPs.	96	9
201503	661	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	If overnight RRP take-up away from the quarter-ends is so high as to raise unacceptable financial-stability concerns, we see additional term RRPs, not quarter-end RRPs, as the first line of defense.	96	9
201503	662	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	Interest costs from the term RRPs are relatively low, and term RRPs are likely to be nearly as effective as overnight RRPs in supporting short-term interest rates.	96	9
201503	663	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	Yet financial-stability risks are lower.	96	9
201503	664	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	We agree that substituting term RRPs for overnight RRPs will not reduce the Federal Reserve’s footprint in financial markets.	96	9
201503	665	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	The best way to reduce that footprint is to phase out reinvestment of principal relatively quickly so that the balance sheet shrinks and both overnight and term RRPs are no longer necessary.	96	9
201503	666	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	We are less confident that term deposits will play a useful role in normalization.	96	9
201503	667	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	They bear relatively high interest costs.	96	9
201503	668	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	They would have to be adopted on a large scale in order to drain reserves to the point at which overnight RRP demand dries up, and it is uncertain that they will induce banks to pursue arbitrage opportunities more aggressively, even with an early withdrawal option.	96	9
201503	669	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	This is something that we would like to learn more about as we go forward.	96	9
201503	670	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	And then, finally, because President Fisher will be president for four more days, I feel compelled to support President Lockhart’s call for advance planning that would lay out options under various possible scenarios and essentially create a decision tree.	96	9
201503	671	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	Thank you.	96	9
201503	672	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	96	9
201503	673	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	President Evans.	96	9
201503	674	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201503	675	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	Helen’s very nice comments about space analogies remind me that I had the very high honor yesterday of meeting former astronaut James Lovell, of Apollo 13 fame.	96	9
201503	676	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	I had the feeling that we are going to find a way to bring everything together here, right?	96	9
201503	677	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	Here we go.	96	9
201503	678	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	You know, to ensure monetary control, at any rate.	96	9
201503	679	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	We hope not like that.	96	9
201503	680	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	[Laughter]	96	9
201503	681	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	My views on the steps we need to take to ensure monetary control have not changed since the previous meeting.	96	9
201503	682	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	When the time comes to raise rates, it is important that we maintain monetary control in line with achieving our policy goals.	96	9
201503	683	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	I do not have strong preferences regarding whether that control should be achieved with an elevated cap or a suspension of the cap.	96	9
201503	684	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	I don’t think at this point we have sufficient knowledge to judge the relative risk of an $800 billion aggregate cap versus a temporary suspension of the cap on financial stability or our footprint in markets.	96	9
201503	685	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	Therefore, to ensure we will have the control we seek, I would be willing to suspend the cap, if the Committee forms such a consensus.	96	9
201503	686	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	As long as we effectively communicate to market participants that the elevated capacity is temporary and we follow through by reducing the capacity as needed, potential financial stability risks and footprint issues should be minimal.	96	9
201503	687	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	Accordingly, we should make sure all other tools are ready, if needed, to reduce the overnight RRP cap.	96	9
201503	688	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	So, I would continue with the testing of the term RRP facility.	96	9
201503	689	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	And, by authorizing quarter-end tests for the remainder of the year, we reduce our administrative costs and avoid potentially confusing signals regarding the timing of liftoff.	96	9
201503	690	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	So, I support this proposal.	96	9
201503	691	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	More generally, I would prefer to rely on our liability-side tools to reduce ON RRP take- up after liftoff.	96	9
201503	692	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	I would not alter our previously agreed-upon exit strategy on asset sales.	96	9
201503	693	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	First, I expect our liability-side tools to work as intended, so I don’t think we will need asset sales to maintain monetary control.	96	9
201503	694	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	More importantly, in the absence of material changes in market conditions, altering the exit strategy we already communicated might confuse market participants.	96	9
201503	695	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	Of course, if circumstances did change enough to call into question our control, I would not be opposed to asset sales.	96	9
201503	696	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	But based on our tests to date, I don’t anticipate we will need to resort to sales prior to our established plan.	96	9
201503	697	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201503	698	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	96	9
201503	699	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	President Williams.	96	9
201503	700	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201503	701	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	And thanks again to the staff for the helpful background memos.	96	9
201503	702	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	This discussion has already been very illuminating.	96	9
201503	703	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	I didn’t actually realize that my colleagues’ both fantasies and nightmares centered on policy normalization.	96	9
201503	704	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	I think when the transcripts come out, the psychologists will have a field day with this discussion.	96	9
201503	705	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	To me, the key overarching priority is for us to maintain monetary control at and after liftoff.	96	9
201503	706	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Embarking on the normalization process with an overnight repo facility with an $800 billion limit would most likely suffice.	96	9
201503	707	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	However, to avoid any chance of losing monetary control at this critical juncture, I am comfortable with operating the facility without an aggregate cap during the initial normalization phase.	96	9
201503	708	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Of course, a potential downside—which has already been raised by a number of people—to having a very large or unlimited initial cap is that it could be misinterpreted as signaling the intention to maintain a large presence in the market in the future.	96	9
201503	709	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	We have already indicated that this is a temporary measure, and it will be ended when it is no longer needed, and we should continue to reiterate that message.	96	9
201503	710	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	But like President Mester, I would like to say that we shouldn’t get locked into a particular timing of the reduction of capacity.	96	9
201503	711	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	For instance, the proposed language from the minutes states that we plan to reduce the facility’s capacity “fairly soon” after liftoff, which some might interpret as within a couple weeks or a couple months.	96	9
201503	712	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	If this phrase appears in the FOMC minutes, I am fairly confident that we will be asked what “fairly soon” means, as it is apparently a new phrase for the FOMC.	96	9
201503	713	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	I would prefer to leave our options open as to the timing of the adjustment of the cap, so that we maintain flexibility to best balance our goals of monetary control and financial stability.	96	9
201503	714	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	So I suggest deleting that sentence.	96	9
201503	715	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Turning to the strategies to limit very high overnight reverse repo facility usage after liftoff, the best course of action is difficult to determine in advance.	96	9
201503	716	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	And although, like President Lockhart, I think it makes a lot of sense to war-game different strategies or to have decision trees in connection with that, I do think the appropriate strategy will depend on the reasons underlying the high take-up rate as well as on the economic landscape.	96	9
201503	717	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	If a high take-up rate materializes, we will have to examine its causes and weigh the costs and benefits of alternative approaches in this light.	96	9
201503	718	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Having said that, we were asked our views on this.	96	9
201503	719	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	In general, I see term RRPs as the preferred tool for curbing demand for overnight reverse repos while still facilitating monetary control.	96	9
201503	720	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Again, this is in the context of the very high sustained usage of the overnight reverse repo facility.	96	9
201503	721	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Importantly, the term RRP tool provides some flexibility, because we can determine the time and size of offerings.	96	9
201503	722	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	And, as the background memo highlights, we could also discourage the use of overnight reverse repos by raising the IOER rate.	96	9
201503	723	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Now, I find that option less attractive, as we would be widening the target range for reasons other than monetary control, which might muddle our communications.	96	9
201503	724	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	I am also concerned about the negative public perceptions that higher interest payments going to banks at a cost to the taxpayer might create in that case.	96	9
201503	725	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Now, on the other side of the ledger, sales of short-term Treasuries would likewise provide a sensible approach from a monetary policy perspective.	96	9
201503	726	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Just think about the economics of it.	96	9
201503	727	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	It would put upward pressure on short-term rates while having little, if any, effect on longer-term rates.	96	9
201503	728	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	However, as has been mentioned by President Rosengren and others, asset sales during the early stages of normalization could be misconstrued as signaling a tighter overall policy stance.	96	9
201503	729	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Some might think it hints that asset sales of longer-term securities may be in the offing.	96	9
201503	730	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Looking further down the road, once we have moved sufficiently away from the zero lower bound and have ceased reinvestments, asset sales, specifically of shorter-term Treasuries, could be a useful approach.	96	9
201503	731	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Under those conditions, they could be accurately described as a tactical means to reduce the balance sheet with no greater implication for future monetary policy.	96	9
201503	732	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	In terms of the term RRP testing, I am supportive of reauthorizing through the end of the year.	96	9
201503	733	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Thank you.	96	9
201503	734	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	96	9

201503	737	2015-03-18	meeting	GEORGE	As the staff memo notes, the ability to clearly demonstrate that we can steer short-term rates is paramount.	96	9
201503	738	2015-03-18	meeting	GEORGE	With that in mind, I support including operational details about the Committee’s plan for liftoff in the minutes of this meeting to remind market participants of the expected contour of the ON RRP’s purpose and its capacity.	96	9
201503	739	2015-03-18	meeting	GEORGE	I can support operating for a brief period after liftoff without a cap on the size of this facility—of course, subject to the size of the portfolio, as others have noted.	96	9
201503	740	2015-03-18	meeting	GEORGE	In terms of strategies the Committee could follow to reduce ON RRP take-up after liftoff, it seems reasonable to adjust the cap at some point, as the staff memo suggests, with sufficient headroom to ensure control of short-term rates, but not too large to make the facility susceptible to large, rapid inflows.	96	9
201503	741	2015-03-18	meeting	GEORGE	A more challenging scenario, of course, arises in the case of a persistently high level of take-up.	96	9
201503	742	2015-03-18	meeting	GEORGE	To prepare for such circumstances, I think all tools, including term RRPs and the Term Deposit Facility, should be considered to the extent they are needed to drain reserves.	96	9

201503	746	2015-03-18	meeting	GEORGE	Waiting until after liftoff to start this process I view as something of a missed opportunity, so I would support keeping such an option available to use sooner rather than later to effect the level of reserve balances.	96	9
201503	747	2015-03-18	meeting	GEORGE	How the Committee determines ex ante the sequence, the priority, and the circumstances for using these different options, of course, is more challenging.	96	9
201503	748	2015-03-18	meeting	GEORGE	I would agree with others that it may be worthwhile to engage in some sort of scenario analysis under various states of the world where the ON RRP facility is larger than we deem appropriate in order to give the Committee a better sense of which tools are first deployed, when, and under what circumstances.	96	9

201503	775	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I am sympathetic, as I said, to the perspective that we really need tight monetary policy control at the time of liftoff or immediately thereafter—in the next two to three weeks thereafter.	96	9
201503	776	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I would suggest that we should be deemphasizing the role of monetary policy control going forward.	96	9
201503	777	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think the focus on it in our communication risks building a misunderstanding of what the purpose of the Federal Reserve is.	96	9
201503	778	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	If you look at a proposal like the Federal Reserve Accountability and Transparency Act, I think it builds in a misunderstanding that the FOMC’s purpose is to control interest rates, whereas in fact our purpose is to deliver good macroeconomic outcomes through using our tools.	96	9
201503	779	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	And, I think being more relaxed about monetary policy control would be one way to help further people’s understanding that really what we are trying to get to is better macroeconomic outcomes.	96	9
201503	780	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Hitting the target range for the federal funds rate on a daily basis is not essential to that purpose.	96	9

201503	783	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	To me, right now, it seems like the interest rate on excess reserves seems like the best way to resolve that tension.	96	9
201503	784	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But, as I said, I remain open.	96	9
201503	785	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	One point that I want to make is that I think having an occasionally binding constraint is a positive thing for us, not a negative.	96	9
201503	786	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	It gives us experience with having a binding constraint.	96	9
201503	787	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	If we evolved to a point at which we have, say—I will just name a number—a $300 billion cap that binds at quarter-end, and that induces us to have a very low federal funds rate at that time, I don’t see that as a negative at all.	96	9
201503	788	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think that will be good in terms of both markets and our own experience with a binding constraint.	96	9
201503	789	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	To wrap up with some final comments, I favor testing through year-end, if we do indeed drop the word “patient” tomorrow.	96	9
201503	790	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think the Committee is going to drop the word “patient” tomorrow.	96	9
201503	791	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We haven’t had that discussion yet, but I do anticipate that happening.	96	9
201503	792	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Because I anticipate that happening, I favor testing through year-end.	96	9
201503	793	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	And, I have a couple of comments on the wording.	96	9
201503	794	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I am comfortable with having the update to our principles in the March minutes as proposed on page 3 of the staff handout, with three emendations.	96	9
201503	795	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In the first sentence, there is a reference to “the FOMC will use, when it becomes appropriate.”	96	9
201503	796	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I would suggest, Madam Chair, changing “will” to “intends to.”	96	9
201503	797	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think “will” sounds overly definitive and determinative.	96	9
201503	798	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Similarly, in the next sentence, “[w]hen economic conditions warrant the commencement of policy firming, the Federal Reserve will,”	96	9
201503	799	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I would suggest replacing “will” with “intends to.”	96	9
201503	800	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Finally, President Williams raised, I think, a very good point that we don’t necessarily want to get into the new game of defining what “fairly soon” means.	96	9
201503	801	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I am a little less comfortable with just dropping that sentence.	96	9

201503	810	2015-03-18	meeting	BULLARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201503	811	2015-03-18	meeting	BULLARD	I have just a few comments on the two questions that were asked.	96	9
201503	812	2015-03-18	meeting	BULLARD	The first question is, should there be an aggregate cap on the overnight RRP program at liftoff?	96	9
201503	813	2015-03-18	meeting	BULLARD	My counsel is that we not have a cap at liftoff and then set a reasonable cap during the aftermath.	96	9
201503	814	2015-03-18	meeting	BULLARD	On the second question—general views on limiting the overnight RRP program take-up after liftoff—in what the memo calls the “complex case” in which demand for overnight RRP is significant during the period after liftoff, I generally think that interest rate control trumps the issues associated with potential financial instability.	96	9
201503	815	2015-03-18	meeting	BULLARD	I would not wish to put an artificial limit on overnight RRP if it would damage the Committee’s interest rate control credibility.	96	9
201503	816	2015-03-18	meeting	BULLARD	The options in a large post-liftoff take-up scenario, as I understand them, include, one, raise the IOER rate to increase the spread between the IOER and overnight RRP rates; two, use term repo; three, use the Term Deposit Facility; and, four, use some type of controlled asset sales program.	96	9
201503	817	2015-03-18	meeting	BULLARD	I find myself in general agreement with the analysis in the memo evaluating these options.	96	9
201503	818	2015-03-18	meeting	BULLARD	Asset sales, in particular, would presumably be a slow approach to reducing dependency on a high-demand overnight RRP facility.	96	9
201503	819	2015-03-18	meeting	BULLARD	Even though I’ve advocated asset sales in the past, I don’t think they’d be useful for this particular purpose, and I agree with President Rosengren in that assessment.	96	9
201503	820	2015-03-18	meeting	BULLARD	The fastest and most direct response, in my opinion, would be to raise the IOER rate in order to increase the spread between the IOER and overnight RRP rates.	96	9
201503	821	2015-03-18	meeting	BULLARD	That seems like the tool the Committee will need to rely upon in real time.	96	9
201503	822	2015-03-18	meeting	BULLARD	I’m not opposed to experimenting further with term repo, the TDF, or both, to reduce reliance on a high-demand overnight RRP program.	96	9
201503	823	2015-03-18	meeting	BULLARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9

201503	825	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Vice Chair.	96	9
201503	826	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201503	827	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	On the first question, I favor operating for a short time without a cap and then imposing a cap based on expected usage.	96	9
201503	828	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I would actually keep the “no cap” in place for maybe the six weeks between FOMC meetings so you’d come back to the next FOMC meeting without any drama.	96	9
201503	829	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Then you would just put the cap in place, so you wouldn’t have to have a video conference.	96	9
201503	830	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	You wouldn’t have to have all of the question marks concerning when are they going to put the cap in place.	96	9
201503	831	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	In my opinion, that would just be a very low-key way of doing—it would avoid a lot of drama.	96	9
201503	832	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I’d set a cap after that six-week period with sufficient headroom so that the market could reasonably expect that it would bind rarely, if ever.	96	9
201503	833	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I would supplement that cap with term RRP around quarter-end.	96	9
201503	834	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	The reason is that we see usage increases around the quarter-end.	96	9
201503	835	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	So why not just have the term RRP take up that slack?	96	9
201503	836	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	That would allow you to operate safely with a lower overnight RRP cap.	96	9
201503	837	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	To put that all in place, I would authorize the series of term RRP tests that we’re talking about over the next three quarter-ends—June, September, December.	96	9
201503	838	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Because you have the tests in place, there would be no errors of signaling to the market that liftoff was going to occur soon.	96	9
201503	839	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	That way, you could go “live” if you actually decide to lift off in June, September, or December.	96	9
201503	840	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	To me, having no cap is slightly more prudent than having a high cap because, obviously, there’s a little bit of tail risk that the high cap might not be high enough.	96	9
201503	841	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I also think it’s superior because, by having no cap, you’re not sending any message about how big you think the usage is going to be, how much headroom you think you need so that it’s not binding.	96	9
201503	842	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	It is actually very content-free in terms of how much you expect the overnight RRP to be used over the medium term.	96	9
201503	843	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	With respect to the second question, I thought the memo made it very clear that we have two broad sets of options in terms of managing the demand for overnight RRPs.	96	9
201503	844	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	We can change the relative interest rates, or we can drain the amount of excess reserves in the system.	96	9
201503	845	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	But my own view is a little different, maybe, from others’.	96	9
201503	846	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I think it’s premature to make a precise decision about what we should do.	96	9
201503	847	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I think all we really need to know at this point is that we have sufficient tools available to make overnight RRP usage go down faster than would occur just from balance sheet runoff and growth of currency outstanding, if we thought that a steeper decline in overnight RRP usage were desirable.	96	9
201503	848	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	It seems to me that we should see what happens after liftoff in terms of demand.	96	9
201503	849	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	We may not have any problem at all that we need to address.	96	9
201503	850	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	The take-up of the overnight RRP could be low.	96	9
201503	851	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I think making too big a fuss about this now sends a mixed message to market participants about how committed we are to monetary policy control over the medium term.	96	9
201503	852	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Now, in terms of ordering them, I would think that raising the IOER relative to the overnight RRP would be your first port of call.	96	9
201503	853	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Then the reserve draining tools, like the Term Deposit Facility and term RRPs, would be a second port of call.	96	9
201503	854	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I’m sort of where President Rosengren is.	96	9
201503	855	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I’m pretty averse to going to the asset sales just because I think it would be very hard to be confident that that wouldn’t leak out into a bigger market reaction in terms of financial conditions.	96	9
201503	856	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I would very much support, though, all the other people that have called for more work on a decision tree to understand, if this happens, what would we do?	96	9
201503	857	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I think there are a lot of branches, and I think we should spend more time working out how we would proceed down these different branches.	96	9
201503	858	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	One final thing:  I thought the language in the minutes was fine.	96	9
201503	859	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	There was some discussion about the issue of “fairly soon.”	96	9
201503	860	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I think we want to tell people that it’s going to come down after some period of time.	96	9
201503	861	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	So, my own view is that taking out that sentence may be “a bridge too far.”	96	9
201503	862	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I know “fairly soon” is imprecise.	96	9
201503	863	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I’d love to come up with better language, but I don’t have anything that’s more precise at this point.	96	9

201503	867	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201503	868	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	I’m grateful to the staff for writing the memos on these topics.	96	9
201503	869	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	They lay out the issues in a clear and straightforward way.	96	9
201503	870	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	I’d also like to thank the Federal Reserve Bank of New York staff who have carried out the experiments that have gone a long way to persuading us that it will be possible to use the ON RRP tool to help achieve the target federal funds rates we set at and after liftoff.	96	9
201503	871	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	As everyone agrees, our primary aim with regard to the use of our new method of setting the federal funds rate by using both the IOER rate and the ON RRP rate must be to make sure that we’re able to insert and maintain the federal funds rate in the ranges that we decide and announce.	96	9
201503	872	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	We’ve been saying for years that we have the tools we need, and we’ve been experimenting for some while, and the credibility of the Federal Reserve would be severely set back if we pushed the button and failed to lift off as announced.	96	9
201503	873	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	That means we have to set a very high initial aggregate cap to make sure we have the capacity we need.	96	9
201503	874	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	Now, I wish I had a probability figure to attach to the scenario in which, if we set it at $800 billion, we’ll hit $800 billion, because if that was an extremely low number, on the whole it’s probably better to have a smaller cap than a bigger one.	96	9
201503	875	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	But the problem is that not only can’t I get anybody to give me a number—or at least nobody has given me a number they’ll commit to—it’s that we don’t actually have any idea about how to figure out that probability.	96	9
201503	876	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	Consequently, I favor not having a cap temporarily and then coming back to one reasonably soon after we start operating the new system.	96	9
201503	877	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	Once we’ve established the new system and learned more about the demand for it and the effectiveness of the facility, we can put a new cap in place.	96	9
201503	878	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	Between President Lockhart’s “couple of meetings” over which I hope we’ll be doing a gradual increase in rates—and that could be a year if we’re doing two or three increases—and President Dudley’s “six weeks,”	96	9
201503	879	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	I don’t know where we’re going to end up on that.	96	9
201503	880	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	Obviously it will be better if it can be sooner, but I think that we just have to accept the fact that you can’t both pre-commit strongly and pay no attention to developments that happen afterward.	96	9
201503	881	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	So we’re going to have to be flexible on this, with enough people being around the table to persuade us that we’d better not be too flexible if we want to retain our credibility.	96	9
201503	882	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	Regarding how long to avoid having a cap, clearly at every stage it would be more convenient to have the ON RRP facility—there’s always some utility to having an extra tool in hand.	96	9
201503	883	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	But we’ll have to find a way of lowering the length of time we use it.	96	9
201503	884	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	There will be a benefit to actually getting rid of it.	96	9
201503	885	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	I think if we were going to do it one way we’d thought through, it would actually be related to the volume of reductions we plan to undertake in the size of our portfolio, because when the portfolio is so big, that’s the period when we need this.	96	9
201503	886	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	I it would, I think, be related to the size of the portfolio and not to the passage of time.	96	9
201503	887	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	But I hope we do it much more rapidly than that.	96	9
201503	888	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	We’ve all discussed the fact that if it doesn’t work, there are other things we could do.	96	9
201503	889	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	We could increase our use of term RRPs and term deposits and, if necessary, we could begin to sell short-term assets.	96	9
201503	890	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	I would be very interested in getting some idea from the Desk, or anybody else who thinks they know, about how effective raising the IOER rate would be in enabling us to stay in the range.	96	9
201503	891	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	If we actually have a thought of doing that, we’ll have to change the statement, which says the target range is going to be 25 basis points.	96	9

201503	897	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201503	898	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	I’ll start by saying that I’m of the view that it’s very important that we have good control of monetary policy at and immediately after liftoff.	96	9
201503	899	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	To achieve that, I may be in a minority, but I prefer the first option, which is to have an $800 billion cap.	96	9
201503	900	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	It seems very likely—and, I think, today got even likelier—that we’re going to be lifting off into a quarter-end.	96	9
201503	901	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	I suspect the market will know at the time of liftoff that we already prepositioned $300 billion of additional capacity in term over the quarter-end, which really is $1.1 trillion over the quarter-end and then $800 billion in equilibrium.	96	9
201503	902	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	That’s almost four times the highest previous between-quarter-end take-up.	96	9
201503	903	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	That seems like plenty to me.	96	9
201503	904	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	I can’t give any assurances about that, but it does seem like that’s enough.	96	9

201503	906	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	That would be my first choice, although we also have the flexibility to take the cap off after a week or so.	96	9

201503	912	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	For one thing, you want to overwhelm demand with supply here, and to the extent you send a long signal ahead of time, you give a chance for the demand for ON RRPs to go up.	96	9
201503	913	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	So I would wait.	96	9
201503	914	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	In addition, I think there’s real risk in going without a cap for any long period of time.	96	9
201503	915	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	There are really two risks.	96	9
201503	916	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	One is that it’s subject to a lot of criticism from people about being insensitive to the size of our footprint in the markets.	96	9
201503	917	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	And the second is, if you’re going to keep it on for two or three meetings, there really is a chance that some kind of an event would happen—and there are plenty of them that we have talked about—that could cause a real run to the balance sheet.	96	9
201503	918	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	So I would say, if we’re going to do it, I wouldn’t preannounce it, and I would do some sort of pre-commitment to imposing a cap.	96	9

201503	922	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	And I would impose a cap that’s $200 billion-ish over the non-quarter-end amount, and then I would continue doing $300 billion at quarter-end.	96	9

201503	939	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Brainard.	96	9
201503	940	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201503	941	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Establishing monetary policy control should be our paramount objective at liftoff, and our deliberations suggest it is highly likely the decision to lift off will take place at a meeting with a press conference, and, thus, proximate to quarter-end.	96	9
201503	942	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	We have seen previously that demand for overnight RRP tends to rise at quarter-end, raising the risk, in the presence of a binding cap, of a downward drift in rates following the announcement of liftoff.	96	9
201503	943	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Moreover, our experience so far with demand for overnight RRPs has taken place with rates near zero, where the floor has likely received some support from the zero lower bound.	96	9
201503	944	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	So, we don’t really know the level of overnight RRPs that will be necessary to keep the federal funds rate in our target zone at liftoff.	96	9
201503	945	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	For all of these reasons, to minimize the risk that the federal funds rate falls below our target range immediately following liftoff, it would be prudent to operate initially without a cap.	96	9
201503	946	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Furthermore, I don’t see significant cost to the temporary suspension of a cap to balance against that achievement of monetary control.	96	9
201503	947	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	By contrast, I do believe the establishment of a permanent overnight RRP facility would raise important risks of changing the structure of money markets.	96	9
201503	948	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	But these risks will be addressed by being unambiguous from the outset, as we have been to date, that the overnight RRP facility will be available only to the extent, and for the duration, necessary to reestablish effective monetary control.	96	9
201503	949	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	For the same reason, I support planning for the phaseout of the facility.	96	9
201503	950	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	But I would be wary of trying to specify a time frame at the outset, and I also am uneasy about using the language that is proposed for the minutes on reducing the capacity “fairly soon,” so as to avoid starting a debate on what, precisely, that means.	96	9
201503	951	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Once we have gained some knowledge about the demand for overnight RRPs away from near-zero levels of interest, we can more comfortably set a cap that is credible and that has the appropriate headroom.	96	9
201503	952	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	By that point, it will also be clear that we have established monetary control following liftoff, and our credibility in this area will be less subject to doubts so that our risk tolerance can be a little greater.	96	9
201503	953	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	If the demand for the overnight facility remains elevated for a protracted period, relative to the usage patterns that we have seen so far, I would support increasing the IOER rate and, thus, the gap between the IOER and the overnight RRP rates in order to reinforce the pull of the IOER rate.	96	9
201503	954	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Of course, we don’t know precisely how a higher IOER rate will affect the demand for the overnight facility, so we shouldn’t take other policy options off the table.	96	9
201503	955	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Should it prove necessary, I would be open to considering additional liability-side options, including term tools, in addition to raising the IOER rate, to limit the usage of the overnight facility over time.	96	9
201503	956	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Precisely what the mix will be will depend on the circumstances, which argues for addressing this issue only after we have some experience with the new policy framework.	96	9
201503	957	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	By contrast, I do not believe that asset sales should be on the table for this purpose, nor do I expect it will be needed in light of the range of available liability-side tools at our disposal.	96	9
201503	958	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Putting asset sales into play could risk that being taken by markets as a signal regarding the overall stance of monetary policy.	96	9
201503	959	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Deliberations surrounding asset sales should be determined on the basis of our overall monetary policy goals and not as a mechanism to fine-tune usage of the overnight facility.	96	9
201503	960	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Thank you.	96	9
