201503	1190	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Let’s move to our next agenda item, and I am going to call on Steve Kamin to begin.	11	1
201503	1191	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	As we did in January, David and I will be switching positions in the order, in light of the prominent role of international developments in jerking around the US economy.	11	1
201503	1192	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	I’ll be referring to the materials titled “The International Outlook.”	11	1
201503	1193	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	As shown in panel 1 of that exhibit, our projection of total foreign GDP growth— the black solid line—is not much changed from the January Tealbook.	11	1
201503	1194	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	To be sure, the outlook is a little weaker in the next few quarters.	11	1
201503	1195	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	The fall in oil prices looks to be taking a greater toll on Canada’s economy than we initially reckoned, and we now believe Brazil will sink a bit further into its morass before finally emerging.	11	1
201503	1196	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Additionally, data for China and Korea came in weaker than we’d expected.	11	1
201503	1197	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	But we are still looking for total foreign economic growth to rise to 3 percent, roughly its trend pace, by the end of this year, supported by continued monetary accommodation abroad, still-low energy prices, and currency depreciations against the dollar.	11	1
201503	1198	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	The recovery of the euro area, shown in panel 2, is a big part of the firming in aggregate foreign growth.	11	1
201503	1199	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	We’ve nudged up our euro-area forecast since January.	11	1
201503	1200	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Part of this reflects the ECB’s quantitative easing program, which was announced just after we put the January Tealbook to bed, and was more aggressive than we had anticipated at that time.	11	1
201503	1201	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Additionally, both fourth-quarter GDP growth of 1.3 percent and more recent readings on production, sentiment, and consumer spending have exceeded our expectations.	11	1
201503	1202	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Accordingly, if nothing bad happens, the euro area may well be on track to reduce its resource slack and add to global demand over the next several years.	11	1
201503	1203	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Unfortunately, that is a pretty big “if.”	11	1
201503	1204	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Right now, the Greek government is running out of money and is in difficult talks with its European creditors on an infusion of new funds to avoid defaulting on debt payments coming due soon.	11	1
201503	1205	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Even if Greece secures this near-term financing, it still must negotiate a new multiyear assistance and reform package to keep it afloat over the longer term.	11	1
201503	1206	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Failure of these talks could lead to a default on the government’s debt, the loss of ECB support for the Greek banking system, and, potentially, Greece’s exit from the euro area.	11	1
201503	1207	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	With the stakes being so high, we assume the two sides will eventually reach agreement.	11	1
201503	1208	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	During the interim, however, brinkmanship amid very tough negotiations will likely cause periodic flare-ups in financial stress that will weigh on the euro-area economy.	11	1
201503	1209	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	So far, markets other than that of Greece have been remarkably complacent, perhaps because they assume that Europe’s strengthened firewalls, together with the ECB’s new government bond-buying program and European banks’ reduced exposure to Greece, will suppress any spillovers from a Greek exit.	11	1
201503	1210	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	But we expect that complacency to erode as Greece steps closer to the cliff and investors give more thought to some of the catastrophic risks described in an alternative simulation in this month’s Tealbook.	11	1
201503	1211	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Beyond Greece and the outlook for foreign economic growth more generally, a number of global developments are exerting an unusually large influence on the US economy.	11	1
201503	1212	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Our near-term forecast for Brent oil prices, shown in panel 3, moved up about $10 per barrel since the time of the January Tealbook, as sharp declines in rig counts reinforced expectations that oil production would decelerate.	11	1
201503	1213	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Since we put the March Tealbook to bed, spot Brent oil prices have fallen back toward their January lows (not shown) as market participants focused on growing inventories.	11	1
201503	1214	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	All told, these prices remain very low, boosting prospects for economic growth here and abroad and, as shown in panel 4, depressing already low headline inflation rates.	11	1
201503	1215	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	We have inflation moving back up as the pass-through of previous declines in oil prices wane.	11	1
201503	1216	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	In principle, central banks should see through such transitory dips in inflation.	11	1
201503	1217	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	But concerns that falling inflation would destabilize inflation expectations have led several central bank to ease policy in recent months, including the Bank of Japan and the ECB.	11	1
201503	1218	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	The ECB’s decisions, in turn, have prompted a rush of rate cuts—including to below zero—in neighboring countries seeking to avoid appreciation of their currencies.	11	1
201503	1219	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Low prices for oil and other commodities have led the central banks of several commodity exporters, such as Canada and Australia, to provide greater monetary accommodation.	11	1
201503	1220	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Finally, a number of emerging market countries, notably China, loosened policy in response to varying combinations of weak data and falling inflation.	11	1
201503	1221	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Panel 5 provides a crude summary measure of foreign monetary policy actions in recent years.	11	1
201503	1222	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	For 37 countries, any monetary policy action—be it a rate change, change in reserve requirements, or asset purchases—is assigned a plus-one (+1) for a tightening and a minus-one (-1) for a loosening.	11	1
201503	1223	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	These are then aggregated across countries, and the cumulative policy changes are displayed over time.	11	1
201503	1224	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	By this admittedly crude measure, from late 2011 through 2013, foreign monetary conditions became steadily more accommodative, then they leveled off for a spell but, since last summer, have become still easier.	11	1
201503	1225	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Monetary easing abroad exerts a number of influences on the US economy.	11	1
201503	1226	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	First, and perhaps most prominently, it pushes up the dollar, which would tend to contract US exports and production.	11	1
201503	1227	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	As shown in panel 6, the combination of continued relatively robust readings on the US economy, mounting anticipations of Fed liftoff, and actions by foreign central banks have pushed the broad real dollar exchange rate—the black line—up some 4 percent since the time of the January Tealbook.	11	1
201503	1228	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Going forward, we have come to believe that a continuing market focus on prospective divergences in the prospects for monetary policy here and abroad, combined with ongoing anxieties about foreign economies, will push the dollar up further over the rest of this year.	11	1
201503	1229	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Our hope is that by capitulating to the trend of recent months and actually predicting additional appreciation, we will cause the dollar to finally top out and start moving downward.	11	1
201503	1230	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	But, assuming our forecast actually materializes, the broad real dollar, measured over the duration of the forecast period, will average 6¼ percent above its level in the January Tealbook.	11	1
201503	1231	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	This is a historically outsized revision to our projection.	11	1
201503	1232	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Even so, I will agree in advance that, in view of current market dynamics, there is a plausible risk that the dollar may rise considerably higher than we are predicting.	11	1
201503	1233	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	While, as David will discuss, the higher dollar exerts appreciable drag on the US economic outlook, foreign monetary easing has positive spillovers to the United States through two other channels:  It raises demand abroad, thus boosting our exports, and it lowers US bond yields, thus boosting our domestic demand.	11	1
201503	1234	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	To focus a bit more on this latter channel, panel 7 shows that major economy yields have long been well correlated, and the rundown in these yields since the beginning of 2014 is no exception.	11	1
201503	1235	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	A note circulated to the Committee last week reviews some of the reasons for the simultaneous decline.	11	1
201503	1236	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	First, yields here and abroad may be responding to common factors, such as fears of secular stagnation or heightened demand for safe assets in response to recent regulatory initiatives.	11	1
201503	1237	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Second, investors may worry that weakness abroad may directly restrain the US economy, leading to lower growth, inflation, and thus bond yields.	11	1
201503	1238	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Third, anxiety about tail risks abroad—Greek exit or a hard landing in China, as well as anxieties about the global outlook more generally—may be fueling safe-haven demand for US Treasury securities and depressing our term premiums.	11	1
201503	1239	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Finally, and looping back to the beginning of this discussion, lower interest rates abroad may be encouraging investors to switch to higher-yielding US assets, thus depressing our term premiums through portfolio-balance channels.	11	1
201503	1240	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	These explanations for the low level of US yields may all be valid to some extent, but they have different implications for the future path of yields, the dollar, and monetary policy.	11	1
201503	1241	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	If term premiums and yields are low because of portfolio- balance spillovers from accommodative foreign monetary policies, those effects are likely to depress US yields for several years; all else being equal, unless a further rise in the dollar fully offsets the stimulus from these lower yields, the Fed’s policy rate may have to rise faster to achieve the desired tightening of US financial conditions.	11	1
201503	1242	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Conversely, if low yields reflect worries about the foreign outlook and those worries turn out to be well founded, Federal Reserve policy may need to be looser in response.	11	1
201503	1243	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Finally, a more complicated and ambiguous case is posed if our relatively benign baseline forecast for the global economy materializes and risk events pass quietly:  Longer-term yields in the United States and elsewhere may rise quickly as risk premiums unwind, which would call for easier Federal Reserve policy, but sentiment might improve and the dollar could fall, which would call for tighter policy.	11	1
201503	1244	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	In light of our uncertainties regarding the relative strength of the factors pushing down US yields at present, we will be watching global financial markets very carefully for clues about future developments.	11	1
201503	1245	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	David will now continue our presentation.	11	1
201503	1246	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	I’ll be referring to the exhibit creatively titled “Material for the US Outlook.”	11	1
201503	1247	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	At long last, I’m finally going to take a leaf out of all of your books and declare that our forecast hasn’t changed all that much since either January or December.	11	1
201503	1248	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	Part of the reason I’m going to say that is that, as I’ll show, it happens to be more or less partly true.	11	1
201503	1249	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	The small revisions that we’ve made to the domestic outlook lately mostly reflect the surprising extent of the appreciation of the dollar and the plunge in oil prices.	11	1
201503	1250	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	The stronger dollar causes us to trim a little out of our forecast for the growth of real GDP over the next few years, while the steeper net drop in oil prices than we’d expected as of the December meeting put a bigger dent in near-term topline PCE inflation; that said, core PCE inflation has been running below forecast, too.	11	1
201503	1251	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	While we haven’t yet seen fit to alter our baseline forecast for the longer-term trajectory of inflation, we are keeping a close eye on a few shreds of evidence suggesting that longer-term inflation expectations may have crept down some in recent years.	11	1
201503	1252	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	Turning to the specifics:  The labor market seems to have been on a stronger course than we anticipated in January.	11	1
201503	1253	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	Average monthly job gains as measured in the establishment survey have been running about 50,000 per month stronger than we had expected.	11	1
201503	1254	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	Although the unemployment rate in February was one-tenth higher than we projected, the employment-to-population ratio—which we think is giving a better fix on labor market slack at present—came in a few basis points higher than we had forecast as a result of slightly better-than-expected labor force participation.	11	1
201503	1255	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	On the other hand, the news outside the labor market has not been as favorable.	11	1
201503	1256	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	For one, the recent indicators of GDP have been disappointing on the whole.	11	1
201503	1257	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	A good chunk of the shortfall relative to expectations has been in net exports.	11	1
201503	1258	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	But given the appreciation of the dollar, we are more cautious than we normally would be about writing that development off as transitory.	11	1
201503	1259	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	The most recent news about consumer spending has been mixed, with the QSS pointing to another bump up in medical care spending in the fourth quarter.	11	1
201503	1260	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	But the weak path of retail sales now estimated for the past three months is a little puzzling, at best.	11	1
201503	1261	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	Moreover, yesterday’s industrial production release was pretty drab, with manufacturing production estimated to have posted another small decline in February, and the figures for December and January were revised down.	11	1
201503	1262	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	All told, manufacturing IP now looks to be on track for zero growth in the first quarter.	11	1
201503	1263	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	This morning’s data on housing starts and permits were pretty bleak on their face, with single-family starts and permits both posting large declines in February—considerably underperforming relative to our expectations that they would roughly tread water in the near term.	11	1
201503	1264	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	Adverse weather is the easy explanation, and, indeed, it probably helps to explain some of the recent weakness in a range of these indicators, but we had been watching our weather metrics carefully and had not anticipated very substantial effects.	11	1
201503	1265	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	As shown by the black dot in panel 2, we now estimate real GDP growth in the first quarter of 1¼ percent, and that was prior to the news on housing starts and permits.	11	1
201503	1266	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	Folding in that news from the housing market, we’d take another tenth or so out of that estimate, and similarly for the second quarter.	11	1
201503	1267	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	To be sure, the confidence interval around our estimate, even for the quarter just concluding, is astonishingly wide, but I would hasten to point out that the risk is two-sided.	11	1
201503	1268	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	Altogether, the labor market looks to have been at least as strong as we had anticipated, and perhaps a little stronger, while the near-term GDP picture has been disappointing.	11	1
201503	1269	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	In the Tealbook, we reconciled these two developments by marking down structural productivity in history by enough to leave our estimate of the output gap roughly unrevised in the current quarter.	11	1
201503	1270	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	Panel 3 gives you a broader perspective on the issue of slack by providing updated estimates of three different measures of resource utilization gaps that we follow.	11	1
201503	1271	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	The dotted blue line shows the judgmental estimate that is reflected in the Tealbook baseline.	11	1
201503	1272	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	The red line shows the production function version of the output gap as estimated in EDO, one of the DSGE models that we maintain at the Board.	11	1
201503	1273	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	Finally, the black line—labeled FRB/US—plots an estimate of slack that combines the information from a variety of production, income, labor market, and price indicators, while explicitly allowing for measurement error.	11	1
201503	1274	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	The Tealbook and EDO models’ point estimates suggest that resource utilization has nearly recovered to its sustainable position, while the FRB/US measure suggests that it’s already there.	11	1
201503	1275	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	Reverting to panel 1, you may be a little puzzled to see the unemployment rate revised up by such a slight amount, in view of our more-guarded outlook for the path of real output.	11	1
201503	1276	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	The reason for the small revision to the unemployment rate is that we extrapolated forward the slower pace of structural productivity growth to the tune of 0.1 percentage point per year.	11	1
201503	1277	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	At the margin, this revised assumption will allow a given amount of real GDP growth to generate a slightly greater amount of labor market improvement and thus is designed to better center the baseline forecast in light of the persistent misses on the unemployment rate that we’ve had during the past couple of years.	11	1
201503	1278	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	If we had left our supply-side assumptions unchanged in this projection, the unemployment rate would have revised up another 0.2 percentage point or so over the medium term.	11	1
201503	1279	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	I should also briefly mention our deliberations over two other assumptions that we use to calibrate the longer-term forecast.	11	1
201503	1280	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	First, we revised down our estimate of the long-term equilibrium funds rate by ¼ percentage point.	11	1
201503	1281	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	As was reflected in the discussion we provided in the Tealbook, the confidence intervals surrounding this parameter are a mile wide, but we view the lower rate as better balancing the risks in light of our judgment that probably not all of the extraordinarily low level of long- term rates around the globe reflects low term premiums, and that lower equilibrium interest rates may have been playing a larger role in driving the downtrend in recent years than we previously thought.	11	1
201503	1282	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	We also debated whether to lower our estimate of the natural rate of unemployment from its current level of 5¼ percent, which is the same level that we think prevailed just prior to the Great Recession.	11	1
201503	1283	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	At least two factors militated toward making such a downward revision.	11	1
201503	1284	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	First, younger workers tend to have higher unemployment rates, and since the eve of the financial crisis and recession, the share of these workers in the labor force has declined.	11	1
201503	1285	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	Second, workers at the margin of moving onto disability rolls also tend to have higher unemployment rates, and the number of individuals reporting themselves as out of the labor force because of a disability has increased significantly since 2007.	11	1
201503	1286	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	However, moving to assume that the natural rate is lower now than we think it was before the recession felt distinctly uncomfortable, especially in view of the historically large increase in permanent job losers, the fact that the long-term unemployed still make up an unusually large share of overall unemployment, and the suggestive evidence that matching in the labor market may still not be as efficient as it was before the crisis.	11	1
201503	1287	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	Furthermore, in light of how flat we think the Phillips curve is, wage and price inflation are doomed not to be very informative in this regard.	11	1
201503	1288	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	Finally, we think we’ve probably had some tendency in the past to adjust our estimate of the natural rate to hew too closely to movements in the actual rate of unemployment.	11	1
201503	1289	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	In the end, after many hours of debate, we left our assumption unchanged at 5.2 percent, though with no pretense of having settled the issue.	11	1
201503	1290	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	Panels 4 and 5 summarize the inflation outlook.	11	1
201503	1291	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	As shown in panel 4, the recent upturn in crude oil prices that Steve discussed led us to temper the decline in headline PCE inflation that we are projecting for the current quarter, relative to our January projection.	11	1
201503	1292	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	However, as you can see from panel 5, core PCE inflation has come in softer than we expected in January.	11	1
201503	1293	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	Most of this miss was attributable to lower-than- expected medical services and core goods prices; because we don’t expect medical services prices to continue to surprise to the downside and we continue to expect that goods price inflation will pick up as import prices accelerate, we did not carry forward the downward surprise to core inflation beyond the near term.	11	1
201503	1294	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	Over the remainder of the medium term, the inflation forecast is essentially the same as in recent Tealbooks, featuring a slow upward creep back toward your 2 percent objective.	11	1
201503	1295	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	The staff’s medium-term inflation forecast is predicated on the assumption that longer-term inflation expectations are well anchored—an assumption that we have maintained in the latest projection.	11	1
201503	1296	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	Given the central role of inflation expectations in our analytical framework, we have been keeping our eyes peeled for evidence that those expectations might be starting to come unmoored, either on the upside or on the downside.	11	1
201503	1297	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	Panel 6 presents some data from the Survey of Professional Forecasters that we found a little disquieting in that regard.	11	1
201503	1298	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	The black line shows the SPF’s median 10-year average expected inflation rate for headline PCE price inflation.	11	1
201503	1299	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	This measure, like the Michigan survey’s long-term expected inflation measure, has remained pretty flat in recent years.	11	1
201503	1300	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	However, as shown by the red line, the SPF long-term CPI projection has moved down more noticeably in recent years and most recently has dipped to 2.1 percent, its lowest level ever.	11	1
201503	1301	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	Thus far, we are not inclined to view this development as persuasive evidence that longer-term inflation expectations are starting to deteriorate.	11	1
201503	1302	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	First, the most recent decline appears to reflect the change in the composition of the survey panel; holding the panel’s composition constant, the first-quarter median response for the CPI forecast would have remained at 2.2 percent.	11	1
201503	1303	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	Second, a measure that focuses on CPI expectations 6 to 10 years ahead has declined less over the past few years; we would expect that respondents’ projections over this horizon would probably give us a better read on what they view as inflation’s longer-term anchor.	11	1
201503	1304	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	Third, this discussion is putting a fine point on small changes in the expectations of professional forecasters, who are not, after all, the people setting wages and prices throughout the economy.	11	1
201503	1305	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	But, by the same token, we are wary of taking too much comfort from the stability in the PCE responses because it could be that the professional forecasters are reluctant to be seen as betting quite so overtly against your 2 percent objective.	11	1
201503	1306	2015-03-18	meeting	WILCOX	All told, we will certainly be keeping a close eye on these and other measures of inflation expectations going forward.	11	1

201503	1431	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Frankly, that’s the best basis we can come up with because that futures curve represents market participants’ best guess as to what will be those prevailing prices.	12	1
201503	1432	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	That was the approach that we basically used for decades.	12	1
201503	1433	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	And moving into 2008 when oil prices were experiencing tremendous fluctuations, there was a lot of concern on the part of the Committee that our forecasts weren’t very helpful in predicting the future.	12	1
201503	1434	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Our division did a full-court press to look at the forecast and ask how we could improve it.	12	1
201503	1435	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	In the event, we decided that we couldn’t improve it by very much.	12	1
201503	1436	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	One thing we could do was take a look at market participants’ outlook for the global economy, compare it with our own, and if there were any differences, we could adjust the futures curve for oil prices to take that into account.	12	1
201503	1437	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	We regularly do that, but the effect on our forecast path is not great.	12	1
201503	1438	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Right now, we alter the path to raise it by 0.5 percent per year, which is very little if you take into account the fact that we may be predicting a little bit more exchange rate appreciation than the market, to take into account some differences between our appraisal of the global economic outlook and the markets’.	12	1
201503	1439	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Basically, we’re stuck with the futures curve, and the upward slope is predicated on a couple of very reasonable premises.	12	1
201503	1440	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	One of them is that, over time, the low oil prices will reduce the incentive for production and production should decelerate.	12	1
201503	1441	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	And we’re certainly already seeing evidence of that in declining rig counts and in declining investment in the energy sector.	12	1
201503	1442	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Directionally, that’s a very reasonable premise, and that should give you, eventually, some upward tilt to prices.	12	1
201503	1443	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Another premise that seems to underlie the upward curve is that, over time, the global economy should strengthen, and that, too, should lead to some increase in prices.	12	1
201503	1444	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Again, the direction seems reasonable.	12	1
201503	1445	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	What’s happened since January has been, first, the evidence of declining rig counts seemed so tangible that markets decided they were sure that, indeed, production was going to slow, and so oil prices rose and the whole futures curve rose.	12	1
201503	1446	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Then more recently, as markets took note of soaring inventory levels, and as concerns emerged that these inventories might actually exceed the storage capacity available to put aside this oil, thus basically leading in a figurative sense an overflow of oil onto the market, those oil prices have come back down.	12	1
201503	1447	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Those are reasonable explanations, and that leaves us, again, with our upward tilt for oil prices, but do we have a lot of conviction that for sure that’s going to transpire?	12	1
201503	1448	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	No.	12	1
201503	1449	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	There have been a lot of analyses of how low oil prices could go, analyses looking at different fields in terms of what are the operating costs for those fields.	12	1
201503	1450	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	Those analyses suggest that oil prices could go down to $40 per barrel before you see shutdowns significant enough to bring oil prices back up.	12	1
201503	1451	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	We do have a lot of uncertainty.	12	1
201503	1452	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	It seems perfectly reasonable that, over the longer term, the oil prices should start trending upward.	12	1
201503	1453	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	There is tremendous uncertainty.	12	1
201503	1454	2015-03-18	meeting	POTTER	I think that’s the crucial part.	12	1

201503	1508	2015-03-18	meeting	KAMIN	In terms of the big picture, there have been two much larger long swings in the dollar since we floated in the 1970s—one of them in the early-to-mid 1980s, and then more recently in the late 1990s, peaking in 2002 and coming down.	12	1

201503	1596	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	Our directors expressed doubt about our muted-growth story.	13	1
201503	1597	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	One reason for the upbeat tone is improving margins.	13	1
201503	1598	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	Firms indicate that they are treating the drop in commodity prices, including energy costs, as an opportunity to boost margins at least temporarily.	13	1
201503	1599	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	Any pass-through to their customers is expected to occur only gradually over the year and in response to competitive pressures.	13	1
201503	1600	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	We were somewhat surprised by comments of our directors and contacts running businesses of national scope regarding February weather.	13	1
201503	1601	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	A number of contacts said work disruptions this year have been as bad as or worse than last year.	13	1
201503	1602	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	In these reports, the weather effects on economic activity were not limited to the Northeast.	13	1
201503	1603	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	In the retail sector, while most firms have not yet seen the benefit of lower gasoline prices in consumer spending, one low-end retailer in the dollar segment did report a sales boost.	13	1

201503	1612	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	Turning to the national economy and my take on the incoming data, I’ve marked down once again my near-term economic growth, unemployment, and inflation forecasts, based on the tone of the data, but I’ve left the basic narrative of my forecast unchanged.	13	1
201503	1613	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	I have real GDP growth about a half of a percentage point above the Tealbook projection over the next three years.	13	1
201503	1614	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	Otherwise my outlook looks much the same as that of the Tealbook.	13	1
201503	1615	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	I have not yet fully bought into the downshift reflected in this meeting’s Tealbook outlook.	13	1
201503	1616	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	In internal discussions in our Bank over the past two years, my staff and I have employed a simplifying device to describe the path of the economy.	13	1
201503	1617	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	We have argued that the economy is in a 3 percent world, or a 2 percent world that prevailed from the start of the recovery to mid-2013.	13	1
201503	1618	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	That’s been the basis of our economic narrative.	13	1
201503	1619	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	The staff preparing the Tealbook seems to have concluded the economy is back in that 2 percent world for the forecast horizon.	13	1
201503	1620	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	The Tealbook forecast is now underpinned by slightly lower longer-term growth potential that is, in turn, reflective of lower productivity growth.	13	1
201503	1621	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	The staff seems to expect a fundamentally slower economy over the medium term.	13	1
201503	1622	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	As I said, I’m not there yet.	13	1
201503	1623	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	However, I have changed my assessment of the forecast risk and now have the risks to economic growth and inflation tilted to the downside.	13	1
201503	1624	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	I find the disharmonious character of the current economic growth and inflation data versus the payroll employment trend to be concerning.	13	1
201503	1625	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	I’m continuing to put a lot of faith in the transitory factors explanation for readings on economic growth and inflation.	13	1
201503	1626	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	With a potentially historic policy decision pending, this is a particularly tough time to read the underlying trends, and I’ll put this thought in more tactical terms in the policy round.	13	1

201503	1639	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	In sum, the effect on the first quarter from these factors may be somewhat higher than anticipated in the Tealbook.	13	1
201503	1640	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	Looking beyond the first quarter, I had been expecting real GDP growth to be well above potential this year.	13	1
201503	1641	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	With the dollar continuing to appreciate and weigh on net exports, I am now anticipating growth only modestly above its potential rate, slowing the decline in the unemployment rate.	13	1
201503	1642	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	I expect the slowdown to be reinforced by more workers returning to the labor force.	13	1
201503	1643	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	Consequently, our forecast envisions a more gradual approach toward my current estimate of the natural rate of unemployment at 5 percent.	13	1
201503	1644	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	In light of the lack of wage pressure to date, I could easily believe that the natural rate of unemployment is below 5 percent, and I will revisit this estimate if we continue to see very modest wage and salary increases as labor markets, I hope, continue to improve.	13	1
201503	1645	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	On the inflation front, most private forecasters and many of our own SEP submissions have been anticipating a gradual return to 2 percent inflation.	13	1
201503	1646	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	In fact, forecasters have repeatedly assumed that we would be close to 2 percent PCE inflation within two years, an expectation that has consistently been foiled by the data.	13	1
201503	1647	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	But, undeterred, most forecasters have simply moved the assumption forward for another try with the next forecast round.	13	1
201503	1648	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	This pattern of recurring forecast errors makes me less confident that models that rely on the strong assumption that well- anchored expectations will drive inflation to 2 percent are capturing current inflation dynamics.	13	1
201503	1649	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	These serially correlated errors should make us less confident of the models and cause us to place more weight on the incoming wage and price data and less weight on models, especially when the incoming data do not conform to the forecast generated by our models.	13	1
201503	1650	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	As has been the case for some years, the most recent inflation data do not indicate that we are likely to quickly return to our inflation target.	13	1
201503	1651	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	At our December meeting, the range for core PCE inflation forecasts for the 2015 SEP submissions was 1½ to 2.2 percent.	13	1
201503	1652	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	However, the incoming price data indicate that even the lowest forecast in the range for December will likely be too high.	13	1
201503	1653	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	The Tealbook has lowered its forecast for 2015 Q4-to-Q4 core PCE inflation from 1½ percent to 1.3 percent, and I have lowered mine to 1.2 percent.	13	1
201503	1654	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	While some may dismiss recent low-inflation readings as largely reflecting the indirect effects of lower oil prices seeping into core inflation, my staff’s work on oil’s effect on core prices finds this effect to be, similar to the Tealbook, quite small.	13	1
201503	1655	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	Similarly, my staff finds only a small effect for the indirect effect of non-oil import prices.	13	1
201503	1656	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	In addition, market indicators of expected inflation outcomes should make us less confident that we are returning to 2 percent inflation over the next two years.	13	1
201503	1657	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	Breakeven inflation rates remain quite low, and inflation probabilities derived from inflation caps and floors have recently implied a substantial increase in the probability that inflation remains below 1½ percent over the next 10 years.	13	1
201503	1658	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	I do not expect that by June we will have enough data to make us reasonably confident that we are returning to our inflation target over the next two years.	13	1
201503	1659	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	As a result, the appropriate policy assumption in the Federal Reserve Bank of Boston’s SEP submission entails liftoff in September, and I remain uncertain about how much evidence of increasing inflation will be available even by then.	13	1
201503	1660	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	In addition, even with a liftoff delayed until September, I expect only a gradual increase in interest rates.	13	1
201503	1661	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	In part, this reflects my expectation that progress on inflation will likely be slow.	13	1

201503	1663	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	This, in turn, reflects the continued disappointing productivity numbers that, in part, account for the significant labor market tightening despite only lackluster real GDP growth by historical standards.	13	1
201503	1664	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	Finally, among the risks that concern me are the continued weakness in China and the possibility of more Greek tragedy that stresses the European economy, each of which could cause a negative surprise that policy at the zero lower bound is poorly situated to address.	13	1
201503	1665	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	As we get to the middle of the year, we may have a better sense of the likelihood that these risks materialize, and pose a greater potential drag on the US economy.	13	1

201503	1762	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	Other measures, including the Federal Reserve Bank of Cleveland’s 10-year expected inflation rate, have moved down a bit, but they remain within recent ranges.	13	1
201503	1763	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	While little of the variation in longer-term inflation expectations can be explained by typical movements in energy prices, research by the Federal Reserve Bank of Cleveland staff indicates that the sharp drop in energy prices can account entirely for the recent decline in the Cleveland staff’s expected inflation measures.	13	1
201503	1764	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	Even though the firming in inflation compensation measures could be viewed as a good sign, I continue to take less signal about expectations from these measures.	13	1
201503	1765	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	Those recent changes may be reflecting changes in liquidity premiums.	13	1
201503	1766	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	As oil prices stabilize, with economic growth above trend and inflation expectations stable, I project that inflation will gradually return to our 2 percent goal by late 2016 or early 2017.	13	1
201503	1767	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	The stability of the survey measures of longer-run inflation helps inform my projection.	13	1
201503	1768	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	Research suggests that these measures are more useful for forecasting inflation than market- based measures.	13	1
201503	1769	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	Within the Cleveland staff’s forecasting model, anchoring inflation around a survey forecast of longer-run inflation performs much better in terms of historical forecast accuracy than anchoring it around measures of expected inflation based, in part or in whole, on financial market measures, including the Cleveland staff’s 10-year expected inflation.	13	1
201503	1770	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	Thus, I am reasonably confident that inflation will gradually return to the FOMC’s goal by the end of 2016 or early 2017.	13	1
201503	1771	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	Of course, it is good to remember that it is very difficult to forecast inflation with any precision.	13	1
201503	1772	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	Reasonable confidence should not require high confidence.	13	1
201503	1773	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	As indicated in the table provided with the request for SEP submissions, historical average projection errors across a range of private-sector and government forecasts indicate that the 70 percent confidence interval around a forecast of CPI inflation two years out is about plus or minus 1 percentage point.	13	1
201503	1774	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	The Cleveland staff’s analysis of a range of forecasting models indicates that current uncertainty around headline inflation forecasts is somewhere between “normal” and “somewhat elevated” compared with the norms of the past 20 years.	13	1
201503	1775	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	There is no reason to think we will be more accurate in forecasting inflation this time, nor should we require that.	13	1
201503	1776	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	My projection is dependent on a policy rate path that has liftoff occurring in June with a gradual rise in rates thereafter, similar to a path suggested by a Taylor (1999) rule with inertia.	13	1
201503	1777	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	Liftoff is one quarter later than in my December projection, reflecting the fact that inflation between one and two years ahead now reaches 2 percent one quarter later.	13	1
201503	1778	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	I am hoping that we will change our policy statement tomorrow so that my projected liftoff date is not inconsistent with our forward guidance.	13	1

201503	1928	2015-03-18	meeting	PRICHARD	For example, the current general activity index in our Manufacturing Business Outlook Survey has dropped from its lofty late-fall levels to readings that are below its nonrecessionary average.	13	1

201503	1933	2015-03-18	meeting	PRICHARD	A somewhat brighter note is seen in the index for future employment, which remains well above its nonrecessionary average, a range in which it has resided now for the past two years.	13	1
201503	1934	2015-03-18	meeting	PRICHARD	The other sector of weakness in our region is residential investment.	13	1

201503	1940	2015-03-18	meeting	PRICHARD	Strength was broad based in the survey, with strong performance in indexes for current sales, new orders, current employment, and future activity.	13	1
201503	1941	2015-03-18	meeting	PRICHARD	Employment growth remains strong as well, and the unemployment rate for the District as a whole is slightly lower than that of the nation.	13	1
201503	1942	2015-03-18	meeting	PRICHARD	Thus, our District reflects fairly well what is transpiring nationally:  strong labor markets, relatively solid consumption growth, a falloff in manufacturing business activity, and a lack of any significant improvement in residential investment.	13	1

201503	1944	2015-03-18	meeting	PRICHARD	I foresee 2.6 percent real GDP growth in the first half of this year and strengthening to 3 percent overall in the second half, implying GDP growth of 2.8 percent for the year as a whole.	13	1

201503	1988	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Why are wage pressures so constrained?	13	1

201503	2067	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Finally, I would like to raise an issue that I think warrants greater attention:  the very low level of bond term premiums.	13	1

201503	2069	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Consider two very different narratives.	13	1

201503	2071	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	In that case, “all else being equal” would imply the need for a more rapid tightening of the US monetary policy.	13	1

201503	2074	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	In the “stay low” scenario, that has implications for pension funds and financial intermediaries like insurance companies that offer products with minimum guaranteed returns.	13	1

201503	2076	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Conversely, in the “snapback” scenario, the financial-stability risk would arise if bond yields moved up abruptly.	13	1
201503	2077	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I think this is a wild card in the economic outlook that we are going to have to think about as we go forward over the next few months.	13	1

201503	2082	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	We face two significant puzzles in understanding the current macroeconomic situation.	13	1
201503	2083	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	The first is that labor market conditions have been improving impressively.	13	1

201503	2089	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	It could be a GDP data problem, one that would lessen as successive GDP data estimates are presented, but I suspect that even the final data will continue to show that productivity growth has fallen dramatically.	13	1
201503	2090	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	This could reflect the mix of economic growth, with employment gains being more weighted than usual to low-tech and low-productivity service jobs.	13	1
201503	2091	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	Whatever the source, we should bear in mind the Herbert Stein wisdom that the difference between a growth rate of 1 percent and a growth rate of 2 percent is 100 percent.	13	1
201503	2092	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	This means that the productivity slowdown is a major long-term problem for the United States, but in terms of our target variables, it’s not directly relevant to our immediate policy concerns, which relate to inflation and unemployment.	13	1
201503	2093	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	In the Tealbook, the staff has responded to the latest discrepancy between spending and labor market data by lowering their estimate of structural productivity growth.	13	1
201503	2094	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	The staff’s view is that when there appears to be inconsistency between national income and labor market data, the labor market data are generally more reliable.	13	1
201503	2095	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	However, part of the problem may be, as has often been said around the table, that we need to look beyond U-3 to understand labor market developments, perhaps even more than the staff does in the Tealbook.	13	1
201503	2096	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	U-3 was almost certainly not a complete measure of slack in earlier stages of the recovery, but several anomalies are gradually being worked out, be it the long-term unemployment rate or the percentage of those working part time for economic reasons.	13	1
201503	2097	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	Further, the quits rate has jumped over the past six months.	13	1
201503	2098	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	The currently low participation rate is the most important aspect of the employment picture that could give us an extra margin of employment as the economy moves ahead, but the bulk of the decline from a 67 percent to a 62 percent participation rate is explained by demographic factors.	13	1
201503	2099	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	Another possibility is that the natural rate of unemployment has been declining to a number that begins with 4, so that the reduction in the unemployment rate has not been as great a reduction in slack as we’ve thought hitherto.	13	1
201503	2100	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	In this case, the unemployment rate will continue to decline if we continue to grow reasonably, but it’s unlikely that it will continue for long to decline at the rate it has over the past two years.	13	1
201503	2101	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	That means that we’re getting closer to full resource utilization.	13	1
201503	2102	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	On the inflation front, we can be reasonably confident that we’ll see an increase in inflation before too long.	13	1
201503	2103	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	Of course, the headline inflation figures will be aided by a turnaround in oil prices, or at least by a decline in the rate at which oil prices might continue falling.	13	1
201503	2104	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	The effect of the appreciation of the dollar on domestic prices will stop after the dollar stops appreciating, but that date is harder to forecast because of the well-known overshooting phenomenon.	13	1
201503	2105	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	Nonetheless, the staff’s projection that core import prices will resume increasing late this year is plausible.	13	1
201503	2106	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	The staff’s forecast that core inflation will reach 1.6 percent in 2016 means that we may be close to our target inflation rate by the end of next year.	13	1
201503	2107	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	The fan charts on page 74 of Tealbook, Book A, suggest that the probability of core inflation being at 2 percent or more by the end of 2016 is somewhere around 35 to 40 percent.	13	1
201503	2108	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	I have two more topics before concluding.	13	1
201503	2109	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	First, why are real wages not rising as we approach the natural rate of unemployment?	13	1
201503	2110	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	Well, they might be, as the box on page 24 of Tealbook, Book A, and evidence from outside the Fed suggests.	13	1
201503	2111	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	And some of the reports we’ve heard today also suggest that.	13	1
201503	2112	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	In addition, real wages may be rising only slowly because productivity growth has been low, or, as mentioned a second ago, the natural rate might be lower than we recognize.	13	1
201503	2113	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	Second, what about the headwinds?	13	1
201503	2114	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	Some of the headwinds may be turning into tailwinds.	13	1
201503	2115	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	Most important of those is that there is far less pessimism and even some optimism about European economic growth than there was only a few months ago, and similarly for Japanese growth.	13	1
201503	2116	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	There are also the promising fragments of information we’ve received during the briefings from the presidents of the Reserve Banks, including that on household formation, which is very interesting.	13	1
201503	2117	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	But some headwinds remain.	13	1
201503	2118	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	The most important among them is the appreciation of the dollar, the slowdown in Chinese economic growth, and the possibility of a Greek exit from the euro area.	13	1
201503	2119	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	I am reasonably confident that inflation will continue moving back to its 2 percent objective over the medium term, and that the unemployment rate is getting closer to the natural rate, but more on that and the other factors relevant to our policy decisions tomorrow.	13	1
201503	2120	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1

201503	2122	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Tarullo.	13	1
201503	2123	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201503	2124	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Up until quite recently, I thought I was going to devote the bulk of my remarks today to various labor market issues—downward nominal wage rigidity, the shape of the Phillips curve, and the like.	13	1
201503	2125	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	There’ll probably be plenty of time to return to those issues in April.	13	1
201503	2126	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	So instead I wanted to comment, like President Dudley, on some reasons, perhaps, for a bit of caution right now.	13	1
201503	2127	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Over the course of the past couple of weeks, I’ve been struck by two things:  one, the degree to which actual as well as likely international developments are increasing downside risks; and, two, the little burst of domestic data suggesting that there may be some pause in what heretofore has been a basically improving economic situation.	13	1
201503	2128	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Beginning with the external risks, which we have been discussing regularly in recent meetings, I believe we’ve seen basically unchanged risk associated with the extent of China’s growth slowdown and with geopolitical tensions on a number of Russia’s borders.	13	1
201503	2129	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	I don’t think those have changed very much one way or the other in the intermeeting period.	13	1
201503	2130	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	I do think—as several of you, most recently Stan, have noted—that chances of a Greek exit from the euro zone have been rising even since the four-month extension.	13	1
201503	2131	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	The seeming inability of the Greek government to navigate between domestic and international expectations has brought discussions almost to a standstill.	13	1
201503	2132	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	And there have been more than a few hints that at least some other euro- zone countries believe a Greek exit would actually be beneficial for the euro zone over the medium term by removing it as a distraction and allowing them to attend to ongoing structural issues and relationships.	13	1
201503	2133	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	As Steve Kamin noted in his briefing, there is still a fairly widespread view that a Greek exit would be manageable and would not have contagion consequences in peripheral, much less all of, Europe.	13	1
201503	2134	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	But I think I’ll have to acknowledge that that may not be the case.	13	1
201503	2135	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	In fact, if it turns out that there are consequences, the fact that everybody has been assuming there are no consequences might make the reaction even stronger because people have not been hedging against that eventuality.	13	1
201503	2136	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	An additional international issue—which is, I think, beginning to loom a bit larger—is the situation in Brazil.	13	1
201503	2137	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	To date, Brazil’s problems have been associated with commodity price declines, the rise in the dollar, and domestic political turmoil.	13	1
201503	2138	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	All of those carry at least some risk of spilling over into the international financial sector if, as appears at least possible, large Brazilian companies have difficulty servicing their external debts—in particular, obviously, dollar-denominated external debts.	13	1
201503	2139	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Brazil is not a small emerging market, so if tensions and problems do begin to rise there, we may see some spillover in other parts of Latin America.	13	1
201503	2140	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Speaking of a strong dollar, we now, as Vice Chairman Dudley has just noted, may be seeing its having shifted from a downside risk to a reality of a drag on economic growth.	13	1
201503	2141	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	The disappointing numbers on industrial production and manufacturing probably reflect that most directly.	13	1
201503	2142	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	I think it’s important to note that the significance of the strengthening of the dollar does depend substantially on the reasons why that strengthening is taking place and the background economic context for the strengthening.	13	1
201503	2143	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	When in the 1990s the dollar was strengthening, it was against the backdrop of really quite strong US growth—including productivity growth, GDP growth, and employment growth—and it was almost as if dollar assets were sucking in investment funds from all over the world.	13	1
201503	2144	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	People wanted to be in the US stock market.	13	1
201503	2145	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	They wanted to be making foreign direct investments in the United States.	13	1
201503	2146	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Today the strength of the dollar is arising largely from, you might say, relative US strength, but it’s basically due to QE in Europe and in Japan and other manifestations of what is really weakness internationally.	13	1
201503	2147	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Under these circumstances, the implications of a stronger dollar are not so favorable at all.	13	1
201503	2148	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	I think that there are at least three reasons to expect that the dollar strengthening may continue, and that it may continue to a greater extent than is incorporated into the Tealbook forecast.	13	1
201503	2149	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	First, it’s not uncommon for sharp changes in exchange rates to continue well beyond what even reassessed fundamentals would have suggested.	13	1
201503	2150	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	There are momentum trades in which people just get caught up in the direction of bets, and they sometimes overshoot.	13	1
201503	2151	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Second, as I was alluding to with Brazil, under conditions of the dollar strengthening, those abroad who hold dollar-denominated debts sometimes find it more difficult to roll those debts over.	13	1
201503	2152	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Thus, they’re required to go out and get dollars by selling domestic resources, which, of course, strengthens the dollar.	13	1
201503	2153	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Third—and this goes back to China—as my little colloquy with Steve Kamin during the staff briefing suggested, I think it’s quite likely that China is going to change its exchange rate policies in reaction to a sustained dollar appreciation, and that they will change the band so the renminbi continues to appreciate on a global trade-weighted basis but will depreciate against the dollar.	13	1
201503	2154	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	That, I believe, is going to actually be a stronger response to the degree that the dollar itself continues to appreciate.	13	1
201503	2155	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	For all of those reasons, I think it’s more than a small possibility that dollar strengthening continues beyond what’s projected in the Tealbook.	13	1
201503	2156	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	So that’s the international side, and I count the dollar as mostly an externally driven phenomenon for these purposes.	13	1
201503	2157	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Unlike the past couple of months, when the dollar’s strength seemed to be the only significant warning sign for the domestic economy, a recent string of data at least gives some grounds for pause about how we’re doing domestically as well.	13	1
201503	2158	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	And I would say that, since that very strong jobs report earlier in the month, just about every number has been disappointing.	13	1
201503	2159	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	David Wilcox, I believe, mentioned the retail sales numbers, which probably ought to apply a discount factor based on weather, although, as President Bullard said, almost nobody thinks the weather nationally was quite as bad as it was last year.	13	1
201503	2160	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Regarding household spending expectations—now, this is survey based, to be sure, and so it’s probably deserving to be discounted—it’s worth noting that they have fallen to their lowest levels of the past couple of years.	13	1
201503	2161	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Housing starts and permits were disappointing, as reported this morning.	13	1
201503	2162	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Business fixed investment is still sluggish, although here it may be that the decline in energy-related investment may be masking some overall improvement.	13	1
201503	2163	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Finally, I noted that the shipments diffusion index for nondefense capital goods is down close to its lowest level since the crisis.	13	1
201503	2164	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Now, this is a pretty volatile series, but it is an interesting window, again, into the expectations of business as to economic growth over the next couple of years.	13	1
201503	2165	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Taken alone and maybe even taken together, each of these pieces of data may turn out to be more noise than trend.	13	1
201503	2166	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	But, against the backdrop of global disinflation and the various downside global risks, it’s at least possible that the decent, though still unspectacular, momentum of the past year may have slowed some.	13	1
201503	2167	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	I think that’s probably something that’s going to be of more consequence to us over the next couple of meetings if, as I assume, we’re going to remove “patient” from the statement beginning tomorrow.	13	1

201503	2173	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	The dollar has increased well beyond expectations, with net exports now forecast to subtract 1 full percentage point from this year’s GDP, and there’s a risk that, as we move or seem to move toward liftoff, the dollar will continue to strengthen.	13	1

201503	2190	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	My GDP forecast is very much in line with the Tealbook, but I think there’s a reasonable likelihood that unemployment will decline more than the Tealbook forecast, given the GDP and payroll forecasts.	13	1

201503	2194	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	I’m reasonably confident that we will see an increase in inflation later this year, but I would emphasize that it’s actually, to me, very notable how much uncertainty there is around the inflation creation process as well as the natural rate of unemployment, both of which are tremendously important in the short term.	13	1
201503	2195	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	In fact, I would say that I found some real attraction in the alternative scenario that the staff offered at our Board meeting on Monday.	13	1
201503	2196	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	In that scenario—this echoes what Governor Fischer was talking about— the natural rate declines further to 4¼ percent; productivity and economic growth are a little bit higher; and inflation is a little bit lower, thanks to the wider unemployment gap.	13	1

201503	2198	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	It is certainly that.	13	1

201503	2200	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	So I think that, as we get closer to full employment, the level and character of these supply-side constraints become ever more important.	13	1
201503	2201	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	To wrap up, I see the main risk to the economy coming from events abroad, particularly strength in the dollar and an exit of Greece from the euro, which might be managed well enough to avoid a catastrophe—at least for the euro system, if not for Greece.	13	1
