201503	2206	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Brainard.	13	1
201503	2207	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201503	2208	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Since we last met, we’ve seen further divergence in the two legs of our dual mandate.	13	1
201503	2209	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Employment has shown further strong gains, while inflation has softened further away from the 2 percent target.	13	1
201503	2210	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	My outlook for the economy has darkened somewhat, in light of the strong headwinds from the continued appreciation of the dollar and lackluster domestic spending.	13	1
201503	2211	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	The news received from the labor market has been positive and continues to suggest that the economy is moving closer to our goal.	13	1
201503	2212	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Since we last met, the data for January and February and the revisions to previous months paint a noticeably stronger picture of employment growth.	13	1
201503	2213	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	In particular, payroll growth is now reported to have averaged 280,000 in the second half of last year and appears to have maintained that pace into the current quarter.	13	1
201503	2214	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Since December, measures of labor utilization have all improved:  The unemployment rate has edged lower, the participation rate has moved up, and the number of employed working part time for economic reasons has declined.	13	1
201503	2215	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	At the same time, the news on inflation suggests that it remains stubbornly low relative to our 2 percent target.	13	1
201503	2216	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	The recent declines in headline PCE inflation over the past several months are largely due to previous large declines in crude oil prices.	13	1
201503	2217	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Once those price movements bottom out, we might expect to see headline prices moving fairly close to the underlying rate of core inflation, but the underlying rate of core inflation is also quite low, according to the recent data.	13	1
201503	2218	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	The 12-month change in core PCE prices in January was 1.3 percent, similar to the rate a year ago, and higher-frequency measures are even lower.	13	1
201503	2219	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	In that regard, I note that even the three-month change in the Federal Reserve Bank of Dallas trimmed mean rate was only 0.7 percent.	13	1
201503	2220	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Obviously, one possible way to reconcile the disconnect between employment and wage and price developments is that the natural rate of unemployment may be lower than many observers have been assuming, and that the participation rate gap may be greater.	13	1
201503	2221	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	In particular, that inflation and wages have increased little or not at all over a time when resources, by many measures, have moved much closer to full utilization suggests we may be further away from full employment.	13	1
201503	2222	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Consistent with that hypothesis, a shift in the demographic profile of our workforce would be in keeping with a reduction in the natural rate, and there may be some structural aftereffects of the financial crisis that also support that story.	13	1
201503	2223	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	In recent months, we’ve seen some crosscurrents among the components of aggregate demand domestically.	13	1
201503	2224	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	On the positive end of the spectrum, consumer spending appears to have increased robustly at the end of last year.	13	1
201503	2225	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Although auto and retail sales softened in February— perhaps in part because of adverse weather—strong job growth, the effect of lower oil prices on real incomes, and increased confidence all point in the direction of supporting consumer spending.	13	1
201503	2226	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	But the other components of domestic aggregate demand appear quite tepid.	13	1
201503	2227	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Residential investment remains very weak, as shown by the most recent data on housing starts.	13	1
201503	2228	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Of course, we all keep holding out hope that low levels of homeownership and some hopeful signs on household formation still point toward the possibility that pent-up demand will start to materialize.	13	1
201503	2229	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Business fixed investment looks to increase only modestly this year, particularly with lower oil prices pushing down drilling investment.	13	1
201503	2230	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	And, of course, government spending, while not subtracting from economic growth, is also not likely to add much.	13	1
201503	2231	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Against this, net exports are exerting a material drag on GDP growth.	13	1
201503	2232	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	The broad nominal dollar has appreciated more than 15 percent since June of last year, and with that appreciation has come a sharp reduction in the contribution of net exports.	13	1
201503	2233	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	In fact, we haven’t seen as strong a negative effect from dollar appreciation and a decline in net exports for more than a decade.	13	1
201503	2234	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	In the Tealbook projections, net exports take away 1 percentage point from real GDP growth this year and next.	13	1
201503	2235	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Thus, the direction of aggregate spending over the next year may largely reflect the outcome of a “tug of war” between domestic consumer spending and net exports.	13	1
201503	2236	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	The hopeful scenario is that faster consumer spending will outweigh the downward pull of an appreciating dollar and that resource utilization will continue to increase.	13	1
201503	2237	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	But there are risks, I think, on both sides.	13	1
201503	2238	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	On the upside, the advent of quantitative easing in Europe may finally lead to a convincing recovery, a noticeable increase in inflation and inflation expectations, and a stabilization or even some reversal of recent gains in the dollar.	13	1
201503	2239	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	In fact, the effect of QE on asset prices in Europe is promising.	13	1
201503	2240	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	One could even imagine that, further out in the medium term, faster foreign economic growth leads to reversals in both energy prices and previous gains in the dollar.	13	1
201503	2241	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Such a confluence of events could push inflation higher, with the attendant implications for monetary policy.	13	1
201503	2242	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	On the downside, however, the effect of quantitative easing on European domestic demand may be somewhat attenuated due to the very bankcentric nature of the financial system in the euro area.	13	1
201503	2243	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Furthermore, many interest rates in the euro zone are now negative, and there’s considerable uncertainty about the effect of negative interest rates on activity, particularly as they fall further.	13	1
201503	2244	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	This greater uncertainty, together with the ongoing uncertainty about the outcome of difficult negotiations between Greece and its creditors, suggests sizable downside risks.	13	1
201503	2245	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	It is also striking that the dollar appreciated substantially further on the commencement of asset purchases in the euro area, even though the markets had already been largely exposed to all of the details surrounding the implementation of quantitative easing.	13	1
201503	2246	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	This, together with a continued large gap in longer-term interest rates between the United States and other advanced foreign economies—as well as the potential for China to adjust its currency—suggests that the upward movements in the dollar could well continue and be larger and more persistent, even, than in the Tealbook baseline.	13	1
201503	2247	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	This could act as a significant headwind for economic activity and put further downward pressure on inflation—both indirectly, through lower resource utilization, and directly, through its effects on core import prices.	13	1
201503	2248	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	The staff’s judgmental estimate is that a 10 percent appreciation of the dollar reduces core import prices by 3 percentage points and PCE prices by 0.3 percentage point over the course of a year or so.	13	1
201503	2249	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	But there’s considerable uncertainty regarding the magnitude of import price pass-through.	13	1
201503	2250	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	And plausible empirical estimates, as well as the staff’s SIGMA model, suggest that the effect could be much larger.	13	1
201503	2251	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	These risks make it considerably less likely we will see evidence by June that will enable us to feel reasonably confident inflation is moving back to its target, a theme I think we will return to tomorrow in our discussion of monetary policy.	13	1
201503	2252	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201503	2253	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you very much, and my thanks to everyone for another interesting round of observations on the economic outlook.	13	1
201503	2254	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	As usual, I will try to summarize briefly some of the main themes in the go-round, and then I’d like to add some remarks of my own.	13	1
201503	2255	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Starting with the labor market, I think everyone agrees that labor market conditions are continuing to improve.	13	1
201503	2256	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	We see broad evidence of that in a range of indicators as well as in anecdotal reports.	13	1
201503	2257	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	It is, of course, a very welcome development.	13	1
201503	2258	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Most important, payroll gains have speeded up over the past three months in spite of harsh winter weather in much of the country.	13	1
201503	2259	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	The unemployment rate has been moving down, and broader measures of labor underutilization, such as U-6, have declined by similar amounts.	13	1
201503	2260	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Labor force participation has moved sideways.	13	1
201503	2261	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	But, as some of you noted, the fact that it’s held steady rather than declining further in line with demographic trends represents an improvement of sorts.	13	1
201503	2262	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	And some of you mentioned that surveys of job market perceptions remain strong.	13	1
201503	2263	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	In spite of the decline in the unemployment rate, all but two of you, based on your SEPs, continue to think that some slack remains in the labor market.	13	1
201503	2264	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Interestingly, quite a few of you revised down your estimates of the longer-run normal unemployment rate this round.	13	1
201503	2265	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Wage developments garnered a good deal of discussion.	13	1
201503	2266	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Measures such as average hourly earnings, hourly compensation, and the ECI all continue to show sluggish nominal gains of around 2 percent or so, well below levels that could ultimately be consistent with 2 percent inflation and trend productivity growth.	13	1
201503	2267	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	But, as discussed in the Tealbook box—and a number of you mentioned this—business surveys are finding that wage increases among firms are becoming larger and more prevalent, and that result seems to be consistent with many reports that you’re hearing from your business contacts.	13	1
201503	2268	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	That evidence suggests that a pickup in nominal wage growth may be under way, although there were also comments suggesting that the pickup in wage growth is still not broad based and is confined to some specific sectors.	13	1
201503	2269	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Turning to developments in the broader economy, I heard general agreement that the current readings on overall activity have, on balance, moderated since the January meeting, and a number of indicators have come in quite a bit softer than expected.	13	1
201503	2270	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Some of you noted that prospects for GDP growth over the rest of the year and beyond now look a little less favorable than in December partly because of dollar appreciation, but also some of you have lowered your estimates of trend growth.	13	1
201503	2271	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	I think most of you, though, continue to view the outlook as still sufficiently favorable to support continued improvement in the labor market.	13	1
201503	2272	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Many of you cited consumer spending as a bright spot for the economy, reflecting low gas prices, rising employment and wealth, and other factors.	13	1
201503	2273	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	But there is the caveat that we’ve had three disappointing retail sales reports.	13	1
201503	2274	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	A number of you mentioned harsh winter weather, and that could be a factor.	13	1
201503	2275	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	In other areas, though, we are seeing weakness.	13	1
201503	2276	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	The recovery in the housing market remains quite sluggish.	13	1
201503	2277	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	A number of you mentioned that nonresidential business investment seems as though it’s weakening further, in large part reflecting lower oil prices and reduced drilling activity, and some of you noted that this is something that could intensify over time.	13	1
201503	2278	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Many of you commented on the likely influence of the marked dollar appreciation we’ve seen, the fact that it’s already affecting foreign trade, and the possibility that the dollar could continue to appreciate further from present levels.	13	1
201503	2279	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Export growth appears to have slowed markedly, and the appreciated dollar is likely to have a persistent effect.	13	1
201503	2280	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	On the other side, some of you mentioned slightly stronger economic growth in places like Europe, in part due to the ECB actions.	13	1
201503	2281	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	On the other hand, there was a lot of concern about downside risks from developments in the global economy, including ongoing risks related to China and Russia; renewed and perhaps intensified risks relating to Greece; and mention of Brazil and other countries for which a strong dollar could affect corporations that have borrowed in dollars, and from which we could see defaults and spillovers.	13	1
201503	2282	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	On the inflation front, incoming data was roughly as the staff expected.	13	1
201503	2283	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	I think we all anticipate that inflation will run well below our 2 percent goal in the near term because of earlier declines in energy prices and decreases in core import prices.	13	1
201503	2284	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	But most of you don’t see incoming data as materially affecting the longer-run outlook.	13	1
201503	2285	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Overall, I heard general agreement that inflation is likely to move back toward 2 percent over the next few years as the effects of low energy prices and dollar appreciation fade and as the labor market continues to improve.	13	1
201503	2286	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	A number of you expressed confidence in your outlook that inflation will return to 2 percent.	13	1
201503	2287	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	However, a number of you also expressed some doubt about that as well as a lack of confidence in this forecast.	13	1
201503	2288	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Some of you, in expressing doubts, pointed to price and wage developments and the fact that core inflation is moving down.	13	1
201503	2289	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	In addition, a number of you commented on the fact that, even though survey-based measures of long-run inflation expectations have largely remained stable, it is concerning, at least to some of you, that market- based measures of inflation compensation, after a short-lived rise, have declined more or less back to the level we saw at the previous meeting.	13	1
201503	2290	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Exactly what’s going on there is hard to determine.	13	1
201503	2291	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	It’s a little bit perplexing that there seems to be such a strong correlation of this measure of inflation compensation with oil prices and the dollar.	13	1
201503	2292	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Nevertheless, for some of you, it is a significant concern and points toward a possible loss of credibility of the Committee in meeting its inflation commitments.	13	1
201503	2293	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Let me stop there.	13	1
201503	2294	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Would anyone like to comment on that summary?	13	1
201503	2295	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	[No response]	13	1
201503	2296	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Then, if I might, I’d like to add some comments of my own.	13	1
201503	2297	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Like everyone else, I see solid evidence that the labor market is improving, and that we’re drawing closer to normal conditions.	13	1
201503	2298	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	But, like many of you, I, too, think we still have a ways to go.	13	1
201503	2299	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Like quite a few of you, I also estimate that the natural rate of unemployment is at 5 percent.	13	1
201503	2300	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	I note that the Beveridge curve has yet to shift all of the way back to its pre-crisis position.	13	1
201503	2301	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Even so, I see that the evidence overall is relatively thin that the natural rate is higher now than it was prior to the financial crisis.	13	1
201503	2302	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	While I recognize that there are alternative explanations for continued subdued growth in wages, I take that as some evidence of a good bit of remaining slack.	13	1
201503	2303	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	In addition, labor market slack is showing up in forms that are not included in U-3, particularly involuntary part-time employment and depressed labor force participation.	13	1
201503	2304	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	The spread between the broadest measure of labor market underutilization, the U-6 rate, and the conventional unemployment rate is currently 1¾ percentage points higher than the average spread in the years preceding the recession.	13	1
201503	2305	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	So even when the unemployment rate reaches its normal longer-run level, the labor market will still be putting downward pressure on inflation until this spread is returned to normal.	13	1
201503	2306	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Turning to the outlook for economic growth, I’m reasonably optimistic that real GDP will expand sufficiently fast this year to enable further progress toward our maximum employment goal, but not all of the indicators are favorable.	13	1
201503	2307	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	My optimism about the near-term outlook for real activity rests in large part on factors like rising employment, low gas prices, expanding household wealth, and a marked improvement in consumer confidence.	13	1
201503	2308	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	I’m cautiously optimistic that these same factors, coupled with low mortgage rates and demographic pressures, will enable a somewhat faster pace of recovery in the housing market.	13	1
201503	2309	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	But I am concerned that other factors, particularly the dollar appreciation and weak activity abroad, will constrain overall GDP growth and net exports.	13	1
201503	2310	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	I, too, am concerned that the tone of recent spending and production indicators has been weaker than I expected, and I am worried about the disappointing string of retail sales reports.	13	1
201503	2311	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	On the inflation front, I continue to expect inflation to move up gradually to 2 percent over the next few years as the labor market tightens.	13	1
201503	2312	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	The core price data have come in roughly as I expected, at least after adjusting for the one-time effect of the surprise in ACA reimbursements.	13	1
201503	2313	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	And survey-based measures of expected inflation have stayed stable, even though, as we discussed, market-based measures remain very low.	13	1
201503	2314	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	As Simon Potter noted earlier, the correlation of recent movements in inflation compensation with recent shifts in oil prices suggests that the decline in inflation compensation may reflect some type of over- extrapolation by investors of what presumably are transitory effects of shifts in energy prices.	13	1
201503	2315	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	If we adopt alternative B, one criterion for an initial tightening is that we need to be reasonably confident that inflation will move back to 2 percent over the medium term.	13	1
201503	2316	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	For the remainder of this year, my guess is that it will be hard to point to data demonstrating that inflation is actually moving up toward our objective.	13	1
201503	2317	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Measured on a 12-month basis, both core and headline inflation will very likely be running below 1½ percent all year.	13	1
201503	2318	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	That means that if we decide to start tightening later this year, a development that I think is likely, we will have to justify our inflation forecasts using indirect evidence, historical experience, and economic theory.	13	1
201503	2319	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	The argument from history and economic theory seems straightforward.	13	1
201503	2320	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Experience here and abroad teaches us that, as resource utilization tightens, eventually inflation will begin to rise.	13	1
201503	2321	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	To me, this seems like a simple matter of demand and supply.	13	1
201503	2322	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	So the more labor and product markets tighten, the more confident I’ll become in the inflation outlook.	13	1
201503	2323	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Because of the lags in monetary policy, the current high degree of monetary accommodation, and the speed at which the unemployment rate is coming down, it would, to my mind, be imprudent to wait until inflation is much closer to 2 percent to begin to normalize policy.	13	1
201503	2324	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	I consider this a strong argument for an initial tightening with inflation still at low levels, and it’s one that I plan to make.	13	1
201503	2325	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	But I also recognize and am concerned that, at least in recent years, the empirical relationship between slack and inflation has been quite weak.	13	1
201503	2326	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	The argument from indirect evidence will be more complicated.	13	1
201503	2327	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	One important thing to point to, I hope, will be the continued stability of survey measures of expected inflation, and I would certainly welcome seeing a backup in market-based measures of inflation compensation that would improve my confidence.	13	1
201503	2328	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	I’ll also feel more confident in the inflation outlook if any downward movements we see in core inflation can be relatively easily attributed to movements in energy prices and the dollar, which I expect to be transitory.	13	1
201503	2329	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Thus far, as the nicely done box in the Tealbook on the topic discussed, it looks as though the pass-through of energy prices to core inflation has been quite small.	13	1
201503	2330	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	The appreciation of the dollar is holding down import prices, and that’s already showing up in goods prices such as those for apparel, which has a relatively high import content.	13	1
201503	2331	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	However, price increases for items with low import content, such as non- energy services, have been little changed over the past year.	13	1
201503	2332	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	This pattern has two implications for our communications.	13	1
201503	2333	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	First, we can probably point to these data and stable inflation expectations as evidence that we don’t face a growing persistent deflation problem.	13	1
201503	2334	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Second, if the dollar doesn’t keep rising, then we should see inflation in these import-intensive categories moving back up over time.	13	1
201503	2335	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	With respect to the behavior of wages, many observers are arguing that we should hold off tightening as long as nominal wage gains remain low, because that’s prima facie evidence that considerable slack remains in the economy.	13	1
201503	2336	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Some have gone further and urged that we hold off tightening until real wages are growing more in line with trend productivity, something many models view as a basic equilibrium condition.	13	1
201503	2337	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Although, in common with the Tealbook projection, I expect nominal wage growth to move up over time, I intend to resist establishing faster wage growth as a prerequisite for an initial tightening, for several reasons.	13	1
201503	2338	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	First, we don’t know what trend productivity growth is or will be, so we cannot be sure what the equilibrium rate of real wage growth should be.	13	1
201503	2339	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Second, real wage gains have been falling short of estimates of trend productivity growth for at least the past 15 years for reasons that are not fully understood but are presumably exogenous with regard to monetary policy, and these may continue into the future.	13	1
201503	2340	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Third, downward nominal wage rigidity may have given rise to pent-up real wage cuts that could restrain wage growth for some time to come.	13	1
201503	2341	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	And, finally, the evidence that nominal wages are a useful predictor for future price inflation simply isn’t very strong.	13	1
201503	2342	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	My final point is that, as we all know, liftoff is only the first step toward policy normalization, and I plan to emphasize in my own communications that even after liftoff, policy is likely to remain very accommodative for quite some time.	13	1

201503	2392	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	As Don Kim noted in his briefing, many of you made downward revisions to your projected federal funds rate paths.	21	2

201503	2394	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	In particular, I first calculate for each of you the values for the federal funds rate at the end of 2015, 2016, and 2017 that a noninertial Taylor (1999) rule, shown to the right, would prescribe based on your individual estimates of the longer-run normal unemployment rate and your projections for core PCE inflation and the unemployment rate through 2017.	21	2
201503	2395	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	So the symbols in the Taylor rule shown to the right—the symbol 𝜋𝜋 denotes four-quarter core PCE inflation, and the letter u stands for the unemployment rate.	21	2
201503	2396	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	In these calculations, I use your estimates of the longer-run real federal funds rate as intercepts, the r*LR.	21	2
201503	2397	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	I then subtract these prescriptions from your actual projections for the federal funds rate.	21	2
201503	2398	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	The median difference between your projections and the rule’s prescriptions is close to minus 1½ percentage points in 2015 and 2016, as shown by the blue dots to the left; by 2017, it narrows to about minus ½ percentage point.	21	2
201503	2399	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	The differences in 2015 are, on average, slightly smaller than they were in your December projections, and in 2016 and 2017, they are slightly larger.	21	2
201503	2400	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	Given these sizable differences, it might appear that your policy projections imply a high degree of policy accommodation, perhaps reflecting considerations such as an assessment that risks to the macroeconomic outlook remain asymmetric as long as the federal funds rate is at the lower bound.	21	2
201503	2401	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	But are these shortfalls relative to the Taylor (1999) benchmark a good measure of the degree of monetary accommodation implied by your projections?	21	2
201503	2402	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	To answer this question, I use a version of a textbook, as it’s called, IS equation, shown in the middle panel, which relates the unemployment gap (u minus u*), as a measure of the cyclical position of the economy, to the real rate gap, defined as the deviation of the real federal funds rate (r) from a time-varying equilibrium level (r*).	21	2
201503	2403	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	As shown by the equation, this equilibrium real rate has the property that, if the actual real rate was kept at its equilibrium level, over time the unemployment gap would close.	21	2
201503	2404	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	Thus, in this set-up, the equilibrium real rate is a medium-run concept that varies over time, capturing persistent shifts in the position of the IS curve.	21	2
201503	2405	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	I estimate the coefficients on the lagged unemployment gap and the lagged real rate gap in this equation using historical data for the fourth quarter of each year so as to be consistent with the data that you provide in your SEPs.	21	2
201503	2406	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	I use the staff’s historical estimates for u* and estimates for r* taken from the model that President Williams and I developed some years ago.	21	2
201503	2407	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	With these coefficients in hand, I then insert each participant’s projected values for the unemployment rate and the real federal funds rate, as well as his or her estimate of the longer-run normal unemployment rate, and solve the equation for the implied value of the time-varying r* at the end of each year.	21	2
201503	2408	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	These implied values are shown in the lower-left panel.	21	2
201503	2409	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	The median is close to zero in both 2015 and 2016 and rises to a little above ½ percent by 2017, still well below the longer-run median estimate of 1¾ percent.	21	2
201503	2410	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	These temporarily low levels of the implied equilibrium real rate reflect the fact that your projected paths for the real federal funds rate run well below your longer-run normal values.	21	2
201503	2411	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	In such circumstances, the IS equation, shown in the middle panel, would predict substantially faster declines in the unemployment rate than shown in your projections if r* was at its longer-run value.	21	2
201503	2412	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	To reconcile your unemployment rate projections with your real rate projections, it must be the case that r* remains depressed for some time.	21	2
201503	2413	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	Put differently, the fact that most of you expect the unemployment rate to remain close to your estimates of its longer-run normal value over coming years implies that the real rate gap cannot be particularly large.	21	2
201503	2414	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	This analysis suggests that the differences relative to the Taylor (1999) benchmark with the longer-run r* value as the intercept may be somewhat misleading as an indication of policy accommodation.	21	2
201503	2415	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	In the lower-right panel, I repeat the Taylor rule calculation shown in the upper-left panel after replacing your longer-run normal value for the real federal funds rate with the time-varying r* values.	21	2
201503	2416	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	The median difference between your projected federal funds rates and those prescribed by this version of the Taylor (1999) rule is close to zero at the end of both 2015 and 2016 and about ¼ percentage point in 2017, substantially narrower than the ones shown in the upper-left panel.	21	2
201503	2417	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	The bullets in the upper panel of exhibit 2 mention a few caveats to this analysis.	21	2
201503	2418	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	The results are conditional on the specification of the IS equation.	21	2
201503	2419	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	A different model of the transmission of real interest rates to real activity might produce different estimates of the equilibrium real interest rate.	21	2
201503	2420	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	Moreover, this simple model does not provide insight into the structural factors that underlie the estimated changes in r*.	21	2
201503	2421	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	That said, it seems plausible that, as several of you suggest in your SEP narratives, lingering effects of the financial crisis and considerable restraint from economic and financial developments abroad may play some role.	21	2
201503	2422	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	Let me now turn to today’s policy decision and the draft alternative statements.	21	2
201503	2423	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	First, I want to thank everyone for responding to our earlier drafts with valuable feedback.	21	2
201503	2424	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	Judging from those communications, the key judgment that you face today is how to replace the “patient” language with new forward guidance that maintains the option to raise the target range for the federal funds rate at any meeting, beginning in June, and describes broad conditions under which you will determine that liftoff is warranted.	21	2
201503	2425	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	Rather than go through each alternative statement separately, I want to focus on how the alternatives address the issues that appear to be central to your decision today.	21	2
201503	2426	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	First, the revised statement will provide an update of your assessment of the current inflation situation and your confidence in the outlook for inflation.	21	2
201503	2427	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	As indicated in the middle panel, all three of the statements report that inflation has declined further below the Committee’s longer-run objective and is anticipated to “remain near its recent low level” in the near term.	21	2
201503	2428	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	However, the alternatives offer different options for characterizing recent movements in inflation compensation and express varying degrees of confidence in the outlook for inflation.	21	2
201503	2429	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	Alternative B notes that market-based measures of inflation compensation remain low, but that survey-based measures remain stable.	21	2
201503	2430	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	Alternative B also retains the earlier expectation that inflation will “rise gradually toward 2 percent over the medium term.”	21	2
201503	2431	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	Alternative C states that measures of inflation compensation have increased, and that inflation “will” reach the 2 percent objective.	21	2
201503	2432	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	It also notes that survey-based measures remain stable.	21	2
201503	2433	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	In contrast, alternative A expresses clear concern that inflation will return only “very gradually” to the Committee’s 2 percent objective and could remain below it “for a protracted period.”	21	2
201503	2434	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	Moreover, alternative A emphasizes that measures of inflation compensation “remain well below levels observed last summer.”	21	2
201503	2435	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	I should also point out that, given the drop in crude oil prices in recent days, the alternative B in front of you deletes the reference to “earlier” in describing energy price declines in paragraph 1.	21	2
201503	2436	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	Moving to the forward guidance, the issue before you is how to revise the guidance in order to both communicate more specifically the data dependence of a decision to increase the target range for the federal funds rate and shape expectations regarding the likely timing of liftoff.	21	2
201503	2437	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	Regarding labor market conditions, your SEP submissions indicate that most of you anticipate further improvement and expect that the unemployment rate will have declined another couple of tenths by the time that liftoff will be warranted.	21	2
201503	2438	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	Thus, your expectations for progress toward the maximum employment goal are broadly represented across the forward guidance in all three draft alternatives.	21	2
201503	2439	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	The alternatives differ on the characterization of inflation prospects that would warrant a liftoff decision.	21	2
201503	2440	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	Alternative B indicates that you would want to be more, or at least not less, confident that inflation will return to your 2 percent objective over the medium term.	21	2
201503	2441	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	Alternative C suggests that you are already sufficiently confident to signal liftoff soon.	21	2
201503	2442	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	And alternative A states that you would need to see clear evidence that inflation was moving up to 2 percent.	21	2
201503	2443	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	Looking at how the three alternatives may shape expectations for the timing of liftoff, alternative B states that, in addition to further improvement in the labor market, the Committee will need to be “reasonably confident” that inflation will move back to its 2 percent objective “over the medium term,” and thus provides flexibility to make ongoing data-dependent assessments of economic conditions.	21	2
201503	2444	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	The data dependence is reinforced with the addition of the sentence stating that the change does not indicate that the timing of the first increase in the federal funds rate has been decided.	21	2
201503	2445	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	Moreover, in order to bridge the forward guidance from the presumed time dependence associated with the “patient” language, alternative B specifically says that an April liftoff is unlikely.	21	2
201503	2446	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	According to your SEP submissions, at present, about half of you see the appropriate timing of the first increase in the target for the federal funds rate as early as June, while the other half expects that the decision will not be made until later this year.	21	2
201503	2447	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	As Simon noted in his briefing, market expectations are broadly similar.	21	2
201503	2448	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	Some of you may be sufficiently confident about the outlook for both the labor market and inflation to want to boost the odds of liftoff in June by substituting “in a couple of meetings” for “patient,” as in alternative C.	21	2
201503	2449	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	Finally, others may want to express more firmly the Committee’s commitment to its inflation objective, as in alternative A, extending the decision to be patient “until inflation is clearly moving up toward 2 percent” and asserting that the Committee would “use its tools as necessary” to reach that objective in two or three years—signals that likely would push forward the expected timing of liftoff.	21	2
201503	2450	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	Thank you, Madam Chair.	21	2
201503	2451	2015-03-18	meeting	LAUBACH	That concludes my prepared remarks, and I’ll be glad to take any questions.	21	2

201503	2634	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	If I could just start our round off with a couple of comments.	23	2
201503	2635	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	I think the economy has made considerable progress toward our objective of maximum employment.	23	2
201503	2636	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	And, because of the likely eventual implications of that progress for the inflation outlook, I believe it serves us well to remove “patient” from our policy statement at this time.	23	2
201503	2637	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Doing so will provide us with the flexibility to raise the federal funds rate at any meeting after April, with the actual timing dependent on how the economy evolves.	23	2
201503	2638	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	I don’t view the removal of “patient” as a signal that liftoff in June is particularly likely.	23	2
201503	2639	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	In my press conference, I intend to make it clear that the modification of our forward guidance doesn’t mean that we’ve determined the timing of liftoff, and that such timing will depend on the Committee’s assessment of incoming information.	23	2
201503	2640	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	In particular, I plan to indicate that the Committee will not necessarily raise rates in June.	23	2
201503	2641	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	That said, I also want to be clear that a June liftoff cannot be ruled out.	23	2
201503	2642	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Between now and the June FOMC meeting, we will receive three more employment reports.	23	2
201503	2643	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Like most of you, I see room for further improvement in labor market conditions, and I expect the rate of decline in the unemployment rate to slow some in the months ahead.	23	2
201503	2644	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	But it is possible we could see a continuing rapid decline in the unemployment rate, which could be approaching 5 percent by the time of the June meeting.	23	2
201503	2645	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	On the other hand, readings on inflation are likely to remain uncomfortably low.	23	2
201503	2646	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	At the time of the June meeting, the latest inflation readings will be for April.	23	2
201503	2647	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	The staff projects that the 12-month change in total PCE prices will be just 0.2 percent in April, and that for core PCE prices will be just 1.2 percent.	23	2
201503	2648	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	And the trend may not be our friend, in that inflation may well soften further for a few more months, especially if the dollar continues to appreciate as we get closer to the beginning of the normalization process.	23	2
201503	2649	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	As I noted in the economic go-round, I have tried to avoid establishing any simple criterion for achieving reasonable confidence that inflation will move up to 2 percent.	23	2
201503	2650	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	I have thus far emphasized—and I intend to continue emphasizing—that we do not have to see an increase in core inflation or an increase in nominal wage growth that would achieve the confidence that’s needed for us to move, and that we intend to consider a broad range of data and evidence in arriving at that judgment.	23	2
201503	2651	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Further labor market improvement on its own will work to improve my confidence in the forecast that inflation will move back up to 2 percent.	23	2
201503	2652	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	But if core inflation, nominal wage growth, or measures of inflation expectations move the wrong way, I think we may find a decision to commence tightening quite challenging.	23	2
201503	2653	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	These uncertainties about the outlook for inflation and the labor market are precisely why moving to a meeting-by- meeting footing in our policy deliberations is appropriate.	23	2
201503	2654	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	As a final point, I intend to acknowledge and communicate that, if the economy evolves in line with our forecast, increases in the federal funds rate over time are likely to be gradual.	23	2
201503	2655	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Indeed, in line with Thomas’s analysis, if r* is gradually rising as the headwinds that have held back the recovery continue to abate, a gradual rise in the federal funds rate is likely to be appropriate.	23	2
201503	2656	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Of course, it’s also true that a gradual rise is required just to keep the level of monetary accommodation constant.	23	2

201503	2663	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	While I support the new forward-guidance language, it’s important to be aware that it introduces some important internal tension into the statement.	23	2
201503	2664	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	The new language states that the Committee anticipates raising rates “when it has seen further improvement in the labor market and is reasonably confident that inflation will move back to its 2 percent objective over the medium term.”	23	2
201503	2665	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	This seems to leave open the possibility that we are not now reasonably confident that inflation will move back to our objective.	23	2
201503	2666	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	In contrast, the second paragraph states that we expect “inflation to rise gradually toward 2 percent over the medium term.”	23	2
201503	2667	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	In the broader context of that paragraph, I take this to mean that we are confident that our future policy actions will bring inflation back to 2 percent.	23	2
201503	2668	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	So our new forward-guidance language appears to be in conflict with the second paragraph, because it seems to suggest we’re not confident about our future conduct of monetary policy.	23	2
201503	2669	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	This is an awkward and potentially confusing implication to convey.	23	2
201503	2670	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	One way to reconcile the two passages is to change the forward-guidance language to read “remains reasonably confident” instead of “is reasonably confident,” implying that we are now confident.	23	2
201503	2671	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	Another approach would be to interpret the “reasonably confident” language as conditional on raising rates—in other words, to interpret the forward-guidance language as meaning to say that the Committee anticipates raising rates “when it has seen further improvement in the labor market and is reasonably confident that an increase in rates is consistent with inflation moving back to its 2 percent objective over the medium term.”	23	2
201503	2672	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	Now, rewording the forward guidance this way would eliminate the apparent conflict with the second paragraph.	23	2
201503	2673	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	The language there is about our confidence that our policy will get inflation back to 2 percent, while the language in paragraph 3 says that, to raise rates, we want to be reasonably confident that raising rates won’t prevent us from getting back to 2 percent.	23	2
201503	2674	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	I understand that, given the weeks and months of deliberations that have gone into crafting this language, this would be a late-in-the-game suggestion to make, so I’m not going to insist on this change.	23	2
201503	2675	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	But I think that it’s worth being aware of this tension as we talk about policy in public going forward.	23	2
201503	2676	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	In any event, this is something you might have to address in your press conference this afternoon, Madam Chair.	23	2
201503	2677	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	And it’s something that, as I said, I think we should be continually aware of.	23	2
201503	2678	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	Looking ahead at how the data might come in between now and June, I believe it’s important to recognize that we could be reasonably confident about inflation then—as you said, Madam Chair—even if the monthly readings on core inflation continue to bounce around at a relatively low level.	23	2
201503	2679	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	Certainly, we’d rather not see persistently soft core inflation, but our focus should be on the outlook for inflation, not on realized values.	23	2
201503	2680	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	In particular, I don’t think we should convey that a substantial rise in reported core inflation is in some way a precondition for lifting off in June.	23	2
201503	2681	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	Setting a high bar by waiting to see a vigorous rise in actual inflation ignores the long and variable lags that we know are associated with monetary policy, and it risks a return to the “go-stop” regime that made monetary policy a driving force behind real fluctuations.	23	2
201503	2682	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	As I noted at the outset, if conditions evolve close to expectations over the next few months, then I’m likely to argue for a rate increase in June.	23	2
201503	2683	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	If so, I will do so based on the premise that we should set our monetary policy instrument so as to align the real short-term interest rate with the economy’s underlying real fundamentals.	23	2
201503	2684	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	What do we know about those fundamentals?	23	2
201503	2685	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	Over the past three years, we’ve seen the following:  Consumption has grown at an average annual rate of 2.5 percent, a number we last saw in the fall of 2007; the unemployment rate has fallen almost 3 percentage points, from 8.3 percent to 5.5 percent; and employment has grown at a 1.9 percent annual rate, a number we last saw in the spring of 2001.	23	2
201503	2686	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	Over the same time period, the short-term real interest rate has been below negative 1 percent.	23	2
201503	2687	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	Our understanding of the relationship between the natural real rate, as it’s called, and observable variables is admittedly imprecise.	23	2
201503	2688	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	But I think both theory and experience tell us that a real interest rate of negative 1 percent is unlikely to be consistent with continuing low inflation in the face of the steady growth we’ve seen in the real economy.	23	2
201503	2689	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	Granted, the natural real interest rate may have shifted down in recent years, but I’d note that attempts to quantify that decline, such as those based on the work of Laubach and Williams, did not generate anything like the current level of real rates.	23	2
201503	2690	2015-03-18	meeting	LACKER	So I think a strong case can be made that our policy rate should be higher right now, and June represents the first opportunity to raise rates without contradicting our past forward guidance.	23	2

201503	2695	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I support alternative A, with one change.	23	2
201503	2696	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	At the end of paragraph 3, alternative A says that the FOMC will “use its tools as necessary to return inflation to 2 percent in two to three years.”	23	2
201503	2697	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I would suggest rewording “two to three years” to be “one to two years.”	23	2
201503	2698	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	This is the definition of “medium term” that we used in past statements, and I don’t see a reason why we would change it now.	23	2
201503	2699	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I favor this modified version of alternative A because it promotes maximum employment and it promotes price stability.	23	2
201503	2700	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In terms of promoting maximum employment, I agree with the assessment of the Tealbook, Book B, that alternative A would be seen as an unexpected increase in monetary accommodation.	23	2
201503	2701	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	That additional stimulus would generate extra demand for goods and services.	23	2
201503	2702	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The extra demand for goods and services would lead employment to grow more rapidly, induce employers to convert part-time jobs to full-time ones, and further increase job- finding rates for the nonemployed.	23	2
201503	2703	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I see all of these effects as being consistent with promoting maximum employment.	23	2
201503	2704	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Of course, I could always cite these beneficial employment effects as a justification for adding monetary stimulus.	23	2
201503	2705	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	As policymakers, we always need to weigh these benefits against the all-too-familiar potential costs of stimulus—the risks of unduly high inflation and financial instability.	23	2
201503	2706	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	These costs seem very small at the current time.	23	2
201503	2707	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In terms of prices, the inflation outlook remains subdued.	23	2
201503	2708	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Like the Board’s staff, I don’t expect inflation to rise back to 2 percent for several years.	23	2
201503	2709	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In terms of financial stability, I see no risks that are material for the macroeconomy.	23	2
201503	2710	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	As the Tealbook, Book B, observes, signs of excessive risk-taking are not widespread, and use of short-term financing instruments and indicators of leverage remain moderate.	23	2
201503	2711	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I’ve described how the incremental risks to financial stability or inflation associated with further stimulus seem small to me.	23	2
201503	2712	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I should emphasize that, unlike the objective function posited in the Tealbook, Book B, my own objective function does not include losses associated with the unemployment rate falling below u*.	23	2
201503	2713	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	As an economist, it’s unclear to me what kind of social waste would be generated by additional job creation, especially given current levels of employment and other labor market metrics.	23	2
201503	2714	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	As a policymaker, I do not see this formulation in the FOMC’s objective function as being consistent with our mandate to promote maximum employment.	23	2
201503	2715	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So alternative A promotes maximum employment.	23	2
201503	2716	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Let me turn to how it promotes price stability.	23	2
201503	2717	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I interpret the heart of this mandate as keeping inflation expectations anchored at 2 percent.	23	2
201503	2718	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	There are three relevant facts.	23	2
201503	2719	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The first fact is that PCE inflation has been below target for nearly three years.	23	2
201503	2720	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	As well, with the exception of a brief period at the end of 2011, core PCE inflation has been below 2 percent for closer to seven years.	23	2
201503	2721	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	A second fact is, my inflation outlook, like that of the Board’s staff, remains low.	23	2
201503	2722	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Under the monetary policy assumptions of the Tealbook, Book A, I do not foresee inflation returning to target in a sustainable way until 2018.	23	2
201503	2723	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	My outlook, like that of the Board’s staff, incorporates estimates of the slope of the Phillips curve from the past 20 years, which is quite flat.	23	2
201503	2724	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Others around the table have more confidence that the Phillips curve will revert to the steeper slope that was seen prior to that time period, and I guess that’s obviously a difference in perspective that we might be able to receive more information about as we go forward.	23	2
201503	2725	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The third fact is that there’s been a market slide in market-based measures of longer-term inflation compensation, and they remain near historical lows.	23	2
201503	2726	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	On this third fact, I want to note that I believe we can think about two different kinds of signals out there in terms of how anchored inflation expectations are.	23	2
201503	2727	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	One signal is coming from the surveys, and one signal is coming from market-based measures.	23	2
201503	2728	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	These are both noisy signals.	23	2
201503	2729	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The usual approaches to decision theory would not say that we should simply ignore one of those signals and just rely on the one that’s remained constant to form our assessments.	23	2
201503	2730	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	A more typical approach to decision theory would try to put weight on both signals and, with humility, conclude that there has been a change in the landscape over the past six months in terms of how anchored we should think inflation expectations are.	23	2
201503	2731	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Taken together, all three of these facts—that realized inflation has been as low as it has been for as long as it has been; that the outlook remains so low, unless we have a steeper Phillips curve than we’ve seen in the past 20 years; and that market-based measures of longer-term inflation compensation have slid so low—suggest that the baseline monetary policy stance outlined in the Tealbook, Book A, is creating a significant risk of inflation expectations sliding permanently below 2 percent.	23	2
201503	2732	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	And this risk is especially troubling in light of how hard it’s been for other central banks to engineer increases in inflation expectations.	23	2
201503	2733	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Now, I view this unanchoring of inflation expectations as intrinsically problematic in terms of the price-stability mandate.	23	2
201503	2734	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We should also keep in mind that a permanent slide of inflation expectations creates first-order losses in terms of the FOMC’s performance with respect to the employment mandate.	23	2
201503	2735	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In a low-inflation scenario, the zero lower bound would bind more frequently, and the ability of the FOMC to buffer the economy against recessionary shocks would be degraded.	23	2
201503	2736	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So that binding constraint creates first-order losses, not second-order losses.	23	2
201503	2737	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	This degradation would be especially severe if the long-run real natural rate of interest ends up being very low.	23	2
201503	2738	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	To sum up, Madam Chair, I recommend that the FOMC adopt alternative A because it promotes both maximum employment and price stability.	23	2
201503	2739	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Let me say a couple of things about alternative B.	23	2
201503	2740	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In contrast, alternative B removes the word “patient” as a characterization of the FOMC’s policy stance.	23	2
201503	2741	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I was very heartened to hear, Madam Chair, what you are planning to say in your press conference by way of modulating what might be conclusions reached by market participants and others about what we mean by removing the word “patient.”	23	2
201503	2742	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Just based on the survey evidence that we saw from the New York Fed, keeping the word “patient” would reduce the perceived probability of a June liftoff, I think, to near zero.	23	2
201503	2743	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Removing the word “patient” pushes that perceived probability of a June liftoff upward to be closer to 40 percent.	23	2
201503	2744	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So just removing the word “patient,” in and of itself, is a tightening of monetary policy.	23	2
201503	2745	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I’m opposed to such a move at this time.	23	2
201503	2746	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	This tightening of policy will reduce the projected rate of employment growth and the projected rate of increase in the inflation rate toward 2 percent.	23	2
201503	2747	2015-03-18	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201503	2748	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	23	2
201503	2749	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	President Evans.	23	2
201503	2750	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201503	2751	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	I can support alternative B today as written.	23	2
201503	2752	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	I recognize that you and the Committee are at the point when we want to actively entertain the possibility of lifting off beginning in June, and every meeting thereafter is a possibility.	23	2
201503	2753	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	To achieve this flexibility for liftoff, it is important to dismantle all elements of our calendar-based guidance and rely simply on meeting-by-meeting conditional assessments.	23	2
201503	2754	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	I can support removing “patient” today and replacing it with meaningful conditional guidance in the form of a statement that we won’t raise rates until we have reasonable confidence that inflation will move back to its 2 percent target over the medium term.	23	2
201503	2755	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	As long as “confidence” represents a meaningful economic threshold, I can support alternative B.	23	2
201503	2756	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	But let me discuss how I think about some of the nuances around this conditionality.	23	2
201503	2757	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	Madam Chair, you made a number of excellent points yesterday and again this morning with respect to the inflation outlook at liftoff.	23	2
201503	2758	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	In particular, you indicated it could be appropriate to lift off while inflation was still quite low, as long as theory and historical experience gave us confidence that a near-term acceleration must be around the corner.	23	2
201503	2759	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	I will likely find such an assessment challenging to support, but it’s not impossible.	23	2
201503	2760	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	I’m not reasonably confident today.	23	2
201503	2761	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	What continues to worry me is that the Committee may not be seriously embracing the symmetry in our inflation objective.	23	2
201503	2762	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	I made a special point of saying this at our January reaffirmation of our long-run strategy.	23	2
201503	2763	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	In weighing the costs and benefits of further policy delay at each meeting, I think it is important that the Committee be willing to risk overshooting our 2 percent inflation objective.	23	2
201503	2764	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	The increased risk of retreating back to the zero lower bound following a premature exit represents a significant cost to an early liftoff.	23	2
201503	2765	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	Unless we accept a substantial chance of inflation overshooting our 2 percent target, we won’t be properly balancing the costs and benefits at liftoff in line with our long-run strategy.	23	2
201503	2766	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	If, while inflation is still too low, we lift off early just to ensure that we don’t cross our 2 percent inflation objective, that’s an enormous problem for me.	23	2
201503	2767	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	I personally think it would be overly conservative, in the Rogoff “conservative central banker” mode, to try to thread the needle to get to 2 percent while only staying all the while below 2 percent.	23	2
201503	2768	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	I can’t see how this would be consistent with a symmetric 2 percent inflation objective.	23	2
201503	2769	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	In such a situation, if theory and experience are going to be our guide while inflation is still too low, I strongly believe we shouldn’t lift off until theory and experience tell us that we risk having inflation accelerate to, say, 2½ percent or higher.	23	2
201503	2770	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	Nothing in the Tealbook or our other forecasts suggests to me that this is close at hand.	23	2
201503	2771	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	For me, that would be a stronger and more useful statement about our confidence in theory and experience as being our guides.	23	2
201503	2772	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	My view of appropriate monetary policy continues to be that liftoff should be delayed until the first quarter of 2016.	23	2
201503	2773	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	This assessment recognizes the strength of the labor market and economic growth outlook, but it also recognizes that the inflation outlook is too low and highly uncertain.	23	2
201503	2774	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	Moreover, I fear that an early liftoff could jeopardize the public’s assessment of our credibility regarding our 2 percent symmetric inflation objective.	23	2
201503	2775	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	We’ve spent six years below 2 percent, and we are projecting another two to four years to get back to 2 percent.	23	2
201503	2776	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	We are not the ECB or the Bundesbank.	23	2
201503	2777	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	We should not be trying our darndest to prevent any crossing of a 2 percent bright line.	23	2
201503	2778	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	The stakes for our 2 percent inflation credibility are very large.	23	2
201503	2779	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	If we don’t get back to 2 percent before this cycle ends, no one will ever think we are serious about our 2 percent goal, except that it’s a ceiling.	23	2
201503	2780	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	That would be very costly for our future success.	23	2
201503	2781	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	On Friday, my colleagues Jonas Fisher, François Gourio, Spencer Krane, and I will be giving a Brookings paper that discusses the important asymmetry created by the zero lower bound when there’s uncertainty about the level of the Wicksellian natural rate of interest.	23	2
201503	2782	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	Thomas’s figure on the range of participants’ r* assessment is one measure of this range of uncertainty.	23	2
201503	2783	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	That’s my interpretation of it at least.	23	2
201503	2784	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	I don’t want to downplay the excellent theoretical work of my colleagues—Jonas, François, and Spence—in our upcoming Brookings paper, but it is not that hard to show that optimal monetary policy under discretion in the workhorse New Keynesian models or older-style Keynesian models implies a strong motive to delay policy liftoff whenever risk and uncertainty increase and a binding and costly zero lower bound looms large.	23	2
201503	2785	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	In this situation, there is a motive to build up a buffer stock of economic and inflation improvements in order to reduce the chance that negative shocks send policy back to the zero lower bound.	23	2
201503	2786	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	Having said all of this, I can agree to remove the “patient” language today and move to a meeting-by-meeting assessment.	23	2
201503	2787	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	But we should avoid becoming unnecessarily impatient and recognize the major asymmetry and the losses we risk as a result of moving too early in June versus later, as in September or even December.	23	2
201503	2788	2015-03-18	meeting	EVANS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201503	2789	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	23	2
201503	2790	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	President Mester.	23	2

201503	2794	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	As Chair Yellen pointed out, we’re going to have three employment reports before our June meeting, and, in light of the strength we’ve been seeing, it would be inappropriate at this point to shut down the possibility of a June liftoff.	23	2
201503	2795	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	The “patient” language has served the Committee well as a transition.	23	2

201503	2806	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	It would seem that the next communications challenge we face is how to convey the idea that we are data dependent, meaning that the first rate increase doesn’t necessarily imply that we’re on a path of rate increases at each meeting, nor does a pause necessarily signify that liftoff was the wrong thing to do.	23	2
201503	2807	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	The Chair has mentioned this in her public statements, and I think it’s worth emphasizing it as liftoff gets closer.	23	2
201503	2808	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	Managing expectations about the post-liftoff policy rate path would seem to be a key factor in ensuring that liftoff itself is not disruptive.	23	2
201503	2809	2015-03-18	meeting	MESTER	We’re also going to need to wean market participants away from detailed forward guidance and move toward language that explains our policy rationale, but not necessarily the timing of every expected action we plan to take.	23	2

201503	2815	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	Regarding the statement, I interpret the forward-guidance language with the removal of “patient” as conveying that liftoff is approaching.	23	2
201503	2816	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	April is highly unlikely, but the exact timing after April has not been determined.	23	2
201503	2817	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	I think this is the appropriate message coming out of this meeting.	23	2
201503	2818	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	This statement, if adopted, puts the Committee in a new decisionmaking and messaging phase.	23	2
201503	2819	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	I’d urge the Committee to confer early about how we’re going to manage through this phase.	23	2
201503	2820	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	In my opinion, it’s always advisable to think through our communications strategy one or two meetings ahead, under a couple of plausible scenarios.	23	2
201503	2821	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	That is especially the case because of the situation the Committee could face in the next few meetings.	23	2
201503	2822	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	I’m concerned about how to reconcile the tensions between or among preserving decision optionality right up to a possible liftoff meeting; preparing markets by signaling in advance; and remaining disciplined regarding data dependency, having laid down a decision criterion of being reasonably confident.	23	2
201503	2823	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	Are we going to help prepare markets by signaling high probability of a liftoff decision at least one meeting in advance?	23	2
201503	2824	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	Or are we going to make the decision at a meeting based on the latest data and present that to the markets and public with little or no signaling?	23	2
201503	2825	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	My preferred approach is to give advance signals at a frequency of one meeting.	23	2
201503	2826	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	If the Committee is inclined to follow the one-meeting-in-advance approach and it’s 50–50 at the April meeting—and I think this is a plausible scenario—we would face a challenging communication situation.	23	2
201503	2827	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	It seems to me that we would have to either lay out the reasoning behind a portrayal of June as still in play—and this was President Kocherlakota’s point in his quite useful memo last week—or provide some information in April about what we would need to see that would tip the scales to liftoff in June.	23	2
201503	2828	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	Assuming continuing strong labor market reports, the scales tipper would likely be price indications that make the Committee reasonably confident that the inflation outlook is satisfactory.	23	2
201503	2829	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	I think it is highly unlikely that by April we will have price data in hand to support a verdict of reasonably confident.	23	2
201503	2830	2015-03-18	meeting	LOCKHART	So, as I said, I think keeping June in play at the April meeting presents a communications challenge.	23	2

201503	2861	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	Making policy based on natural rate, potential growth, and equilibrium rate assumptions that are too high could deprive workers who are out of the labor force or part time for economic reasons of being fully and gainfully employed.	23	2
201503	2862	2015-03-18	meeting	ROSENGREN	Finally, after missing our PCE inflation target on the low side for many years, we need to be sure to engineer liftoff only once we have truly attained reasonable confidence that we will hit the target within the forecast horizon.	23	2

201503	2887	2015-03-18	meeting	BULLARD	We can look at other measures of labor market performance, such as the labor market conditions index, but the correlation between those indexes and unemployment is around 0.95.	23	2
201503	2888	2015-03-18	meeting	BULLARD	The same is true for nonfarm payroll employment growth.	23	2
201503	2889	2015-03-18	meeting	BULLARD	I think our workhorse indicators of unemployment and nonfarm payrolls are telling us what we need to know about labor market improvement.	23	2
201503	2890	2015-03-18	meeting	BULLARD	The goal for 2015 should be to make modest moves in the policy settings to position US monetary policy more appropriately for the state of the economy in 2016 and beyond.	23	2
201503	2891	2015-03-18	meeting	BULLARD	Even when we come off the zero lower bound, policy will remain extremely accommodative.	23	2
201503	2892	2015-03-18	meeting	BULLARD	In particular, there will still be upward pressure on inflation coming from monetary policy.	23	2
201503	2893	2015-03-18	meeting	BULLARD	In fact, according to traditional analysis, there will be upward pressure on inflation coming from monetary policy at all times in the next several years as the normalization process proceeds.	23	2
201503	2894	2015-03-18	meeting	BULLARD	That will help move inflation back toward the Committee’s 2 percent target.	23	2
201503	2895	2015-03-18	meeting	BULLARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201503	2896	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	23	2

201503	2898	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2

201503	2900	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	And I fully support your description of the economic outlook that you gave yesterday and your plans in terms of the press conference and thinking about policy.	23	2
201503	2901	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	The first paragraph of alternative B properly characterizes the various crosscurrents in the data—some softening in spending numbers and positive surprises in the labor market—and my own expectation remains that the unemployment rate will fall below its natural rate around the middle of this year.	23	2
201503	2902	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	I also continue to view the dip in core inflation as transitory, especially in view of tentative signs that reduced slack is starting to boost wage growth.	23	2
201503	2903	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	I therefore continue to view the risks to the outlook as balanced and little changed from our previous meeting.	23	2
201503	2904	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	This outlook and risk assessment point toward making policy decisions on a meeting-by-meeting basis going forward, based on the data as they come in.	23	2
201503	2905	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Importantly, alternative B appropriately notes that the change in forward guidance does not have explicit implications for the timing of future policy changes.	23	2
201503	2906	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	I do want to comment on President Lacker’s remark that there is some conflict in the language.	23	2
201503	2907	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	I think there’s absolutely no conflict in the language at all.	23	2
201503	2908	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	It does not imply at all that we don’t have confidence that inflation will return.	23	2
201503	2909	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	It just says that, at the time of liftoff, what we’re looking for is improvement in the labor market, and that we will have confidence.	23	2
201503	2910	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	It doesn’t suggest that that’s a change or anything.	23	2
201503	2911	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	It just says that those are the two conditions that we need to have in order to have liftoff.	23	2
201503	2912	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	So I don’t see a conflict or tension in the language.	23	2
201503	2913	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	It appropriately captures our dual-mandate goals and the progress we’re making on those.	23	2
201503	2914	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	Looking ahead, I agree with President Lockhart that we really should be thinking ahead to the future statement language.	23	2
201503	2915	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	I’ve thought some about that and have some comments.	23	2
201503	2916	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	My own view is, we don’t want to be writing the statement in the meeting before, stating what we’re going to do in the next meeting.	23	2
201503	2917	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	I don’t think that’s the right approach.	23	2
201503	2918	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	What we want is to have a statement that, through words, gives a probabilistic interpretation of how we see policy going forward.	23	2
201503	2919	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	I agree that these decisions should be meeting by meeting, based on the data that we have at the time.	23	2
201503	2920	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	In thinking about the future statements, I prefer a communications strategy that avoids specific commitments to future monetary policy actions.	23	2
201503	2921	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	So I looked ahead to alternative C for possible thinking—again, for the future—about an approach.	23	2
201503	2922	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	In one sense, a hint that perhaps we’re getting closer to a rate increase would be provided by the language that says “In determining future adjustments of the target range for the federal funds rate,” as opposed to “In determining how long to maintain” the funds rate.	23	2
201503	2923	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	That’s a way to lean a little bit toward the idea that an increase may be coming sooner.	23	2
201503	2924	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	That said, paragraph 3 in alt-B, the one that I think we’ll be using today, is a really good and flexible structure for our future statements.	23	2
201503	2925	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	We’ll have to clear some scaffolding that we built around the sentences referring to the April meeting and the fact that we’re changing the forward guidance.	23	2

201503	2927	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	But once we clear that scaffolding around it, the language in alt-B, paragraph 3, gives that data dependence pretty clearly.	23	2
201503	2928	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	It implies that we will be making decisions based on the incoming data and our objectives.	23	2
201503	2929	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	In that regard, I really do think that’s preferable to returning to a date-based guidance such as “in a couple of meetings.”	23	2
201503	2930	2015-03-18	meeting	WILLIAMS	I believe that we want to avoid going back to date-based guidance in future statements, and that we really want this to be open-ended in the future.	23	2
