201503	2939	2015-03-18	meeting	GEORGE	Beyond the language in this statement, though, I believe it’s becoming increasingly important to say something about the path of interest rates after liftoff, as others have noted.	23	2
201503	2940	2015-03-18	meeting	GEORGE	The public’s fixation on the timing of liftoff often is accompanied by concern about a steady move to the neutral rate.	23	2
201503	2941	2015-03-18	meeting	GEORGE	Given uncertainty about how the economy might respond to the initial removal of accommodation, a more gradual path may be prudent as we evaluate the effect of liftoff after a prolonged period of near-zero rates.	23	2
201503	2942	2015-03-18	meeting	GEORGE	Communicating the possibility of a more gradual path also could help dispel expectations that policy is poised to move on a preset course.	23	2
201503	2943	2015-03-18	meeting	GEORGE	So it may be appropriate to pause after liftoff, not only to see how the economy and financial markets respond, but also to reinforce that we are not marching steadily to the neutral rate at increments of 25 basis points at each meeting.	23	2

201503	2947	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201503	2948	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	First, I’d like to thank the Board’s staff for the effort that was taken in the Tealbook, Book B, to explore the policy implications of a nonlinear link between the unemployment rate and the rate of wage inflation.	23	2
201503	2949	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	As you may know, the Dallas research staff has found evidence of such a link in both aggregate and regional data.	23	2
201503	2950	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	As I understand it, the question today boils down to whether to take June off the table for liftoff from the zero bound, put it on the table, or go one step further and signal the intention to raise rates in June.	23	2
201503	2951	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	I think that liftoff in June is quite likely to be appropriate, but I see no reason to tie our hands, so I favor alternative B.	23	2
201503	2952	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	I see a June liftoff as likely to be appropriate not because of an immediate inflation threat or because we see our 2 percent inflation target as a ceiling.	23	2
201503	2953	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	In looking to prolong this expansion, we think that the best approach is to ease off on policy accommodation relatively soon so that we don’t need to take stronger and more risky action later.	23	2
201503	2954	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	As President Fisher emphasized, the track record in withdrawing accommodation after we’ve already pushed past full employment is not good.	23	2
201503	2955	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	Perhaps one reason that “later and steep” may not work in practice is that the promise of “steep” isn’t seen as credible.	23	2
201503	2956	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	Because it isn’t regarded as credible, people make financial bets that pay off only if low rates continue.	23	2
201503	2957	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	Whether that is the explanation or not, we note that, in each of the three longest economic expansions in post–World War II economic history, the Federal Reserve began raising short-term interest rates while unemployment was at or above the natural rate and above the jobless rate we see today.	23	2
201503	2958	2015-03-18	meeting	HOLCOMB	Thank you.	23	2

201503	2961	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201503	2962	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	I support alternative B.	23	2
201503	2963	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	At the previous meeting, I was uncertain that I’d be able to support the removal of the “patient” language at this meeting.	23	2
201503	2964	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	At the same time, at this meeting, I’ve actually moved back my projected liftoff date until December.	23	2
201503	2965	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	How do I reconcile those two positions—that I’m actually now quite strongly supportive of removing “patient”?	23	2
201503	2966	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Well, there are basically three reasons.	23	2
201503	2967	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	First, there’s the background reason, which almost all of us agree with, that it is actually good to get this phrase out of the regular FOMC statement because, number one, it was intended to be a transitional phrase and, number two, it’s another one of those phrases to which I think markets are attaching potentially excessive weight.	23	2
201503	2968	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	So by removing it, we get rid of a lot of the speculation about it.	23	2
201503	2969	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	The second reason is that I think the Chair has been very effective in her monetary policy testimony in shifting perceptions of what I have previously referred to as the “kitchen timer” phenomenon, which is to say that once “patient” is removed, the kitchen timer is flipped and we’re on course to a two-meetings-later federal funds rate liftoff.	23	2
201503	2970	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	The additional language in the statement reinforces that.	23	2
201503	2971	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Third, and somewhat contrary to some of you who are looking forward to a potential June liftoff, I actually believe the recent softening of economic news makes it less likely the markets will think that there’s a kitchen timer phenomenon here—or, in Helen’s terms, that the countdown has begun.	23	2
201503	2972	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	There’s some risk that it’ll still be read that way, but that’s a risk worth taking in order to achieve the benefit that I noted earlier.	23	2
201503	2973	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	I don’t see the case, as I said a moment ago, for liftoff any time soon, but it’s healthy for us to be thinking actively about our monetary policy stance at each meeting.	23	2
201503	2974	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Now, on the substance, we may be moving into a normalized procedural and institutional environment, but the conditions out there remain very unusual, with the aftermath of the financial crisis and the Great Recession and a variety of ongoing secular changes.	23	2
201503	2975	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	So in thinking about the theory and history that are relevant, I’m not entirely sure what history is most instructive, given the number of things that have changed from more recent episodes of recessions and recoveries.	23	2
201503	2976	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	I do understand the abstract point that a return to full employment and continued recovery will, at some juncture, push inflation up, but I haven’t yet heard the reasons why, at some particular point, we’ll know that we have crossed that threshold and we should have reasonable confidence that that’s the path that we’re on.	23	2
201503	2977	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	It will presumably be based on something specific that isn’t present right now.	23	2
201503	2978	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	We’re all emphasizing our data dependence, and so I look forward in future meetings to hearing what specifics people have that make us think we should conclude that now we have that reasonable confidence.	23	2
201503	2979	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	I presume that those of you who have been ready to move for some time don’t need any more data, but, for those of us who have not, I think it is important to have that conversation and, specifically, to say, again, what has changed so that now we can have that kind of confidence that we didn’t beforehand.	23	2
201503	2980	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	I will say that there are a couple of other background reasons why my instincts are for later rather than sooner.	23	2
201503	2981	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	One is just a conversation to which I shouldn’t attach enormous significance, I guess, but it did have an effect on me.	23	2
201503	2982	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Some weeks ago, I asked an economist who watches financial markets pretty closely what his explanation for the low level of inflation compensation was.	23	2
201503	2983	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	He proceeded to give me several interesting technical explanations, and then he said, “I don’t actually think that your inflation target is 2 percent.	23	2
201503	2984	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	I think it’s closer to 1.7 percent.	23	2
201503	2985	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	So the amount of inflation compensation required is actually less than you seem to have been assuming.”	23	2
201503	2986	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Now, that’s one guy’s view.	23	2
201503	2987	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	But he’s a straightforward, smart person who was just purporting to interpret what he was seeing in markets, and that did concern me.	23	2
201503	2988	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	I’m also concerned with the issue that many in and out of this Committee have raised:  While we’ve got a lot of ways to tighten, we don’t really have that many ways to be accommodative, and so moving prematurely could risk putting ourselves into a circumstance in which we had a limited number of efficacious responses.	23	2
201503	2989	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	The final point I’d make, though, on the substance is that, although I pushed back liftoff, as I said, to December, in 2016 and 2017 I move back closer to the pack—that is, my rate of increase of the federal funds rate will be somewhat faster than the norm.	23	2
201503	2990	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	It doesn’t quite get me to the middle of the pack, but it gets me back into the pack.	23	2
201503	2991	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	That reflects a view that we really should be sure and have a high degree of confidence.	23	2
201503	2992	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Maybe my implicit reaction function is a high rather than reasonable degree of confidence, but, once we get there, I think that it will probably be more appropriate to normalize more quickly.	23	2
201503	2993	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	In conclusion, I’d just say that I hope I am surprised in the coming months by the intensification of economic growth and maybe some wage growth and the diminution of downside risks.	23	2
201503	2994	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Short of that, I look forward to discussions in April and thereafter of the specifics that will help me, at least, come to the conclusion that the relevant corner has been turned, and that the level of confidence that we’re moving back toward a 2 percent inflation target, while giving more opportunity for employment to grow, has been reached.	23	2
201503	2995	2015-03-18	meeting	TARULLO	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2

201503	2997	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Fischer.	23	2
201503	2998	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201503	2999	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	As I said yesterday, I believe we’re closing in on full employment, and I’m reasonably confident that inflation will move back to its 2 percent objective over the medium term, not least because I’m confident that this Committee will keep monetary policy sufficiently expansionary until we get there.	23	2
201503	3000	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	So I support alternative B—that it’s time to take “patient” out of the statement and to signal that it is not unlikely that we’ll want to raise rates in June.	23	2
201503	3001	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	At the same time, I support the language that says we’ve not determined when we will lift off, as it’s easy to envisage circumstances that will make us prefer to wait until after June, because either the incoming data we’ve seen recently or unanticipated developments lead us to reconsider and wait to see how events unfold.	23	2
201503	3002	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	So I think that those who are supporting alternative B, which seems to be generally accepted, are correct, and that that’s the right way to proceed.	23	2
201503	3003	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	But I’d like to discuss a few issues that are worth mentioning because they’re likely to be relevant to the debate we’re going to have about timing over the next several months.	23	2
201503	3004	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	First, there is the issue of the length of the lags with which monetary policy actions affect the real economy.	23	2
201503	3005	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	Estimates of dynamic monetary policy multipliers imply that the decisions we make this year may not have their greatest effect until 2017.	23	2
201503	3006	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	While we cannot now place much faith in the 2017 forecasts for the state of the economy, it’s more likely than not that a smaller punch bowl will be wholly appropriate for the tight labor market and rising inflation that we may well face a year or two from now.	23	2
201503	3007	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	Second, we need a sense of proportion.	23	2
201503	3008	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	Raising the federal funds rate ¼ percent is not akin to shifting monetary policy from accommodative to contractionary.	23	2
201503	3009	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	Rather, we’ll be moving from an ultraexpansionary monetary policy to an extremely expansionary monetary policy.	23	2
201503	3010	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	We’ll still have rates that are low enough to continue to support the recovery while beginning to normalize monetary policy, itself a relevant positive factor in making our decision.	23	2
201503	3011	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	Moreover, if the economy turns out to have less momentum than we are—or at least I am— currently estimating or if we’re hit with more negative shocks, we can lower the rate again.	23	2
201503	3012	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	Indeed, we should all be looking forward to a time when rates might more regularly be expected to move in either direction.	23	2
201503	3013	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	Third, if I can just insert a brief comment relating to the discussion on forward guidance—namely, the interchange between Presidents Lockhart and Williams on forward guidance—I, too, believe we need to avoid date-based guidance.	23	2
201503	3014	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	But, even more, I think we should avoid constraining ourselves going forward.	23	2
201503	3015	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	We should do what we can to reveal to the markets the way we’re thinking, but without committing ourselves to tying our hands going ahead.	23	2
201503	3016	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	We could give forecasts.	23	2
201503	3017	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	That’s what’s being done in many other countries.	23	2
201503	3018	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	I don’t think it was particularly helpful to have those forecasts, but what they do do is to make it clear as you look at them ex post that our knowledge about what we’re going to do is quite limited.	23	2
201503	3019	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	But we can find other ways of revealing that than publishing the forecasts.	23	2
201503	3020	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	Fourth, the choice of interest rate path is sometimes described as a choice between an early and gradual path and a later and steeper path.	23	2
201503	3021	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	The main argument given for starting later has been that, all else being equal, the existence of the lower bound should make us wait at least a bit longer to raise rates than we would have otherwise.	23	2
201503	3022	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	But that argument is always true, and, at every moment, you can say that.	23	2
201503	3023	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	That choice means, on average, staying at the lower bound longer, which, to my mind, also has costs.	23	2
201503	3024	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	What we have to do is to calibrate when the costs have exceeded the benefits.	23	2
201503	3025	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	That’s very difficult, but I think we’re very close to that point or will be within, say, a couple of months or perhaps a bit more.	23	2
201503	3026	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	In addition, I do not believe, although I’ve heard it said repeatedly, that having to reverse course is the end of the world.	23	2
201503	3027	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	Let me explain a factor that I think we overlook.	23	2
201503	3028	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	If the situation becomes dire enough, we could once again use QE.	23	2
201503	3029	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	But if the situation is sufficiently dire to move us from plus 25 basis points back to zero, it would have been very dire if we had stayed at zero, and we’re going to have to respond in that case as well.	23	2
201503	3030	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	So it’s not that we get away from having to confront situations in which it will be very uncomfortable with being at the zero lower bound.	23	2
201503	3031	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	Finally, I’d like to add a detail about when to lift off.	23	2
201503	3032	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	We’re all familiar with the argument that we should lift off late because of the possibility that, by lifting off earlier, we’d face a higher probability of having to reverse course and return to the effective lower bound.	23	2
201503	3033	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	The question is not whether we might have to reverse course.	23	2
201503	3034	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	It is whether and when the expected gain from lifting off becomes positive.	23	2
201503	3035	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	That means we have to weigh the costs of having to reverse course by the probability of having to do so.	23	2
201503	3036	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	I received but haven’t, unfortunately, had time to read the paper by President Evans and his colleagues, but I did look at it.	23	2
201503	3037	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	I’ll instead talk about results that are in the memo submitted in January by de Groot, Gagnon, and Tetlow, whose title is “Stochastic Implications of Alternative Strategies for the Beginning of Policy Normalization.”	23	2
201503	3038	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	The memo has in it the following, among several other, conclusions: “The probability, under the [earlier and gradual] strategy, of returning to the [effective lower bound] within eight quarters is moderate, at 10 percent, and falls to only about 5 percent under the [later and steep] strategy; however, the chance of the prescribed federal funds rate climbing to at least 3 percent within a year of initial departure is negligible under the [earlier and gradual] strategy, and about 10 percent under the [later and steep] strategy.”	23	2
201503	3039	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	We’ve really got to look at the alternative paths and not at staying here or not.	23	2
201503	3040	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	There are consequences to delaying, and we need to take them into account as well.	23	2
201503	3041	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	I see considerable benefits to the gradual strategies because I think that will enable us to deal with later disturbances in a more moderate way if we have negative disturbances.	23	2
201503	3042	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	The issue of timing—of when the expected return from raising the interest rate is greater than the costs of not doing so—is a critical element in the calculation of when to lift off.	23	2
201503	3043	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	It’s a critical element, but it doesn’t tell us when to lift off.	23	2
201503	3044	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	The argument for not lifting off at any particular point remains the same.	23	2
201503	3045	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	It almost goes without saying that that calculation and that decision will be at the center of our discussions over the coming FOMC meetings.	23	2
201503	3046	2015-03-18	meeting	FISCHER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201503	3047	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	23	2
201503	3048	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Powell.	23	2
201503	3049	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201503	3050	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	I will support alternative B.	23	2
201503	3051	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	The revised statement puts the Committee in a position to react to incoming data and events without any specific time commitment about the liftoff or path of rates.	23	2
201503	3052	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	Independent of one’s view of the appropriate date of liftoff, that is an important step on the path to normalization and one that I welcome.	23	2
201503	3053	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	In this SEP, I moved my estimate of the most likely liftoff date from June to September in light of the run of weaker data, the strength of the dollar, and the likely continued weakness in inflation readings.	23	2
201503	3054	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	But, as several have noted, there will be three employment reports between now and the June meeting and a smaller number of inflation readings.	23	2
201503	3055	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	If we continue to get very strong payroll numbers, declining unemployment, and at least modest inflation readings, I could be prepared to support liftoff in June, but I think it’s more likely that the date will slip to September.	23	2
201503	3056	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	I’ll say again that, to me, in the long run not much rides on whether the first rate increase happens in June or September.	23	2
201503	3057	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	Far more important is that the Committee have a plan to deal with the range of possible data and events as well as a consistent and clear way of communicating that plan to the public.	23	2
201503	3058	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	And the center of that plan as we go forward will be the test of continued improvement in the labor market and reasonable confidence that inflation will move back to the 2 percent medium-term objective.	23	2
201503	3059	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	If the Committee does choose to lift off this year, which today seems to me both desirable and highly likely, there will be a need to explain how that decision is consistent with our 2 percent medium-term inflation objective.	23	2
201503	3060	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	And that will not be easy—particularly if the dollar continues to strengthen and oil prices remain weak or even decline.	23	2
201503	3061	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	I see this explanation as based on the thoughts that diminishing slack will eventually produce inflation, and that monetary policy works with long lags.	23	2
201503	3062	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	The Chair persuasively outlined these points last evening and then again this morning.	23	2
201503	3063	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	I think that case needs to be made consistently—and no doubt repeatedly—if we’re to be seen as defending the 2 percent objective.	23	2
201503	3064	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	There will also be a need to foreshadow liftoff at least one meeting ahead, perhaps by signaling that the Committee is gaining confidence that inflation will move back to the 2 percent objective over the medium term.	23	2
201503	3065	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	It’s become a near cliché to say that the path of rates is more important than the date of liftoff, a statement that is obviously true in the long run but not that helpful in the short term when what we’re trying to do is to choose the date of liftoff.	23	2
201503	3066	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	But it is appropriate that the Committee now turn to thinking about, and communicating more about, the path of rates after liftoff.	23	2
201503	3067	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	And I do think that, after liftoff, we can move rates up fairly gradually, particularly if inflation continues to be weak, as seems likely.	23	2
201503	3068	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	We don’t need to be in a hurry.	23	2
201503	3069	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	In my view, policy should remain highly accommodative for quite a while longer, and that is consistent with a gradual path of rate increases after liftoff.	23	2
201503	3070	2015-03-18	meeting	POWELL	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201503	3071	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	23	2
201503	3072	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Brainard.	23	2
201503	3073	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201503	3074	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	I support alternative B.	23	2
201503	3075	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	It represents a carefully balanced approach that’s an appropriate response to the divergence we are seeing in the two legs of our dual mandate.	23	2
201503	3076	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	While it seems likely that we will see further movement in the direction of maximum employment over the next two meetings, it also seems highly likely we could see lingering softness in inflation and no observed progress toward our inflation target.	23	2
201503	3077	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	This is especially likely if the dollar continues to strengthen and core import prices soften further.	23	2
201503	3078	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	The recent momentum in the labor market suggests that resource utilization has continued to increase and may continue to do so going forward.	23	2
201503	3079	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Just how much slack remains in the economy is difficult to say, but there appears to be some slack along several margins, including unemployment, participation, and people who are working part time for economic reasons.	23	2
201503	3080	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	The outlook for inflation is more uncertain.	23	2
201503	3081	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	We should expect over time that temporary factors holding down inflation, such as energy price declines and dollar appreciation, will fade, and that continued increases in resource utilization will begin to put upward pressure on wage and price inflation.	23	2
201503	3082	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	But the fading of the so-called temporary factors may, in fact, take more time than we currently expect.	23	2
201503	3083	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	In particular, the effects of the dollar may fade only slowly, and dollar appreciation may well have some distance to go, exerting a significant tightening effect.	23	2
201503	3084	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	At the same time, we’ve seen little convincing evidence that tighter resource utilization is yet having a significant effect on prices and wages.	23	2
201503	3085	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	And we can’t dismiss the possibility that the lingering effects of the financial crisis may have some persistent effects on the relationship between resource utilization and inflation domestically.	23	2
201503	3086	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	While the partial retracement of market- based inflation compensation measures gives some support to our hope that inflation expectations will hold steady, it’s possible that they are softening in the face of stubbornly low inflation, which would be highly troubling.	23	2
201503	3087	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Thus, I think the risks around the outlook for inflation are slightly tilted to the downside.	23	2
201503	3088	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	I view it as highly significant that the removal of the word “patient” is accompanied by economic projections from the Committee that point to a later and more gradual path of policy firming.	23	2
201503	3089	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	I hope this combination accurately conveys to the public the high degree of nuance in the discussion that we’ve had in this room.	23	2
201503	3090	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Let me be clear about how I interpret the removal of the word “patient.”	23	2
201503	3091	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	I view this statement as announcing the end of forward guidance—which is to say, the commitment to a stated policy rate path for some time into the future—and the return to data-dependent, meeting-by-meeting policy determination starting in June.	23	2
201503	3092	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	It’s important that the public understand the end of forward guidance does not prejudge the outcome of any subsequent meeting.	23	2
201503	3093	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Rather, it creates optionality that the target rate could be moved without a commitment far in advance.	23	2
201503	3094	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	It’s also very important that the public understand there is nothing inevitable about either the pace or even the direction of policy moves following liftoff.	23	2
201503	3095	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	In fact, the economic and price developments since we last met in January cause me to be more hesitant that we will see the appropriate conditions for liftoff in June.	23	2
201503	3096	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Nonetheless, I support the removal of the “patient” language to communicate clearly that we will be very closely attuned to the incoming data and will have the option of altering the policy rate path to respond to those data starting in June.	23	2
201503	3097	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	The policy reaction function in alternative B places great weight on our being reasonably confident that economic conditions and a monetary policy based on contemporaneous liftoff would be consistent with inflation moving back toward our 2 percent goal over the medium term.	23	2
201503	3098	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Assuming that core inflation remains soft relative to our target, the set of factors that might give me reasonable confidence that inflation is likely to move back toward our target are that employment growth continues at or near current rates; resource utilization gaps continue to close at about the same pace as over the previous year; measures of inflation expectations continue to firm; and we observe an inflection point in the forces that we now believe to be transitory that are weighing on core inflation—in particular, oil prices and core import prices associated with dollar strengthening.	23	2
201503	3099	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Although the confluence of these events is possible by June, I find it more likely that many of these conditions will not be met in June.	23	2
201503	3100	2015-03-18	meeting	BRAINARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201503	3101	2015-03-18	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	23	2

201503	3105	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I’ve had a headache about the Taylor rule for a long time, as you all know—in large part because of the slavish adherence to a constant real equilibrium rate of 2 percent, which I think has been contradicted by the actual performance of the economy over the past few years.	23	2
201503	3106	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	So thank you.	23	2
201503	3107	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Your analysis is a welcome dose of aspirin.	23	2

201503	3109	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I support alternative B.	23	2
201503	3110	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Taking out the “patient” language makes sense, given that there are some scenarios, especially those in which the labor market tightens further and wage inflation climbs, in which we’d want to lift off in June.	23	2
201503	3111	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	At the same time, the statement language, the Chair’s earlier testimony, and, I expect, the statement at the press conference today should make it clear that removal of the “patient” language in no way indicates any commitment to moving in June.	23	2

201503	3113	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	I also like the fact that we’ll no longer be boxed in meeting to meeting by our forward guidance.	23	2
201503	3114	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	We’ve said that we’re data dependent.	23	2
201503	3115	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	Now, I think, the statement is finally consistent with that.	23	2
201503	3116	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	In terms of market reaction, I would expect a slightly adverse reaction from this change even though it’s widely anticipated, because the deed is often worse than the expectation.	23	2
201503	3117	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	That said, though, I think any effect should be modest, because the shift downward in the SEP’s federal funds rate trajectory for 2015 will likely be interpreted by market participants as suggesting that the Committee is shifting more toward September, away from June.	23	2
201503	3118	2015-03-18	meeting	DUDLEY	As far as the statement language is concerned, I believe I’m like everyone else except President Lacker—I’m perfectly happy with the statement as it reads right now.	23	2
